The Ozloc & Dragon serves wealthy patrons and operates a subtle but strict dress code to keep out the riff raff. Customers must look the part and characters turning up in armour or their normal travel clothes—even if they are here to meet a wealthy patron—will be politely turned away.

# WHAT' S GOING ON?

While the characters are at the Ozloc & Dragon, one or more things from the list below may occur:

- 1. **Quiet**: The Ozloc & Dragon is quiet; if the characters are dressed appropriately, they easily secure a table.
- 2. **Rister on the Floor**: Rister is making an effort to meet, greet and get to know his customers. He is incredibly friendly and welcoming to everyone (or at least everyone with ready coin to spend).
- 3. **Busy**: The Ozloc & Dragon is busy, and Rister is literally vibrating with excitement as he hopes the tavern's popularity is growing. Sadly, unless the characters are wealthy or important, there is no empty table available.
- 4. **Annoying Drunk**: A drunk commoner stands outside the inn shouting incoherent insults at the customers within. The man once drank here when it was the Green Griffon and hates what Rister has done to "his" tavern.
- 5. **Closed**: The Ozloc & Dragon is closed for a private function; sounds of merriment emanate from within.
- 6. **Ozloc's Adventures**: Rister is a huge fan of Sir Ozloc the Brave and is enthusiastically (and loudly) recounting stories of the half-elf's adventures to a customer.

# OPPORTUNITIES & COMPLICATIONS

Lucky adventurers find opportunities almost anywhere; unlucky adventurers find complications almost anywhere.

- 1. **Complaining Merchant**: The merchant Antero Kalervo "Folk Out & About #1" sits with a friend and a character overhears him moaning that he has a problem in his cellar, which requires adroit handling by "specialists".
- 2. **Rister Greets the Party**: Rister introduces himself to the characters and tries to get to know them. He senses they are adventurers and knows several patrons in need of such folks' services. Depending on how their conversation progresses, he may or may not pass on their names. In this way, he hopes his wealthy customers will see him as the kind of person who "knows people".
- 3. **Vandalised Sign**: The tavern's ornate wooden sign has been vandalised—someone has thrown paint all over it. A character cleaning it (perhaps with magic) gets a free bottle of wine and Rister's thanks.
- 4. **Stolen Sign**: The characters hear Rister bemoaning that someone has stolen the tavern's ornate wooden sign. He would be grateful to anyone retrieving it. (Luckily, he has a spare, as this is not an isolated incident.)
- 5. **Annoying Drunk**: As #4 "What's Going On" but the drunk staggers into the inn and creates a terrible scene. If the characters help to discreetly resolve the problem, they gain Rister's thanks (and a free bottle of wine).
- 6. **Giants Rats**: Rat tunnels intersect the inn's cellar, and several giant (perhaps diseased) rats burst into the common room. Rister is horrified, and chaos reigns.

# WHISPERS & RUMOURS

The characters may overhear or learn some of the rumours (which may or may not be true) below:

- 1. **Tax the Rich**: Things are good in Dulwich, and its folk grow wealthy—particularly the merchants. Wido Gall is planning a new tax on the merchants, and they are not happy about it.
- 2. **Foundation Way's Deep Cellars**: Foundation Way is aptly named. An older settlement once stood there, and the street's shops and homes were built over the top of it. Many of the buildings feature deep, multi-level cellars. Some folk speak of even older, deeper tunnels.
- 3. **'Ware the Dragon**: A dragon's lair—complete with a red dragon—has been discovered buried in the hills to the west of Dunstone. Apparently, the beast lairs in caverns below a ruined monastery. Most of the adventurers who made the discovery are dead; only one survivor—the heroic, and fleet of foot, half-elf, Sir Ozloc the Brave of Mossvale—escaped the beast. Some folk name the half-elf a hero for bringing news of the danger back to the town, while others mutter he abandoned his friends to save his own skin.
- 4. **The Ozloc & Dragon is the Place**: The Ozloc & Dragon is Dulwich's newest exclusive tavern catering to only the town's wealthiest and most influential folk. Here, Dulwich's riff-raff are not welcome, the prices are high, and the owner enforces a strict dress code. If you want to meet the town's movers and shakers, this is the place.
- 5. **Angry Regulars**: Many of the regulars of the old Green Griffon—the tavern that preceded the Ozloc & Dragon—are angry at their beloved watering hole's fate. Sometimes, they turn up outside and shout at the monied folk ruining "their" tavern.
- 6. **Old Cellar**: The Ozloc & Dragon's cellar is much older than the building above. Some folk say the cellar is a remnant of the old settlement that predated Dulwich.

![](_page_56_Picture_24.jpeg)

![](_page_57_Picture_0.jpeg)

# <span id="page-58-0"></span>TH E SURROUNDS

# <span id="page-59-0"></span>TH E SURROUNDING WOODLANDS

The Shadowed Keep stands at the end of an overgrown trail upon a wooded bluff overlooking a steep-sided valley. A small pack of wolves dwells in the wood as does a black bear. Characters wandering the woods may also encounter small hunting parties of bandits and goblins skulking in the gloom.

Beyond the Shadowed Keep, several other locations of interest lie in the woodland to the south of Dulwich. While this adventure cannot provide comprehensive detail of all these locales, some of the more prominent and interesting are detailed below to enable further design and development.

# TRACKS & TRAILS

A network of tracks and trails honeycomb the woodlands to the south of Dulwich. Dulwich itself stands on the South Road, which skirts the southern edge of the Salt Mire and links the western and eastern portions of the duchy. This road—a vital artery for commerce in Ashlar—is well-travelled and heavily patrolled by Wido Gall's loyal troops. Still, banditry is a constant menace.

# RANDOM ENCOUNTERS

Characters exploring the area around the keep may encounter some of the denizens lairing nearby. Alternatively, they may encounter some of the creatures dwelling in the keep. Every hour the characters are in the area surrounding the ruin, they have a 1 in 20 chance of encountering something. Roll on the table below to determine what the characters encounter.

# **D20 ENCOUNTER, EVENT OR DISCOVERY**

- 1 **Tracks**: The characters discover bandit tracks. A DC 15 Wisdom (Survival) check identifies the tracks as those of four humans. They lead toward the keep.
- 2 **Crossbow Bolt**: A crossbow bolt sticks in a tree. Judging by the moss growing on the tree's trunk and the bolt's shaft it has been here for some time.
  - **Bandits**: This group comprises one **brigand veteran**  and **three brigands**; they are only interested in attacking defenceless travellers. If the characters have previously attacked the Shadowed Keep's watchtower, the bandits unleash a volley of crossbow bolts before fleeing. This encounter does not occur at night.
- 4 **Wolves**: Searching for food, two **wolves** attack the party, and focus their attention on the smallest character. A wolf reduced to half hit points, flees.
- 5 **Campsite**: The characters discover a recently used campsite. A DC 15 Wisdom (Survival) check reveals the campsite was used two days ago by a small group of man-sized humanoids.
- 6 **Goblins**: Three **Blood Moon warriors** sneak through the wood searching for victims. They only attack small or weak groups; otherwise they retreat to warn their master of intruders.

- 7 **Goblins**: Six **Blood Moon warriors** search for bandits to kill and loot. Emboldened by their numbers, they attack from ambush, if they get the chance.
- 8 **Black Bear**: The bear shambles out of a deep thicket. It is initially indifferent to the characters and attacks only if provoked. It dwells in a small, dry cave nearby.
- 9 **Discarded Sack**: A small sack lies in the undergrowth (DC 15 Wisdom [Perception] spots); it holds four day's worth of trail rations, a waterskin and a pouch containing 15 sp.
- 10 **Ruined Cottage**: Perhaps once the home of a charcoal burner or hunter this cabin was abandoned years ago. Its roof has collapsed and its small root cellar is all but filled with leaves and other wind-blown detritus. (The cellar could make a good wolfs' den).
- 11 **Heavy Rain**: Heavy rain pummels the woodland. Characters not seeking shelter quickly get soaked (and miserable). The rain lasts for several hours.
- 12 **Quiet Woods**: One of the characters notices the woods have gone unnaturally quiet, all of a sudden. Is something creeping up on them or are they about to make an unwholesome and distasteful discovery?
- 13 **Deep Thicket**: The trees grow tall and close together, here. Gloom blankets the forest floor and going is slow. Treat the area as difficult terrain.
- 14 **Meadow**: A huge fallen tree has created a break in the forest canopy. In the sunlight, a wide swath of wild flowers and small bushes have taken hold.
- 15 **Deer**: Rustling nearby presages the appearance of two **deer**. The pair bolt, if the characters make sudden movements or attack them.
- 16 **Webs**: Thick webs festoon the branches of a dense stand of trees filling a small hollow. The hollow is gloomy and cold. Herein dwell four **wolf spiders**.
- 17 **Burial Cairn**: An old burial cairn of tumbled stone stands atop a low rise. The remains of a black flag bearing a rampant stag hangs listlessly above the cairn.
- 18 **Dead Goblin**: A decomposing goblin corpse lies sprawled under a bush. A crossbow bolt protrudes from its back. The body has been comprehensibly looted.
- 19 **Unicorn**: A **unicorn** grazes on the grass in a small clearing. If the characters are goodly, the unicorn, Vilimza, may speak with them or even heal the party's injuries. This is a good random encounter to run if the characters are lost or need critical information. Vilimza does not join the party.
- 20 **Double Trouble**: Two encounters occur at the same time. Roll twice more on this table to determine what happens; re-roll any subsequent result of 20.

3

#### <span id="page-60-0"></span>LOCAL FEATURES O F INTEREST AT A GLANCE

Beyond the Shadowed Keep, several other locations of interest lie in the woodland to the south of Dulwich. Many other sites of minor note stud the woodlands. Such locales include isolated cottages (the homes of charcoal burners, hunters and the like) as well as logging camps, bandit hideouts and so on. Additionally, characters exploring the woods will likely encounter many of its denizens—some benign, some ambivalent and some malign.

**Elle's Mere**: Elle's Mere is a rarely visited, reputedly haunted place. Tavern tales, whispered rumours, and local legends name the lake's shaded waters as home to ghosts, water spirits and worse. Even the trees growing about the lake are said to come alive to slay those venturing too close to the lake.

**Forest of Gray Spires**: While not part of Ashlar, the Forest of Gray Spires forms its southern border. Deemed all but impenetrable, wild rumours cluster thickly about these brooding woodlands and the legion of strange, slender rock spires thrusting upwards from the plateau on which the forest stands.

Adventurers often use Dulwich as a base from which to explore the forest. Many of the legends hanging over the strange forest speak of ancient inhuman empires and their glittering treasures. The Picaroon Peninsula lies hundreds of miles west and south of Dulwich; no known land route exists through the forest, but that doesn't stop the occasional explorer or traveller claiming to have forged such a route.

**Shunned Valley of the Three Tombs**: Hidden deep in the forest lies a marshy, boggy valley. Woodsmen and hunters shun the place—kept away by rumours of a terrible beast lairing within and of a ghost haunting the valley's boggy mere. But, as well as great danger, treasures magical and mundane may yet lie unclaimed in the valley, for three unexplored tombs, built by ancient hands, stand amid the mud and reeds. (For more about the valley, refer to "Shunned Valley of the Three Tombs").

**Slaughter Meadow**: This wide swath of undead-haunted greensward nestles amid the surrounding forest. Valentin Ironwolf won a great victory here when he defeated the orcs of the Severed Hand and the Blood Moon goblins at the Battle of Slaughter Meadow. Undead are said to haunt the old battlefield.

**The Demon's Bowl**: Here, a steep-sided natural amphitheatre plunges downwards several hundred feet. A rugged outcropping of jagged rock at the bowl's lowest point has given rise to numerous rumours of demon worship and foul sacrifices hanging over the place. A nameless hamlet of shacks and rude cabins straggles through the bowl. Some of the folk dwelling in the bowl suffer from leprosy; few visit the place, as a result, and Wido Gall's troops stay well clear.

**Tower of Kivutar**: The bandits and goblins lurking in the southern woodlands have learnt to avoid the Tower of Kivutar. Herein dwells the wizard Kivutar Ilmarinen (LG old female human **mage**). She is a recluse of sorts but occasionally wanders the woods near her home to gather berries, herbs and other things she needs for her experiments. Despite a foul reputation, Kivutar is a good person and helps those in need if she can.

**Valley of Bones**: Piercing the foothills of the nameless range of tree-crowned hills rising up to form the mysterious plateau on which stands the Forest of Gray Spires, the valley is a place rich in local legend. The kobolds of the Ebon Scales once claimed the valley, but Valentin Ironwolf annihilated them. The Valley of Bones is named for the battle's aftermath.

**Vongyth**: Vongyth fell to the depredations of a pair of mated dragons two centuries ago. The dragons have since been slain by the Crimson Swords adventuring group, but adventurers still go missing searching for the ruin. It is generally assumed something terrible yet lurks in the eternal dark of Clan Nurthen's fallen home.

![](_page_60_Picture_11.jpeg)

An untagged version of this map appears in the adventure's free downloadable map pack.

# <span id="page-61-0"></span>ELLE' S MERE

Crowded close by thick stands of trees clustering hard against its banks, Elle's Mere is a rarely visited, reputedly haunted place. Tavern tales, whispered rumours, and local legends name the lake's shaded waters as home to ghosts, water spirits and worse.

A ring of partially submerged stone monoliths surrounds a low, swampy tree-choked island rearing from the lake's centre. Amid the fecund undergrowth at the island's highest point stands an altar of black rock worn smooth by the rains of countless years.

A tumbled stone wall, slick with moss and lichens and obscured by thick stands of rushes, bounds the island, hinting at its artificial origin. The island is the top of a huge sacred barrow mound built hundreds of years ago by a people long since faded from the world. The (now partially flooded) barrow served as a tribal burial place and is yet watched over by an ancient guardian —a slumbering **treant** so old it has taken root above the barrow.

A colony of giant frogs dwells in and around Elle's Mere. Their cacophonous night-time croaking has given rise to the legends of ghostly hauntings at the lake.

#### LORE

A character making a DC 10 Intelligence check knows something about Elle's Mere. A successful check gains all the information revealed by a lesser check.

- **DC 10**: Elle's Mere is a reputedly haunted lake hidden deep in the woods. At night, the horrible cries of the ghosts haunting the lake can be heard echoing through the surrounds. Those entering the lake rarely emerge.
- **DC 15**: A swampy, tree-choked island lies at the centre of the lake; at its highest point stands a smooth black altar of horrible aspect.
- **DC 20**: Fragments of ancient stories speak of the trees growing on the lake's island coming alive to destroy intruders.

# FOREST O F GRAY SPIRES

South of Ashlar, where the southern woods grow thick against a lofty plateau, the woodlands give way to the legend-wreathed Forest of Gray Spires. Here, tall, slender spires of grey rock tower above the densely packed trees clustering thickly about their flanks. Eroded into weird and fantastical shapes by frequent, fierce rains lashing the plateau, these jagged splinters of limestone rear from the forest like the towers of some legendary lost fortress.

The forest is a torturous, labyrinthine place which remains almost completely unexplored. Few paths pierce its depths, and no accurate maps of the interior are known to exist. The dense forest and horrendous terrain effectively block all but the most determined or desperate of travellers.

Rumours and legends about the forest are legion. Some tales tell of a race of semi-intelligent apes dwelling deep in its most inaccessible reaches atop spires they have carved to suit their atavistic tastes. Others speak of a fallen race of forsaken, demonworshipping elves or even a lingering enclave of cyclops yet clinging to their ancient heritage amid the crumbling, mossy ruins of their former kingdom.

#### LORE

A character making a DC 10 Intelligence check knows something about the Forest of Gray Spires. A successful check gains all the information revealed by a lesser check.

- **DC 10**: The Forest of Gray Spires extends for hundreds of miles south and is all but impassable.
- **DC 15**: Rumours place the vestiges of many ancient civilisations—elvish, cyclopean and ape—within the forest.
- **DC 20**: The elves of the Gray Spires battled an ancient enemy millennia ago. They defeated their enemy, but they fell into darkness and shadow.

# SHUNNED VALLEY O F THE THREE TOMBS

Far from Dulwich, hidden deep in the forest, lies a marshy, boggy valley. Woodsmen and hunters shun the place—kept away by rumours of a terrible beast lairing within and of a ghost haunting the valley's boggy mere. But, as well as great danger, treasures magical and mundane may yet lie unclaimed in the valley, for three unexplored tombs, built by ancient hands, stand amid the mud and reeds.

#### LORE

A character making a DC 10 Intelligence check knows something about the Shunned Valley of the Three Tombs. A successful check gains all the information revealed by a lesser check.

- **DC 10**: The valley lies a day's journey into the forest. No proper paths head in that direction, but game trails crisscross the area.
- **DC 15**: A pool—Aila's Mere—named for an adventurer who drowned therein long ago fills much of the valley.
- **DC 20**: Three tombs are said to lie in the valley itself. They are variously thought to be the resting place of ancient and savage barbarians, forgotten kings or even the burial site of a long-forgotten hobgoblin tribe.

**More**: For more about the valley, refer to "The Shunned Valley".

#### SLAUGHTER MEADOW

This wide swath of greensward nestles amid the surrounding forests. Well watered by several streams flowing down from the southern hills, the meadow would be bucolic except for the vast quantity of bleached bones, rusting equipment and the like dotting the once peaceful place. Both corporeal undead (mainly **skeletons**, but sometimes **ghouls**) and incorporeal undead (mainly **ghosts** and **spectres**) are occasionally encountered here. Sometimes, adventurers come to Slaughter Meadow to search the battlefield for long-dropped loot. Some such heroes watered the meadow with their blood and added their bones to those of the numberless fallen.

#### <span id="page-62-0"></span>LORE

A character making a DC 10 Intelligence or Intelligence (History) check knows something about Slaughter Meadow. A successful check gains all the information revealed by a lesser check.

- **DC 10**: Valentin Ironwolf fought the orcs of the Severed Hand and the Blood Moon goblins at the Battle of Slaughter Meadow. It was the doughy adventurer's most famous battle. During the fighting, Valentin slew the Severed Hand's chief, Baggi the Deluded, in single combat.
- **DC 15**: The battlefield is haunted. Every year, on the anniversary of the battle, the dead rise to fight once again. (While widely believed this is untrue…probably).
- **DC 20**: The orc chieftain, Baggi the Deluded, wielded an enchanted axe which was lost during the fighting. The axe, named *Thaliat* by the elves, was reputed to have the powers of a *flame tongue* weapon.

# TH E DEMON' S BOWL

Deep in the forest, a steep-sided natural amphitheatre plunges downwards several hundred feet. A rugged outcropping of jagged rock at the bowl's lowest point has given rise to numerous rumours of demon worship and foul sacrifices.

A nameless hamlet of shacks and rude cabins straggles through the bowl. Its people are displaced, hapless folk. Here they dwell far from Lord Wido Gall's easy grasp, trusting to the dark legends of the place to keep Gall's soldiery and roving bandits away. Along with the outlaws and dispossessed, a small band of lepers also dwell here in a small network of dry caves far away from the other bowl's other folk.

The bowl's folk are foresters, hunters and—occasionally thieves of opportunity surviving however they can. The community numbers roughly 100 souls, 18 of whom suffer from leprosy. Some have nowhere else to go, while others dwell here because they like the peace, seclusion and freedom. Most of the bowl's inhabitants know the surroundings well and could serve as local guides. Money has little use for these folk; rather, most prefer payment in useful tools, luxuries such as wine and other finished goods they otherwise lack.

Notable folk include:

- **Heta Ihamuoto** (CG female human **bandit captain**) serves as the de facto leader of the bowl's folk. Friendly but wary toward newcomers, she suspects visitors of being Wido Gall's spies and watches them closely. Earning her trust is difficult. She does not, however, turn anyone in true need away.
- **Iisak Jurva** (NE middle-aged male human **commoner**) suffers from leprosy and, with a bitter heart, rails against his fate. Angry at the world and furious with anyone he thinks could heal him but chooses not to, he particularly hates clerics and the like. Murder lurks in his heart, and he is not above deliberately attempting to infect newcomers who fail to help him. Iisak has no eyebrows, and the disease has begun to melt his nose.

• **Esko Paasia** (NG young male human **commoner**) exhibits endless curiosity about the outside world and could easily become infatuated with an adventurous newcomer. He might become obsessed with a heroic warrior type or develop a devastating crush on an attractive woman in the group. Barely 15, and full of the invincibility of youth, he might follow an adventuring party when they set forth to explore the southern woods. He knows the area well and is an athletic youth blissfully unaware of his own shortcomings.

#### LORE

A character making a DC 10 Intelligence check knows one or more pieces of information about the Demon's Bowl. A successful check gains all the information revealed by a lesser check.

- **DC 10**: The Demon's Bowl is a refuge for those escaping the harsh rule of the Galls in Dulwich.
- **DC 15**: The Demon's Bowl is reputed to be a site of ancient demon worship. A jagged rock at the lowest point of the bowl served as an altar.
- **DC 20**: Some of the folk dwelling in the bowl suffer from leprosy. They dwell in caves and roam the surrounds.

# TOWER O F KIVUTAR

The bandits and goblins lurking in the southern woodlands have learnt to avoid the Tower of Kivutar. Standing on a low hill overlooking a sluggish river meandering from the gloom of the deep woods, the tower (and its mistress) are well known in Dulwich but seldom visited.

Herein dwells the wizard Kivutar Ilmarinen (LG old female human **mage**). She is a recluse of sorts but occasionally wanders the woods near her home to gather berries, herbs and other things she needs for her experiments. Ill-at-ease with other folk, she does not turn away those in need. A courteous and respectful adventuring party could find her a useful ally.

#### LORE

A character making a DC 10 Intelligence check knows something about the Tower of Kivutar. A successful check gains all the information revealed by a lesser check.

- **DC 10**: Kivutar dwells alone in her tower. She does not like to entertain visitors.
- **DC 15**: She sometimes wanders the surrounding woods. Don't be fooled by her appearance, she is a powerful wizard.
- **DC 20**: In her youth, Kivutar was a renowned adventurer and known to be a strong defender of the common folk.

#### VALLEY O F BONES

Piercing the foothills of the nameless range of tree-crowned hills rising up to form the mysterious plateau on which stands the Forest of Gray Spires, the valley is a place rich in legend.

Contorted dwarf oaks, their lichen-cloaked boughs and branches twisted into fantastical shapes, grow between mosswreathed boulders fallen from the cliffs above. The valley floor is <span id="page-63-0"></span>rocky and uneven and prone to suddenly drop off into steepsided pits, hollows and troughs gouged from the valley floor by some unknown, ancient process. This is a feral, primal place.

A fast-flowing stream courses through the valley over a halfdozen waterfalls and through a series of deep plunge pools before it turns north and west to join the mighty Selka. An overgrown pathway threads its way through the gloomy valley. Sometimes the path runs along the stream's banks, while other times it veers off into the valley's interior. At two points, the path traverses the stream on weirs of slick and slimy piled stone.

Named for the aftermath of Valentin Ironwolf's most successful campaign, where once it resounded to the harsh clarion of battle, the Valley of Bones is now a quiet place. Here, the Ironwolves trapped and annihilated the kobolds of the Ebon Scales. The kobolds dwelled in a series of small caves at the valley's head, and although they had set many traps in the valley, Valentin slowly wore down their defences over a week of bitter struggle. Trapped in the valley, the kobolds had nowhere to flee and were eventually obliterated—Valentin putting to the sword even the young in an orgy of slaughter.

#### LORE

A character making a DC 10 Intelligence or Intelligence (History) check knows something about the Valley of Bones. A successful check gains all the information revealed by a lesser check.

- **DC 10**: The Valley of Bones was the site of the Ironwolf's most comprehensive victory—the annihilation of the kobolds of the Ebon Scales.
- **DC 15**: The kobolds of the Ebon Scales dwelled in a series of tunnels at the head of the valley and, uncharacteristically, defended their home to the last.
- **DC 20**: A green dragon once dwelt in the valley, but adventurers slew it a century ago.

#### VONGYTH

Two centuries ago, the dwarves of clan Nurthen were typical of their kind. Dwelling in the fortified mine-hold of Vongyth, these industrious miners toiled deep beneath the earth to bring forth precious metals. Doughty warriors all, they fought hard to defend their home from the foul humanoids dwelling in the bizarre, grotesque depths of the Forest of Gray Spires.

Cut into the northern flank of the nameless plateau upon which stands the Forest of Gray Spires in the wilderlands beyond the Duchy of Ashlar's southern border, Vongyth is a small, isolated place. To the west, on Vongyth's very doorstep, Kymi's Run tumbles down Thangar's Steps before flowing sluggishly northwards through the human village of Longbridge and under its bridge of olden dwarven artifice into the Salt Mire. To the south lies nothing but the oppressive gloom of the Forest of Gray Spires —a vast stretch of gnarled trees clustering thickly about strange and fantastical twisted columns of jagged grey stone thrusting grotesquely, almost blasphemously, skyward.

Proficient miners, the dwarves were wealthy, and it was their wealth that spelt their doom. A mated pair of green dragons, Klauthosk and Yeiarxin, fell upon several merchants carrying gold bars and other precious metals northwards into the Duchy of Ashlar for trade. After torturing (and then eating) the few survivors, the pair learnt Vongyth's location and shortly thereafter—exhibiting typical, draconic greed—led their kobold minions in a devastating attack on the unsuspecting dwarves.

With acid and fang, the dragons drove the dwarves from their fortress, slaughtering all who resisted them. (Many of the survivors sought sanctuary in the subterranean dwarven fortress of Don Galir below the human village of Wellswood; the others dispersed further afield—many leaving Ashlar for good.) After the orgy of slaughter and looting, Klauthosk and Yeiarxin settled in the hold and ordered their kobold servants to find every scrap of treasure hidden therein. Sated by the carnage and the dwarves' hoardwealth, Yeiarxin laid several eggs, and the dragons began to terrorise and loot the surrounding area.

Thus did matters stand until the Crimson Swords invaded the hold 40 years later and slaughtered Klauthosk and Yeiarxin along with scores of their fanatical, diminutive servants. Exulting in their victory, the surviving adventurers looted the dragons' hoard and returned to civilisation to bask in the common-folks' adulation and to enjoy all the comforts of life their new wealth could provide.

The years after the Crimson Swords slew Klauthosk and Yeiarxin saw a slow trickle of adventurers and dwarves seeking Vongyth—the adventurers in hopes of finding glimmering treasures missed by the Crimson Swords and the dwarves in the hopes of reestablishing their ancient home. None who have passed Vongyth's graven valves of bronze-banded stone have returned to tell of what now lurks among the ruin of this shattered, fallen hold. Some folk whisper of a curse lingering over the place, while others mutter that perhaps the Crimson Swords did not slay all the dragons. Whatever the truth of the matter, few people now willingly seek out Vongyth.

#### LORE

A character making a DC 10 Intelligence (History) check knows something about Vongyth. A dwarf native to Ashlar automatically knows the information revealed by a DC 15 check and gains advantage on any checks made to recall further information. A successful check reveals all information gained by a lesser check.

- **DC 10**: Vongyth was a dwarven hold known for its deep mines and industrious folk. Two centuries ago, a pair of dragons and their kobold minions drove out the dwarves. Forty years later, the Crimson Swords—a famous adventuring band—slew the dragons and brought forth a great treasure from the ruined hold.
- **DC 15**: Adventurers sometimes go south to find and explore Vongyth in hopes of recovering lost treasures. Few return and it is assumed they never find the hold or that something terrible yet lurks in the dwarves' fallen home.
- **DC 20**: Before his death, Valentin Ironwolf—enticed by the stories of the dwarves' treasure—was said to have been planning an expedition to Vongyth. Some say he'd even found an old map or two of the place.

# <span id="page-64-0"></span>TH E SHUNNED VALLEY

# <span id="page-65-0"></span>TH E ADVENTURE BEGINS

The adventure begins with the party in the town of Dulwich. The Shunned Valley of the Three Tombs lies about a day's journey to the south.

#### ABOUT THE SHUNNED VALLEY

Hidden deep in the forest lies a marshy, sodden valley. Woodsmen and hunters shun this place, kept away by rumours of a terrible beast lairing within and of a ghost haunting the valley's boggy mere. But, as well as great danger, treasures, magical and mundane, lie unclaimed in the valley, for two unexplored tombs, built by ancient hands, and a small cave complex stand amid the mud and reeds.

# ADVENTURE HOOKS

Before play begins, have each character make an Intelligence check and consult "Valley Lore" to determine what they know of the place. These checks simulate the knowledge the characters have picked up while in Dulwich. Such knowledge—of a nearby site of adventure—might be enough to spark their interest in the valley and its tombs. If not, use one (or more) of the hooks presented below to propel them to the valley.

- **Aila's Fate**: One or more of the characters want to determine Aila's fate. Perhaps they are distantly related to the lost adventurer, have been hired by someone to do so or are merely curious. To use this hook, you must also run the optional encounter "Dead Aila".
- **Missing Woodsman**: A young boy, barely ten years old, approaches the party. The boy, Jani Ahokas, tells the characters of his father, Taisto, who recently disappeared into the woods near the valley. Taisto hasn't been seen for almost a week, and Jani is worried about him. He offers the party his father's meagre savings (mixed coinage worth 35 gp) if they find him.
- **Rival Sages**: A learned sage, Ilari Sianio (N male old human **noble**), is embroiled in an argument with a rival, Ulpa Varala (LN female middle-aged human **noble**), over the origin of the tombs in the valley. Ilari hires the party for 100 gp to investigate the valley and learn more about the tombs' origin. He'd also like any artefacts the party finds in the tombs. Meanwhile, Ulpa has hired other adventurers (see "Rival Adventurers") to secure the same proof; groups will likely meet in the valley.

# VALLEY LORE

A character making an Intelligence check may know something about the Shunned Valley. A successful check gains all the information revealed by a lesser result.

- **DC 5**: The valley lies a day's journey into the forest. No proper paths head in that direction, but game trails crisscross the surrounding area.
- **DC 10**: A pool—Aila's Mere—fills much of the valley. Named for an adventurer who drowned therein long ago, it is a marshy, boggy place.
- **DC 15**: Three tombs are said to lie in the valley itself. They are variously thought to be the resting place of ancient and savage barbarians, forgotten kings, or even the burial site for the chieftain of a long-extinct hobgoblin tribe.
- **DC 20**: A decade ago, a party of adventurers lost several members in the valley. The survivors buried their friends there before leaving the area.

# WHISPERS & RUMOURS

A character can use Charisma in Dulwich to gather information about the Shunned Valley and its tombs. Doing so takes 1d4 hours and requires a DC 10 check. A character exceeding this check gains one additional rumour for each 5 points by which they exceeded DC 10. Use the list below to determine what the character learns.

- 1. The ghosts of those buried in its tombs haunt the valley. They prey on travellers and explorers—many of whom do not return to tell of their adventures. (False rumour.)
- 2. Something large and predatory lives in the valley. The few woodsmen who go near the place have reported finding its leavings—droppings, half-eaten animals and so on. None have seen the beast itself.
- 3. Something terrible lives in Aila's Mere. Aila was a brave and skilled adventurer—how could such a person merely drown? Something must have dragged her into the pool.
- 4. The valley's tombs have never been opened—who knows what lies within?
- 5. The valley is very boggy. In some places, the mire acts like quicksand and can suck explorers down to a terrible death. (False rumour.)
- 6. The stories about terrible things living in the valley are rubbish. The place was explored, and its tombs were looted long ago; there's no point going there. (False rumour.)

![](_page_65_Picture_23.jpeg)

# <span id="page-66-0"></span>GETTING T O THE VALLEY

The adventure begins with the party in the town of Dulwich. The valley lies five miles to the south in the midst of a dense forest. No pathways lead to the valley, but a network of game trails crisscross the area. Going is difficult and slow:

- **Speed 30 ft**.: A group moving at a base speed of 30 feet takes four hours to reach the valley (assuming they do not get lost or delayed).
- **Speed 20 ft**.: A group moving at a base speed of 20 feet takes six hours to reach the valley (assuming they do not get lost or delayed).
- **Getting Lost**: For every hour of travel in the woods, the party might get lost. Have the character most skilled in Wisdom (Survival) make a DC 14 Survival check to avoid this fate. Getting lost wastes an hour of the party's time.

#### MINOR EVENTS

For every hour of travel, roll on the list below for a minor event or discovery:

- 1. The wind sighs through the branches, causing them to clack together like the demented chattering of some ancient, primaeval woodland spirit.
- 2. A small, non-hostile woodland animal such as a rabbit, squirrel or fox bursts from the undergrowth. The animal appears skittish and flees the party's presence.
- 3. A small clearing wreathed in wildflowers makes an excellent campsite, a good place to rest or somewhere to get one's bearings. It is peaceful here.

- 4. A wide, dense swath of brambles and bracken bars progress. Detouring around the area adds one hour to the party's journey.
- 5. A steep-sided, 15 ft. deep gulley with a stream cuts across the party's path. It takes an hour to find an easy place to cross. Alternatively, the characters can scale the gulley's sides with DC 15 Strength (Athletics) checks.
- 6. An old campsite stands in a clearing by the path; the camp's fire pit contains cold ash and is partially covered by blown leaves. Bits and bobs of discarded (and now worthless) equipment are scattered about the area.
- 7. Far off in the forest, the sounds of something large moving through the bushes reached the characters' ears. After a few minutes, the sounds fade away.
- 8. Thick clouds pass before the sun, plunging the forest into gloom. After a half-hour, the sun re-emerges.
- 9. A fallen tree lies half-sunken into the forest floor. Great stands of mouldy leaves lie piled about, and mushrooms grow thickly upon its rotten trunk.
- 10. Trees grow thickly together, plunging the forest floor into perpetual gloom. Here, the undergrowth is sparse, and the going is easier.
- 11. The half-eaten, rotting corpse of a deer lies in a pool of gore. Something large clearly worried the corpse. Other, smaller creatures—foxes and suchlike—have also subsequently feasted upon the corpse.
- 12. Large clawed tracks mar the ground. A DC 10 Wisdom (Survival) check reveals the creature was Large—about the size of a bear—and bipedal. (These are the tracks of the adult owlbear lairing in the Shunned Valley.) The tracks lead in the general direction of the valley.

Modify or reroll results as appropriate.

![](_page_66_Picture_20.jpeg)

# <span id="page-67-0"></span>TH E SHUNNED VALLEY AT A GLANCE

Several noteworthy locations lie within the Shunned Valley. Present the Player's Map to facilitate play here.

*A shallow valley lies amid the trees. A wide mere, fringed with reeds and rushes and fed by a waterfall, fills much of the valley floor. Three burial cairns lie to the east of the pool, while to the south, two lines of old statues lean drunkenly toward the sky.* 

#### A: BURIAL CAIRNS

Three stone cairns stand close to Aila's Mere.

*Three cairns of piled stones stand in a ragged triangle. Lichens and moss cover all three.* 

**Old Cairns**: Moss and lichen grow thickly on the piled stone cairns. The cairns are obviously old.

**Remains**: Each cairn holds the remains of a decade-dead adventurer. Much of their equipment has rusted or rotted away. However, perceptive characters taking the cairn apart may discover some small treasure; this takes four characters an hour. While doing so, a character making a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check finds something interesting. Use the list below to determine what they find. Use each entry only once.

- 1. A gold ring woven with silver wire (worth 50 gp).
- 2. A chipped ivory scroll tube decorated with once beautiful carvings of angels (worth 20 gp).
- 3. A rusty longsword (worth 30 gp) with a rearing wolf sigil on its pommel.
- 4. Six tiny azure blue translucent stones, each with a hole bored through the middle (azurites, each worth 10 gp).
- 5. A blunt and tarnished silver dagger (worth 22 gp).
- 6. A bronze cloak pin shaped like a dagger; usable as such by a Small-sized character (worth 20 gp).

#### B: WEATHERED STATUES

Six statues guard the entrance to location F—Champions' Rest.

*These weatherworn, moss-covered statues depict ferocious humanoid warriors. The warriors wear chainmail and hold a longsword grounded between their feet. One of the statues—the one nearest the pool—has fallen and lies in shards.* 

**Old Weathered Statues**: The statues depict hobgoblin warriors (DC 10 Intelligence determines).

**Broken Statue**: The fallen statue has half sunk into the boggy ground. Lichens and mould grow thickly upon it.

**Buried Skulls**: Characters digging below the statues discover an aged hobgoblin skull buried below each warrior. Buried to placate the tribe's war gods, each skull contains a small transparent yellow gem (a citrine worth 20 gp).

#### C: AILA' S MERE

This marshy pool fills much of the valley. Due to frequent flooding, the area surrounding the pool is boggy.

**Denizen**: A **giant frog** lurks here but has grown somewhat cowardly after several near-fatal encounters with the owlbear in location G. It attacks only when disturbed or when a tempting target is in the mere.

*A wide, marshy pool fringed with reeds and rushes dominates the valley floor. Boggy, marshy ground surrounds the pool.* 

**Calm Water**: The water is calm (DC 10 Strength [Athletics]), cold, and murky. Within 10 feet of shore, the mere is two feet deep; further out, it is five feet deep. Cloying three-foot-deep mud and silt comprise the pool's bottom.

**Boggy Ground**: The ground surrounding the pool is boggy. This does not inhibit movement, but the wet ground makes this an unpleasant place to camp.

**Frog's Lair**: The giant frog's noisome lair is hidden in the reeds. Partially eaten fish, bones and excrement dot the area.

#### D: WATERFALL

Here, a small waterfall tumbles into Aila's Mere (location C).

*A waterfall tumbles into the valley over a series of three cascades before flowing into a wide, marshy pool.* 

**Rough Water**: In the immediate vicinity of the waterfall, the water is rough (DC 15 Strength [Athletics] navigates).

**Noise**: The continuous roar of falling water imposes disadvantage on hearing-based Wisdom (Perception) checks within 20 feet of the waterfall.

#### E: TOMB O F THE STONE WOMAN

Filled with fearsome traps, this tomb has not been opened since it was sealed long ago.

*A moss-covered capstone blocks a narrow fissure in the rock. Swamp grass grows thickly over the boggy ground.* 

**Development**: Proceed to "E: Tomb of the Stone Woman".

#### F: CHAMPIONS ' REST

Herein lie two hobgoblin heroes of old. This tomb has not been disturbed since it was sealed…and one of its inhabitants is very, very hungry.

*A heavy capstone covered in verdant moss blocks what appears to be a passageway leading into the hill. Grass and weeds grow thickly about the entrance.* 

**Development**: Proceed to "F: Champion's Rest".

#### G: LAIR O F THE HUNTERS

An owlbear and its young lurk in these small caves. When the characters enter the valley, the adult owlbear is away hunting.

*A narrow crack—perhaps five-foot-wide—pierces the cliff. A faint carrion odour wafts from within. The ground is churned up around the entrance.* 

**Development**: Proceed to "G: Lair of the Hunters".

![](_page_68_Picture_0.jpeg)

# <span id="page-69-0"></span>VALLEY DRESSING

The characters are likely to spend quite some time poking about the valley. Whenever they search and don't discover anything noteworthy, roll on this list to add verisimilitude and a minor point of interest to the proceedings.

- 1. A large, mottled brown and white feather lies on the ground. The feather is obviously far too large to have come from a bird. This is an owlbear feather.
- 2. The obvious tracks of a large clawed bipedal creature mar the muddy ground.
- 3. The vegetation—reeds, rushes, or grass as appropriate—is crushed and broken. Something large obviously passed this way.
- 4. A loud, distinct splash comes from Aila's Mere. Ripples spread across the water, but their cause is unclear.
- 5. High up in the sky, a large bird circles the valley. After a few minutes, it dives into the grass, snatches a mouse and flies away to feed.
- 6. For a moment, the character catches the faint scent of carrion on the breeze.
- 7. A small patch of yellow and red wildflowers—incongruously grows amid the mud.
- 8. The wind picks up. For a moment, it sounds like the moaning of forlorn spirits.

# RANDOM ENCOUNTERS & EVENTS

To a certain extent, the characters determine the pace and direction of events in the valley. However, it's always good to throw some randomness into proceedings. Thus, during the characters' exploration of the valley, use the list below to spice up the adventure.

**Frequency of Checks**: You can roll every half-day, whenever the party exit a tomb or once a day. Make this determination based on the speed at which the characters are tackling the valley's adventure sites and the pace you want to set for the adventure.

- 1. Minor Event
- 2. Minor Event
- 3. Minor Event
- 4. Heavy Rain
- 5. Corpse in the Water
- 6. Wolf Pack
- 7. The Owlbear Returns
- 8. Rival Adventurers

#### 1-3: MINOR EVENT

To determine what minor event occurs, roll on this list:

1. A large crow flutters down and lands on one of the cairns (location A). It caws loudly and seems to peck at the rock. Unless disturbed, it continues doing this for about an hour before flying away.

- 2. A band of drizzle crosses the valley. The drizzle persists for 1d3 hours. Characters remaining outside during the drizzle eventually get wet. This has no in-game effects.
- 3. A head-sized rock loudly clatters down one side of the valley. It comes to rest in the marshy ground surrounding Aila's Mere (location C). There is no sign of what—or who—dislodged the rock.
- 4. A large branch tumbles down the waterfall (location D) and into Aila's Pool (location C). Its branches still bear green leaves. Eventually, it floats into the reeds to the west of the cairns (location A). Investigations reveal blood smeared on the branch.
- 5. The croaking of frogs from among the reeds surrounding Aila's Mere suddenly grows disconcertingly loud. If the giant frog is still alive, it joins in, adding a louder, deeper element to the chorus.
- 6. A flock of swallows wheels and dives across the sky in a complicated, mesmerising dance.
- 7. At dawn or dusk, a light mist rises from Aila's Mere (location C), cloaking the valley in its damp, ethereal embrace. The mist lingers until the next dawn.
- 8. The sound of something large roaring (or hooting if the owlbear isn't yet dead) reaches the characters' ears. The sound comes from the surrounding woodland…and is getting closer.

#### 4: HEAVY RAIN

It rains heavily and continues to rain for 2d6 hours. Characters without tents—or who don't take cover—get soaked and are (probably) miserable.

**Effects**: Heavy rain cuts visibility in half, Wisdom (Perception) checks and ranged attacks are made with disadvantage, unprotected flames are extinguished, and protected flames may be extinguished (50% chance).

#### 5: CORPSE I N THE WATER

Many foul things dwell and hunt in the surrounding forest. Several days ago, a goblin was slain, and its corpse fell into the river. Eventually, the body tumbles over the falls and into Aila's Mere (location C). Perceptive characters (DC 10 Wisdom [Perception] spots) notice it floating face down in the centre of the pool.

**The Giant Frog**: The giant frog—if still alive—also spots the corpse. It views the slain goblin as a tasty snack and attacks anyone entering the pool to retrieve it. The frog fights ferociously but retreats to its lair if reduced below 7 hp.

**Retrieving the Corpse**: If the characters retrieve the corpse, they discover it is battered and partially decomposed. The cause of death is impossible to determine, but the goblin still wears ragged leather armour and has a small shield strapped to its left arm. The shield bears the crude device of a moon dripping blood. This is the sigil of the Blood Moon tribe of goblins (DC 11 Intelligence reveals; a DC 16 check reveals the tribe are thought to lurk near Valentin's Folly—otherwise known as the Shadowed Keep on the Borderlands). The goblin has 13 sp in a sodden pouch.

# <span id="page-70-0"></span>6: WOLF PACK

Two **wolves** enter the valley searching for prey. Their scent ability gives them ample warning of something terrible lurking within location G, and they do not approach that cave. However, the rest of the valley holds no terror for them. If the giant frog is still alive, it flees into Aila's Mere (location C) and waits until the wolves leave (or are slain).

The wolves prefer to strike a lone or vulnerable target but might attack the party's camp if the encounter occurs at night. A wolf flees if reduced to less than half hit points. An injured wolf does not return.

#### 7: TH E OWLBEAR RETURNS

The **owlbear** lairing in location G returns to the valley. It enters the valley from the southeast on the north bank of the stream. Unless distracted or attacked, it drags its kill—a half-eaten deer—back to its lair (location G).

**The Young Owlbear is Dead**: The owlbear emerges from its den in a fury soon thereafter and rampages about the valley looking for revenge. Driven by rage, it attacks any creature it sees.

**The Young Owlbear is Alive**: The owlbear shares its kill and then sleeps until the next morning. Then, in the afternoon, it emerges to hunt again. If it spots the party, it attacks and fights until slain.

#### 8: RIVAL ADVENTURERS

A rival band of adventurers arrives in the valley, intent on exploring the tombs. They might be working for the sage Ulpa Varala (see "Adventure Hooks"). The group comprises:

- **Aelliah Uthliavar** (NE female elf; Appendix 1): This smoothtalking, beautiful woman has a cold, merciless heart.
- **Elir Garsten** (N male dwarf; Appendix 1): This dour, foulmouthed dwarf has a burning hatred for goblins and their ilk.
- **Helmi Ojanen** (NE female human; Appendix 1): Fascinated by how things work, Helmi lacks many social skills required for civilised society.
- **Vesa Takala** (NE male human; Appendix 1): Handsome and cold-hearted, Vesa is obsessed with magical power.

The group are black-hearted and cares nothing for any claim the characters might have over the valley.

**Tactics**: When the adventurers first meet the characters, they feign friendship, try hard to ingratiate themselves with their rivals, and appear as nonthreatening as possible. They set up camp at the opposite edge of the valley.

Their plan is simple. They don't see the point in breaking into these tombs when someone else will do it for them. Thus, they only attack once the characters have cleared out all three tombs (preferably when the characters are injured or as they rest overnight before leaving the valley).

#### AELLIAH UTHLIAVAR

*This slender elf's silver hair tumbles over her shoulders and her purple eyes seem alive with amusement.* 

This smooth-talking, beautiful elf has a cold, merciless heart.

**Personality**: Merciless and utterly self-obsessed, Aelliah delights in bending the weak-willed to her whims.

**Mannerisms**: Beautiful and graceful, Aelliah's rarely—if ever raises her voice.

**Distinguishing Features**: Aelliah's purple eyes constantly sparkle as if she is permanently amused.

**Background**: Exiled from her homeland after being caught blackmailing several men, she lusts for revenge.

#### ELIR GARSTEN

*This dwarf is wide and heavily muscled, and his thick black beard is neatly trimmed. He wears battered but serviceable scale mail and carries several weapons.* 

This dour, foul-mouthed dwarf has a burning hatred for goblins and their ilk.

**Personality**: Dour and foul-mouthed, Elir is a joy to be around. He blames the world for his status as an outcast.

**Mannerisms**: Elir is hard of hearing in his left ear; he cocks his right ear towards those speaking to him.

**Distinguishing Features**: Elir's left ear is crushed and broken the legacy of an ogre's club.

**Background**: Elir was banished from his home after he refused to serve in the militia. With nowhere to call home, he has wandered ever since.

#### HELMI OJANEN

*Lank brown hair frames this human woman's oval-shaped face.* 

Fascinated by how things work, Helmi lacks many social skills required for civilised society.

**Personality**: Abrupt and rude in manner, Helmi is not pleasant company. Fascinated with machinery and how it works, she is never happier than when tinkering with her latest acquisition.

Helmi is used to living rough—or at least from day to day. She is tough, resilient and self-sufficient. She greatly desires to accumulate enough coin to live a life of comfort and excess. In fact, she has already identified the house she plans to buy; she even occasionally breaks in to look around while the current owners slumber in their beds.

**Mannerisms**: Dextrous and possessing great coordination, Helmi often dances a battered copper coin—her lucky coin—across the knuckles of her left hand.

**Distinguishing Features**: Helmi rarely smiles; instead, her face seems locked in a perpetual grimace. Her attempts at smiling appear ridiculous in the extreme.

**Background**: Beaten as a child, Helmi distrusts everyone and hates being vulnerable—either emotionally or physically. She grew up in Dulwich and has had several run-ins with the law. There, she is known as a petty thief.

#### <span id="page-71-0"></span>VESA TAKALA

*Slender and pale-skinned skinned, this handsome man has a ready smile. He wears polished studded leather armour.* 

Handsome and cold-hearted, Vesa is obsessed with magic and power.

**Personality**: Driven to understand and control magic, Vesa is a fanatical follower of Morden the god of magic. Vesa senses some additional power within himself and is eager to understand them. Even though he plans to murder them, he will happily engage in hours of conversation about magic with any wizards or sorcerers he encounters.

**Mannerisms**: Vesa always smiles, no matter the situation. His grin grows truly wide when treasure is within his grasp.

**Distinguishing Features**: Vesa has perfect, white teeth (of which he is very proud).

**Background**: Both Vesa's parents had sorcerous abilities magic is literally in his blood. His mother was also a priestess of Morden and inducted him into the clergy as soon as he was old enough. He hungers for power and to surpass his hated parents' abilities.

# OPTIONAL ENCOUNTER: DEAD AILA

Use this encounter if the players are experienced or seem keen on roleplaying. Note that **Aila** is a potent foe for 1st-level characters, and if the group is prone to unrestrained violence, this encounter may go poorly (for them).

**What Has Gone Before**: Aila was a neophyte druid who, with her companions, stumbled into the valley while tracking an injured deer. While she examined the deer's tracks, the owlbear burst forth from its lair and surprised the group. It quickly killed three of the party and forced another to flee. Seeing all was lost, Aila retreated into the mere. The owlbear did not follow her but waited on the bank for her to emerge from the lake. Eventually, Aila tired and drowned, and the owlbear wandered off after savaging the three slain adventurers.

Once the owlbear left, the lone survivor returned and buried all the remains (location A) he could find. He couldn't find Aila—but had seen her enter the mere—and so named it in her memory. Her spirit has haunted its waters ever since.

![](_page_71_Picture_11.jpeg)

# MEETING AILA

If the characters spend some time poking about the mere, Aila becomes aware of them. She silently emerges from the water near the waterfall and floats across the lake to speak with them. Her ghostly appearance may cause panic among the adventurers:

*The ghostly, translucent figure of a woman— long black hair gently floating in the air around her—emerges from the turbulent water near the waterfall. Silently, she glides toward you.* 

Aila starts the encounter indifferent toward the adventurers. However, if they have obviously broken open the cairns of her fallen companions (location A) she is unfriendly.

- **Indifferent**: Aila asks the characters to recover her bones from the mere and then bury her near her slain companions. She can offer no physical reward but warns the party of the owlbear (location G) and giant frog (location C).
- **Unfriendly**: Aila demands the party rebuild her companion's cairns. Doing so—and acting apologetic—makes her indifferent toward the party.

**Personality**: Death has given Aila a new appreciation of nature and its beauty. She has taken great solace in watching the creatures—even the owlbear—living in and around the valley, and she has no desire to "leave."

**Distinguishing Features**: Aila's hair gently floats in the air about her head as if caressed by unseen (and unfelt) currents.

**Mannerisms**: Aila often seems to struggle for breath before speaking—this is a symptom of her death by drowning. She is touchy about this subject if the characters mention it.

# RETRIEVING AILA' S REMAINS

Aila would like to be laid to rest in a cairn alongside her fellow adventurers. If the characters retrieve her remains from the mere and bury them, award the party 350 XP. Aila thanks them for their efforts but can offer them no material reward.

Aila's mouldering corpse is buried in the mud and sludge at the bottom of the mere near the waterfall.

• **The Mere**: The water near the waterfall is ten feet deep and rough (DC 15 Strength [Athletics]). The waterfall churns up the muddy water, reducing visibility underwater to mere inches.

**Searching**: Finding enough of Aila's bones to satisfy the ghost is difficult. It takes a character able to swim 2d4 hours to retrieve the bones, but more than one character can search the lake. A character who fails to make a DC 15 Strength [Athletics]) check does not provide meaningful assistance.

• **Attack of the Killer Frog**: If the characters have not yet dealt with the giant frog lairing in the nearby reeds, their extended presence in the water draws it forth. Hungry, it decides to snack on an adventurer. It targets a character in the water. Once it has caught a snack, it drags its victim back to its lair.

# <span id="page-72-0"></span>E: T OMB O F THE S TONE WOMAN

This tomb, filled with fearsome traps, has not been opened since it was sealed centuries ago. Within lie the remains of an ancient hobgoblin wizard. She was both feared and respected by her fellows—hobgoblins tend to distrust "elf magic"—and so to keep her quiet in her grave, they built this elaborate tomb.

#### GENERIC TOMB FEATURES

The Tomb of the Stone Woman has these generic features:

**Illumination**: Darkness.

**Worked Stone Floor**: The stone floors are relatively smooth and free of obstruction.

**Dust**: Thick dust covers the floor. No tracks are evident.

**Worked Stone Walls**: The walls are smooth (DC 20 Strength [Athletics] scales) and covered in peeling yellowed whitewash. Faded murals showing hobgoblins in battle cover the walls. Some areas in the tomb have specific murals of interest; these are detailed in the relevant location descriptions.

**Stone Doors**: These doors are heavy and difficult to open (DC 15 Strength forces) but not locked.

**Ceiling**: The ceilings are of worked stone and roughly eight feet high.

# E1: ENTRANCE

A heavy capstone wards access to the tomb.

*Weeds grow thickly about this heavy moss-covered capstone.* 

**Capstone**: This capstone is heavy and difficult to roll aside (DC 20 Strength moves). It has a crude carving of an esoteric rune (DC 15 Intelligence [Arcana] reveals the rune means "danger") graven upon it.

# E2: DEATHTRAP CORRIDOR

This seemingly empty corridor is a death trap.

*Dust lies heavily on the floor here. Faded murals of hobgoblins in battle cover the walls.*

**Murals**: The niche opposite the entrance to E3 has a particularly lurid mural of a female hobgoblin calling down fire and lightning to slay her enemies.

**Traps**: Two traps—a collapsing ceiling trap and a poison gas trap that activates shortly after the ceiling collapses—ward this area.

• **Collapsing Ceiling Trap**: Part of the ceiling is rigged to collapse. When the door to E3 is opened, the ceiling above the square nearest the entrance collapses, sealing would-be robbers inside.

• **Poison Gas Trap**: Tiny holes pierce the corridor's walls. Six rounds after the ceiling collapses, poisoned gas starts to issue into the corridor.

#### E3: TH E LURE

This chamber is designed as a lure for the traps in E2.

*Three dusty chests stand in this small storage area. The middle chest is open, and within it lies a great mass of coins.* 

**Chest 1 (Locked)**: This old wooden chest is in bad condition but is locked (DC 15 Dexterity check made with thieves' tools unlocks). It contains mouldy (worthless) clothes of ancient cut. The chest has a shallow false bottom (DC 20 Wisdom [Perception] spots) containing six transparent red gemstones (jaspers, each worth10 gp).

**Chest 2 (Open)**: This open chest contains a mass (794 cp and 476 sp) of tarnished copper and silver coins. The coins are primitive things from kingdoms long since fallen into ruin.

**Chest 3 (Locked)**: This old wooden chest is in bad condition but is locked (DC 15 Dexterity check made with thieves' tools unlocks). It contains a carefully folded but mouldy and fragile black banner depicting a flaming lightning bolt. If roughly handled, the banner falls apart. A transparent pale blue stone (a tourmaline worth 250 gp) is hidden in its folds.

#### E4: TH E BAT TLE VAULT

Frescos on the walls here depict some of the hobgoblin wizard's greatest victories.

*Faded frescos depicting many battle scenes cover the walls. In all of them, a female hobgoblin is depicted annihilating her foes with lightning and fire.* 

**Frescos**: If a light source is in the room, a character making a DC 15 Wisdom [Perception] check notices some elements of the frescos glimmer and glitter. Investigation reveals the outlines of the wizard's spells are picked out with gemstone fragments. Characters spending an hour carefully removing these fragments gather gem fragments worth 25 gp.

![](_page_72_Picture_31.jpeg)

#### <span id="page-73-0"></span>E5: CHAMBER O F LIVING STONE

Herein stands the Stone Wizard. Imbued with a fragment of the long-dead hobgoblin wizard's power, the statue is animate, and it attacks any and all intruders.

*A low, rough-hewn stone sarcophagus fills the centre of this chamber. Behind the sarcophagus, on a low stone plinth, stands the stone statue of a female hobgoblin clad in form-hugging robes.* 

**Denizen**: The statue—the **Stone Wizard**—depicts the ancient hobgoblin wizard. It stands upon a low stone plinth. The Stone Wizard steps down from its plinth and attacks when robbers defile the sepulchre by trying to force open the lid. It chases intruders but does not leave the tomb.

**Trap**: The round after the Stone Wizard steps down from her plinth, the dart swarm trap activates.

**Sarcophagus (External)**: This stone sarcophagus has a rough finish—as if the mason didn't finish the job. The lid is heavy (DC 18 Strength check opens). It shatters if pushed off onto the floor.

**Sarcophagus (Internal)**: A mouldering skeleton amid the decayed remains of once fine robes of an elder cut lies inside the sarcophagus. Amid the bones lies a plainly wrought silver dagger etched with mystical symbols that was the wizard's arcane focus. The bones also wear a set of rotting leather bracers decorated with gold and silver wire worth 25 gp.

**Sarcophagus (Underneath)**: The sarcophagus hides a stone trapdoor which protects the entrance to the Dread Shrine of the Supreme Warlord. Characters searching the chamber may notice (DC 18 Perception spots) an intriguing groove in the floor next to the sarcophagus; this is an edge of the trapdoor. Dragging the sarcophagus aside reveals the trapdoor.

# F: CHAMPIONS ' REST

Herein lie the remains of two hobgoblin heroes—Craz and Drezna —of old. This tomb has not been disturbed since it was sealed… and one of its inhabitants is very, very hungry.

# GENERIC TOMB FEATURES

The Tomb of the Champions' Rest has these generic features:

**Illumination**: Darkness.

**Worked Stone Floor**: The stone floors are relatively smooth and free of obstruction.

**Dust**: Thick dust covers the floor. No tracks are evident.

**Worked Stone Walls**: The walls are smooth (DC 20 Strength [Athletics] scales) and covered in peeling and yellowed whitewash. Faded murals cover some of the tomb's walls. The relevant area descriptions detail specific murals of interest.

**Stone Doors**: These doors are heavy and difficult to open (DC 15 Strength forces) but not locked.

**Ceiling**: The ceilings are of worked stone and roughly eight feet high.

# F1: ENTRANCE

A heavy capstone wards access to the tomb.

*A large capstone wards access to whatever lies beyond. It bears a worn and moss-spattered depiction of two warriors lying side by side on a stone bier.* 

**Capstone**: This capstone is heavy and difficult to roll aside (DC 20 Strength moves).

#### F2: HALLWAY

This hallway is unoccupied.

*A dusty corridor ends in a stone door roughly 50 ft. away.* 

**Illumination**: Dim light fills the corridor when the capstone at location F1 is rolled aside.

**Faded Mural**: A mural of two hobgoblin warriors surrounded by piles of slain foes decorates one wall.

#### F3: SLEEPLESS MINIONS

Goblin slaves were left here to serve their masters in death.

*Three burial niches pierce this short corridor's walls.* 

**Denizens**: Three **tomb guards**—undisturbed for centuries—lie here. They animate when intruders reach location F2.

**Burial Niche**: Covered in dust, each niche bears faded pictures of goblin warriors depicted in ferocious poses. There are no grave goods in the burial niches.

#### F4: EMPTY CHAMBER

Intended as a burial chamber, this room was never finished.

*The walls of this chamber have been hewn from the rock but not whitewashed like the others.* 

**Carven Walls**: The walls are of undecorated worked stone.

#### F5: SHIELDS O F THE FALLEN

This room displays battle trophies taken by Craz and Drezna.

*Dusty shields and timeworn banners hang from the walls here.* 

**Faded Murals**: Murals of battle cover the walls. Each of the banners and shields hanging here are cleverly woven into the scenes—in which hobgoblins are winning every encounter.

**Banners**: The banners are ancient tribal devices; none of the tribes survive to the present day. However, a sage interested in such matters (or a noble trying to increase their house's standing) might pay 100 gp for the collection.

#### F6: LAIR O F THE FALLEN

Herein rest Craz and Drezna. Lovers in life they rest together eternally. Horrifyingly, Drezna—depraved in life—rose as a ghoul and was so hungry she gnawed the decomposing flesh from her lover's bones.

<span id="page-74-0"></span>*A wide stone bier stands in the centre of this chamber. Faded murals cover the whitewashed walls.* 

**Denizens**: A **tomb guard** attends **Craz** and **Drezna**. All three are ready for combat. Craz and Drezna view the tomb guard as expendable but aid each other in battle.

**Stone Bier**: A three-foot-high, ten-foot-wide stone bier stands in the centre of the chamber.

**Faded Murals**: Murals cover the walls of the chamber. One scene depicts two hobgoblins during an act of love, another shows them using skulls as drinking cups, and a third shows them surrounded by slain enemies.

**Treasure**: The two champions carry the only treasure here. Refer to their stat blocks for more information.

# G: LAIR O F THE HUNTERS

An owlbear and its young claim this small cavern complex. Luckily, when the characters arrive, the adult is away hunting.

#### GENERIC CAVE FEATURES

The caverns have the following generic features:

**Illumination**: Darkness.

**Stench**: The smell of wet fur, rotting flesh and faeces pervades this cave complex.

**Floor**: Covered in rubble and the remains of the owlbears' hunts, the floor throughout the lair is difficult terrain. Dexterity (Acrobatics) checks are made in the cave with disadvantage.

**Remains**: The remains of dozens of creatures—wolves, deer, foxes and other woodland beings—cover the floor. Some are little more than skeletons; others yet rot. A DC 10 Wisdom (Medicine) check reveals all were killed by something clawed and immensely strong.

**Walls**: Climbing the cave walls is easy (DC 15 Strength [Athletics] scales). In several places, the owlbears have sharpened their claws on the walls, leaving deep scrape marks in the rock.

**Ceiling**: Small stalactites hang from the ceiling. The ceiling varies in height between five and ten feet.

**Natural Stone Steps**: These natural stone steps are difficult terrain. Dexterity (Acrobatics) checks are made on the stairs with disadvantage.

#### G1: ENTRANCE

Beyond this narrow entrance lies the owlbears' lair.

*The stench of carrion, wet fur and other unwholesome smells emanate from this narrow cave mouth. Bones and chunks of unidentifiable meat lie just beyond the entrance.* 

**Tracks**: A character searching around the narrow crack who makes a DC 5 Wisdom (Survival) check identifies the tracks of a large clawed creature entering and exiting the cave. A DC 10 Wisdom (Survival) check reveals the presence of an additional smaller set of tracks among the larger tracks.

**Illumination**: Dim light from outside pervades the first 30 ft. or so of the cave. Beyond, darkness reigns.

**Fur & Feathers**: The adult owlbear squeezes through this narrow passage. Consequently, clumps of fur and feathers are stuck to the walls. A DC 14 Intelligence (Arcana) identifies these as coming from an owlbear.

# G2: HALL O F RUIN

This corridor comprises the "spine" of the complex.

*The passageway widens to perhaps 20 feet in places. To the right, a set of natural steps disappears down to a lower level. Further on, an escarpment drops away to another cave.* 

**Escarpment**: A 20 ft. high escarpment provides access (DC 10 Strength [Athletics] scales) to location G5. The smell of excrement wafts up from the bottom of the escarpment.

#### G3: OWLBEAR NURSERY

One young owlbear lurks in the nursery, noisily consuming a wolf's corpse. Luckily for the characters, it is distracted by its meal (it has disadvantage on Perception checks) and may not notice them.

• **DC 5 Wisdom (Perception)**: The character hears crunching bones and tearing flesh coming from the cave.

*Hunched in a corner lurks a bizarre half-bear, half-owl monstrosity the size of a grown man. It greedily tears at a dripping chunk of flesh it holds in its claws.* 

**Denizen**: When it notices intruders, the **young owlbear** hoots loudly and attacks. It fights savagely and to the death.

**Nest**: A pile of broken tree branches, rotting flesh and cracked bones in one corner is the young owlbear's nest.

**Shattered Egg**: The shards of two large shattered eggs lie about. Mixed in with the detritus of the nest are the skeletal remains of a tiny owlbear.

![](_page_74_Picture_33.jpeg)

<span id="page-75-0"></span>![](_page_75_Picture_0.jpeg)

# G4: OWLBEAR NEST

Herein, lairs the adult owlbear.

*The stench in this chamber is almost overpowering. A large pile of tree branches forms a noisome nest while the remains of various animals are scattered about.* 

**Large Nest**: The owlbear's nest comprises a pile of broken tree branches, rotting flesh, and cracked bones. Mixed in with the detritus are a human's gnawed remains.

• **Dead Hunter**: These are Taisto Ahokas' remains (see "Adventure Hooks" for more information). Wearing a tattered cloak and hunter's clothes this human male has been partially eaten. He has 15 sp and 3 gp along with a small potion vial containing effervescent red liquid (a *potion of greater healing* in a blood-stained pouch. He also has a dagger hidden in his boot (DC 15 Wisdom [Perception] finds).

#### G5: CAVE O F BATS

Hundreds of bats live among the stalactites here.

• **DC 5 Wisdom (Perception)**: The terrible smell emanating from this chamber differs to that found elsewhere in the caves.

*Stalactites grow thickly on the roof of this high chamber. Piles of rank-smelling guano cover the floor.* 

• **DC 14 Wisdom (Perception)**: If a character looks into the cave, they spot scores, if not hundreds, of tiny bats hanging upside down among the stalactites.

**Denizens**: Countless bats slumber among the stalactites. If they are attacked or a bright light is brought into the cave, they for a **swarm of bats** and attack.

**Stench**: The smell of excrement fills this chamber.

**Ceiling**: The ceiling is 30 ft. high and festooned with stalactites. Creatures among the stalactites gain half cover (+2 AC, +2 Dexterity saves).

**Guano**: Piles of guano cover the floor to a depth of about one foot. A character searching the guano who makes a DC 10 Wisdom (Perception) check discovers some skeletal remains. Searching characters must also make a DC 10 Constitution save or contract a disease.

• **Skeletal Remains**: Buried beneath the guano lies the broken body of a dwarf killed by a falling stalactite. Much of his equipment is ruined, but a character searching the remains finds a heavy warhammer, the head of which is engraved with lightning symbols. The dwarf also possesses four small yellow transparent gemstones (jaspers, each worth 50 gp) and 14 sp, 13 gp and 2 pp.

#### <span id="page-76-0"></span>DREAD SHRINE O F THE SUPREME WARLORD

The entrance to the Dread Shrine lies under the sarcophagus in location E5.

Centuries ago, the powerful hobgoblin warlord Morg Drolak dominated much of the land that would become the Duchy of Ashlar. However, like all living things, eventually, he fell—whether to time's remorseless onslaught or a foe—history does not record. His followers built him a subterranean shrine and tomb to celebrate his glory and his devotion to Malbut, the greater god of hobgoblins, bravery, war and conquest. They hid the place below a simple tomb for one of Morg's concubines, and gradually, but inevitably, the place slipped from the memory of the world.

Nothing stays hidden forever, though.

#### MALBUT, THE LORD O F WA R

LE greater god of hobgoblins, bravery, war and conquest

**Epithets**: The Lord of War, Marshal of the Eternal Host, the Bloody Axe

**Symbol**: A double-headed battleaxe

**Domains**: Death, War

**Favoured Weapon**: Battleaxe

**Raiment**: Malbut's worshippers are never without their armour; even at rest, they wear studded leather armour. Hobgoblin warriors wear chain mail at the least, while champions and priests wear plate armour. Plate armour normally has Malbut's double-headed battleaxe engraved into its breastplate, while worshippers clad in chain cover it with a red or black surcoat similarly emblazoned.

**Worshippers**: Hobgoblins, hobgoblin warriors

**Teachings**: War is the natural state of things; diplomacy and compromise are the refuge of the weak. In discipline, there is strength. Obey orders. The strong take what they want, and the weak die. If a warrior must die, a glorious, brave death ensures their place in the Eternal Host.

**Holy Texts**: Malbut's faithful take their lessons from the *Book of War*. Each *Book of War* is different. While each book lists Malbut's core teachings, the faithful acknowledge that war is an ever-changing thing and that the tactics and strategy required for victory constantly evolve. Each church or tribe thus uses the book to record their victories and defeats and the lessons they learned from their struggles. Thus, does the faithful's knowledge of war and its practices evolve.

**Additional Notes**: Services to Malbut often feature the ritual killing of enemies captured on the battlefield. The faithful's bodies are burnt on pyres so that their spirits can join Malbut in his Obsidian Citadel.

**Temples & Shrines**: Malbut's temples and shrines are often underground and are always extensively decorated with battle booty taken from the hobgoblins' slain enemies. Images glorifying Malbut—ever triumphant—are carved into the walls; it is a great honour for a hobgoblin chief or warrior to be added to the carving as one of Malbut's warrior-companions.

# TH E ADVENTURE BEGINS

The characters may find the Dread Shrine of the Supreme Warlord while searching the Chamber of Living Stone (location E5) in the Tomb of the Stone Woman. If they fail to find it, use one of the hooks below to draw them back to the tomb (if you so desire).

- **Ancient Map**: During an adventure, the characters recover an ancient map from a monster's treasure hoard. The ragged map shows the location of "Drolak's Tomb". Deep in the wild woods, the tomb's isolated location presents the possibility that it has not yet been looted.
- **Getting Out of the Storm**: The characters are trapped in the Shunned Valley while a horrendous storm savages the area. They wait in the Tomb of the Stone Woman and while doing so, one of the characters notices the partial outline of what could be a hidden trapdoor under the tomb's sarcophagus.
- **Talkative Peasants**: The characters overhear two hunters talking about a recent discovery either they or an adventurer made. They talk about an unopened, secret trapdoor hidden in a looted tomb. They'll share the tomb's location for a fee.

# WHISPERS & RUMOURS

A character might know something about the Dread Shrine of the Supreme Warlord. Perhaps they are steeped in local lore. Alternatively, they may have heard a rumour about the place while drinking in a tavern or overheard two locals gossiping while browsing a marketplace.

Use this list to determine what the character knows:

- 1. In ancient times, a mighty hobgoblin warlord claimed much of the land that was to become the Duchy of Ashlar as his empire. History forgets his ultimate fate.
- 2. Hobgoblins once ruled the surrounding lands; every now and then, adventurers—or sometimes even peasants tilling their fields or collecting wood in the deep forests— come across old sites linked to the hobgoblins.
- 3. The mightiest of all the ancient hobgoblin warriors and warlords was Morg Drolak. His prowess was legendary. He was said to have even defeated death.
- 4. Hobgoblins worship Malbut, their Lord of War. Champions and chieftains are believed to join their patron's Eternal Host when they die.
