- 5. Hobgoblins are the most martial and organised of the goblin races. Some tribes subjugate wide territories and gather much wealth and glory to their banners.
- 6. Morg Drolak—the mightiest of all the ancient hobgoblin warlords was buried in a secret tomb which has never been found. It is bound to be stuffed full of antiquities and treasure!

(Not all the rumours above may be true; determine the veracity of the information based on your vision for the Dread Shrine.)

#### <span id="page-77-0"></span>NOTABLE LOCATIONS AT A GLANCE

The dungeon has several notable locations.

- 1. **The Forgotten Entrance**: This passage is the only entrance to the Dread Shrine of the Supreme Warlord.
- 2. **Antechamber**: Carvings on this chamber's walls show Malbut's Invincible Host striking down a horde of orcs.
- 3. **Western Processional**: Replete with statues of long-dead hobgoblin champions and a pair of sarcophagi (one holding a skeletal warden), this corridor runs almost the entire length of the shrine.
- 4. **The Flooded Font**: Fed by a natural underground spring, this font leaks after heavy or sustained rainfall.
- 5. **Eastern Processional**: This corridor hides a secret door.
- 6. **Chapel of War**: Two animate guardian axes ward this sacred chamber. They attack anyone coming within five feet of the dais who does not bear Malbut's sigil.
- 7. **Secret Chamber**: This secret chamber and its attendant secret doors (see locations 5 and 6) enabled the shrine's priests to enter the chapel without raising the portcullis.
- 8. **The Grand Processional**: In this corridor, the hobgoblins' heroic dead were cheered a final time before they were interred in the crypts to the north.
- 9. **Chamber of the Sacred Axe**: Herein, the hobgoblins gathered to venerate Malbut's favoured weapon. A charnel guardian yet protects the chamber.
- 10. **Hall of Victory**: This chamber is the antechamber to the Necropolis of Heroes (location 11) and the Warlord's Rest (location 12). Here, the hobgoblins gathered to chant the many victories of their buried warlord.
- 11. **Necropolis of Heroes**: Four zombie hobgoblin warriors rest in their sarcophagi, waiting for Morg Drolak, to call them to once again march forth to war.
- 12. **Warlord's Rest**: Here, amid the dust of ages, Morg Drolak awaits Malbut's call.

# GENERIC DUNGEON FEATURES

Many of the dungeon's locations share certain features:

**Illumination**: Darkness.

**Ceilings**: The arched ceilings are ten-foot-high in the corridors and most of the chambers.

**Stone Walls**: The walls are of dressed stone (DC 20 Strength [Athletics] scales) in fair condition. In places, moss and lichen grow on the walls, and water oozes through the crumbling mortar.

In corridors, iron torch sconces are set every 20 feet on opposite walls. Most sconces are empty, rusty and dusty.

**Flagstone Floor**: The floor's flagstones have started to shift and move under time's remorseless influence, but generally, they do not inhibit movement.

**Wooden Door**: Warped and rotting wooden doors (AC 13, hp 15, immune to poison and psychic damage; DC 15 Strength opens) open into the room or space beyond. Most are in a poor state of repair. A locked door can be opened with a DC 15 Dexterity check made by someone using thieves' tools.

**Stone Steps**: The flights of stone steps in the shrine are well crafted and count as difficult terrain.

#### DUNGEON DRESSING

Use this list to breathe life and detail into the dungeon:

- 1. Deep dust lies on the floor; nothing has passed this way for many long centuries.
- 2. Dust-wreathed cobwebs hang from the ceiling, creating grey curtains that undulate slightly as the sluggish air flows through the tomb.
- 3. Water oozes through cracks in the wall to drip onto the nearby floor. Thick greyish sludge covers the damp section of the floor.
- 4. Cold, dirty water drips from a crack in the ceiling.
- 5. Drifts of dust have accumulated against the walls.
- 6. Dusty grey cobwebs hang from the ceiling and waft gently as the characters pass underneath.
- 7. A flagstone rocks slightly under a character's foot.
- 8. Scattered rubble, issuing from a small collapse in a wall, lies across a small section of floor.
- 9. A faint breeze ruffles the characters' hair; it comes from the direction of location 1.
- 10. A faint moaning sound fills the air—outside, powerful winds batter the valley.

# THINGS TO FIND

Use this list to determine what minor objects or features of interest the party find if they search a dungeon location. Modify the value of items found to suit your campaign.

- 1. This small golden broach—perhaps once used to secure a cloak—is wrought in the shape of a spear.
- 2. Three thin golden coins lie amid the dust. Their designs are worn away, and they are little more than golden disks.
- 3. Scratches on the wall in Goblin spell out the message, "All Hail the Lord of War".
- 4. An old, dusty battleaxe leans against a wall.
- 5. The brittle, charred stub of a torch lies amid the grime.
- 6. A single worn silver coin lies amid the dust.
- 7. A flagstone rocks under a character's foot; underneath it, a small hollow hides a silver battleaxe unholy symbol.
- 8. This tiny stone figurine of a hobgoblin warrior is missing its left arm (and weapon).
- 9. Scraps of rotting tapestry are scattered across the floor; a few gold and silver threads, however, have survived time's remorseless onslaught.
- 10. An iron dagger of exceptional strength and sharpness is stuck into a crack in the wall; only its worn handle is visible, so deeply is it buried.

# <span id="page-79-0"></span>1: TH E FORGOTTEN ENTRANCE

This passage is the only entrance to the Dread Shrine of the Supreme Warlord.

*A narrow set of stone steps descends steeply into darkness. Stalesmelling air wells up the stairs.* 

**Stone Trapdoor**: The stone trapdoor is heavy but has a thick iron ring set at its centre. It has not been raised for centuries (DC 20 Strength opens).

**Stale Air**: Stale-smelling air wells from the passage below the trapdoor once it is opened.

**Stone Stairs**: The stone stairs descend for about 30 feet; they are difficult terrain.

**Iron Portcullis**: This rusty but still strong iron portcullis (AC 19, hp 40, damage threshold 10, immune to poison and psychic damage; DC 23 Strength lifts; a Small creature squeezes through with a DC 20 Dexterity check) wards access to the Chapel of War (location 6). It has not moved for centuries. If a character lifts it and does not wedge it in place, it immediately falls back into its original position.

# 2: ANTECHAMBER

Carvings on this chamber's walls show Malbut's Invincible Host striking down a horde of orcs.

*Intricate, low-relief carvings shrouded in dust and spider webs cover the walls of this small, square chamber.* 

**Bas-Relief Carvings**: The carvings depict an epic battle between an iron-shod hobgoblin army—the Invincible Host—and an orc rabble. Throughout the carvings, the hobgoblins are shown slaughtering the orcs. An observant character making a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check spots a small section hidden away near the floor in which a hobgoblin depicted fleeing the battle is cut down by one of its fellows.

#### 3: WESTERN PROCESSIONAL

Replete with statues of long-dead hobgoblin champions and two sarcophagi, this corridor runs almost the entire length of the Dread Shrine.

*Two niches in the passage's western wall hold statues of hobgoblin warriors. A third niche holds a sarcophagus, while a fourth holds nothing but a pile of rubble and bones.* 

**Foes**: A skeletal warden lurks in the intact sarcophagus; it attacks anyone opening the sarcophagus.

**Southern Statue**: This stone statue depicts a proud hobgoblin warrior wearing ornate but archaic plate armour and holding a battleaxe grounded before it. The warrior wears a closed helmet.

![](_page_79_Picture_16.jpeg)

**Viewing Slit**: This viewing slit is designed to allow those not allowed into the chapel to gaze upon the services held therein. The viewing slit provides three-quarters cover (+5 AC, +5 Dexterity saves). Small-sized characters can squeeze through the slit with a DC 15 Dexterity check. Medium-sized characters must make a DC 20 Dexterity check to squeeze through. (Note, however, it may be impossible for bulky characters or those wearing rigid metal armour to squeeze through.)

**Sundered Sarcophagus**: A pile of bones, rusting armour and rubble is all that remains of a plain stone sarcophagus and its honoured occupant. The pile fills the niche and is difficult terrain. Nothing of value remains in the pile.

**Intact Sarcophagus**: This plain sarcophagus (DC 15 Strength opens) holds the skeletal remains of a hobgoblin priest—he was one of the Dread Shrine's wardens and yet watches over the fane in death as a skeletal warden. The warden attacks as soon as the lid of the sarcophagus is opened. While it stands in the sarcophagi, it has half cover (+2 AC, +2 Dexterity saves).

**Northern Statue**: This stone statue depicts a snarling hobgoblin warrior wearing plate armour with a raised battleaxe above its head—as if ready to strike. If a light source is present, a character making a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check notes the hobgoblin's brown eyes glimmer. Investigation reveals the statue's eyes comprise small translucent brown stones (jaspers, each worth 50 gp).

# 4: TH E FLOODED FONT

Fed by a natural underground spring, this font leaks after heavy or sustained rainfall.

*A large, roughly wrought stone font stands in the centre of this small, square chamber. Much of the floor here looks damp.* 

**Flooding Font**: The mortar holding the font together has failed over the long centuries. After heavy or sustained rainfall, water oozes through the cracks between the stones and onto the floor.

**Slippery Floor**: The floor around the sundered font is slick and slippery; it is difficult terrain.

#### 5: EASTERN PROCESSIONAL

This corridor hides a secret door.

*Darkness fills this dusty and cobweb-shrouded narrow corridor.* 

**Viewing Slit**: This viewing slit is designed to allow those not allowed into the chapel to gaze upon the services held therein. The viewing slit provides three-quarters cover (+5 AC, +5 Dexterity saves). Small-sized characters can squeeze through the slit with a DC 15 Dexterity check. Medium-sized characters must make a DC 20 Dexterity check to squeeze through. (Note, however, it may be impossible for particularly bulky characters or those wearing rigid metal armour to access the chapel in such a fashion.)

**Secret Door**: A secret door (DC 20 Wisdom [Perception] finds, DC 15 Intelligence [Investigation] locates the door's mechanism—a slightly raised piece of flagstone) pierces the west wall of this area.

# <span id="page-80-0"></span>6: CHAPEL O F WA R

This chamber is sacred to Malbut.

*A raised dais set with two altars and a bronze statue of a huge hobgoblin clad in war gear dominate this shrine. Carvings of war decorate the walls. An iron lever juts from the east wall.* 

**Foes**: Two animate guardian axes ward this sacred chamber. They attack anyone coming within five feet of the dais who does not bear Malbut's sigil.

**Ceiling**: The arched ceiling is 20 feet high in the centre of the room and about 15 feet high where it meets the walls.

**Low Dais**: A five-foot high dais edged with three broad steps is the chapel's focal point. The steps are difficult terrain.

**Statue of Malbut**: This 12-foot-tall old bronze statue is a tribal relic. It depicts the hobgoblin god, Malbut, the Lord of War (LE greater god of hobgoblins, bravery, war and conquest), in all his martial glory. He is depicted wearing ornate plate armour and wielding a battleaxe. The statue can be scaled with a DC 10 Strength (Athletics) check.

**Western Altar**: Images of warrior hobgoblins decorate this altar. A battleaxe—a guardian axe—lies atop it next to a beaten silver tray (worth 50 gp).

**Eastern Altar**: An ancient flag—faded and stained by time—is draped over this altar. A battleaxe—a guardian axe—lies atop it next to an oversized, ceremonial silver goblet of simple design (worth 50 gp).

**Carvings**: Low-relief carvings depicting arrayed ranks of hobgoblin warriors worshipping Malbut decorate the walls.

**Secret Door**: A secret door (DC 20 Wisdom [Perception] finds, DC 15 Intelligence [Investigation] locates the door's mechanism pushing in the head of a battleaxe in a nearby carving) pierces the chapel's north wall.

**Portcullis Mechanism**: This iron lever controls the portcullis to the south. It is rusted and stuck in place with long disuse and requires a DC 15 Strength check to first operate. Once operated, the characters hear clanking for about one minute before the portcullis ponderously rises.

#### 7: SECRET CHAMBER

This secret chamber and its attendant secret doors (see locations 5 and 6) enabled the shrine's priests to enter the chapel without raising the portcullis.

*Dust lies thickly about the floor of this small chamber. Two rusting iron levers jut from the room's walls.* 

**Iron Levers**: The levers are rusted and stuck in place with long disuse. When first used, the lever of an unopened door requires a DC 15 Strength check to operate.

**Alcoves**: These two alcoves each hold high relief carvings of hobgoblin war priests clad in all their finery. Both individuals are depicted as heavily scarred; one has lost an eye. Both are wearing ceremonial plate armour and carrying large battleaxes.

# 8: TH E GRAND PROCESSIONAL

In this corridor, the hobgoblins' heroic dead were cheered a final time before they were interred in the crypts to the north.

*A stone door with graven words upon it pierces the north wall of this curved corridor. A huge carving of a hobgoblin war host carrying their dead toward a series of immense burial cairns decorates the walls.* 

**Carven Stone Door**: This stone door (AC 17, hp 20, damage threshold 8, immune to poison and psychic damage) is heavy and hard to force open (DC 20 Strength succeeds). The carving on the doors says, in Goblin:

#### *"Beyond Lie the Lord of War's Heroic Dead. Disturb Them Not."*

**Bas-Relief Wall Carvings**: The impressive and intricate carvings decorating these walls show a hobgoblin host carrying their war dead toward a series of immense burial cairns. A character making a DC 15 Intelligence (Investigation) check notices that a particularly ornate sarcophagus carried by six warriors leads the procession.

**Tapestry**: A tapestry depicting yet another scene of heroic battle—in which hobgoblins slaughter an army of dwarves and elves—hides the entrance to the Chamber of the Sacred Axe. A character physically examining the tapestry automatically discovers the entrance; other characters who make a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check notice something odd about how the tapestry is hanging.

A character behind the tapestry is heavily obscured. Characters can scale a tapestry with DC 10 Strength (Athletics) checks; however, a tapestry only supports 130 lbs. of weight. (Common sense suggests the tapestries are unlikely to support heavy climbers.) Heavier characters rip the tapestry from the wall once they have climbed ten feet; such climbers suffer 1d6 damage and land prone.

**Secret Door**: Two secret doors (DC 20 Wisdom [Perception]

![](_page_80_Picture_26.jpeg)

#### <span id="page-81-0"></span>9: CHAMBER O F THE CLEAVING AX E

Herein, the hobgoblins gathered to venerate Malbut's favoured weapon. A charnel guardian—wrought as a huge axe-shaped statue**—**protects the chamber.

*A man-sized stone statue of a battleaxe stands behind an altar at the end of this roughly circular split-level chamber. Two short staircases provide access to the higher level, where tapestries decorate the walls, and four axe-shaped pillars rise to meet the lofty ceiling.* 

**Foes**: A charnel guardian protects this chamber. The charnel guardian animates five minutes after a living creature enters the chamber unless a battleaxe is placed on the groove in the altar. Placing a battleaxe in the groove after the statue has animated commands the statue to return to its plinth (unless it is subsequently attacked).

**Ceiling**: The arched ceiling is 25 feet high in the centre of the room and about 20 feet high where it meets the walls.

**Tapestries**: Tapestries depicting heroic hobgoblins, their heads bowed in prayer, decorate the walls of this chamber and the short passageway leading to it. A character behind a tapestry is heavily obscured. Characters can scale a tapestry with DC 10 Strength (Athletics) checks; however, a tapestry only supports 130 lbs. of weight. (Common sense suggests the tapestries are unlikely to support heavy climbers.) Heavier characters rip the tapestry from the wall once they have climbed ten feet, fall prone and suffer 1d6 damage.

**Tapestry Remnants**: The remnant of a tapestry lies on the floor in the northeast part of the chamber. Here, water oozes through a crack in the ceiling, and a remnant of sodden and slimy tapestry is all that remains.

**Stairs**: Two short flights of steep stone steps lead upward to a higher level, which stands about ten feet above the floor; the stairs are difficult terrain.

**Stone Pillars**: These slender stone pillars are styled like immense axes whose curved heads blend into the ceiling.

Characters in an adjacent square to a pillar gain half cover (+2 AC, +2 Dexterity saves).

**Statue**: This battleaxe-shaped carven statue—actually a variant charnel guardian—stands upon a low plinth at the southern end of the chamber.

**Altar**: This otherwise plain, severely hewn stone altar bears a battleaxe-shaped groove cut into its top. The altar is hollow, and a DC 20 Wisdom (Perception) check discovers a secret door in the side facing into the chamber. A subsequent DC 20 Intelligence (Investigation) check reveals that pushing in the door's top left

# AR E THOSE MUMMIES ?

The characters may panic when the mummified zombie warriors emerge from their various resting places if they mis-identify the undead as mummies. That's an intentional decision design to add excitement and a sense of danger to the encounter.

and bottom right corners causes it to spring open. Doing so releases a noisy cascade of old coins onto the floor.

• **Treasure**: The coin-hoard comprises 2,134 cp, 1,056 sp and 73 gp.

# 10: HALL O F VICTORY

This chamber is the antechamber to the Necropolis of Heroes (location 11) and the Warlord's Rest (location 12). Here, the hobgoblins gathered to glorify their warlord's many victories.

*Four man-high wrought iron candelabras stand about this room. An altar covered in the decaying flag or cloth fills a niche to the north. A battleaxe lies on the altar.* 

**Altar**: This plain stone altar is about three feet high and fills much of the niche in which it stands. The rotting scraps of a war banner once red and black but now mostly faded to grey—cover the altar. A battleaxe rests upon the altar.

**Iron Portcullises**: Rusty but still strong iron portcullises (AC 19, hp 40, damage threshold 10, immune to poison and psychic damage; DC 23 Strength lifts; a Small creature squeezes through with a DC 20 Dexterity check) wards access to the adjacent chambers (locations 11 and 12). They have not moved for centuries. If a character lifts a portcullis and does not wedge it in place, it immediately falls back into its original position.

**Wrought Iron Candelabras**: Four six-foot high wrought iron candelabras stand about this chamber. The candelabra closest to each portcullis features a clever, hidden mechanism which both anchors it to the floor and controls the nearby portcullises.

- **Is This a Trap?** A character investigating the candelabras who makes a DC 15 Intelligence (Investigation) check understands what their mechanism will do. A subsequent DC 15 Dexterity check made by a character proficient with thieves' tool can modify this mechanism so that each candelabra only operates the nearest portcullis.
- **Opening the Portcullises**: Pushing a candelabra away from the nearby portcullis (DC 15 Strength check to first operate) causes both portcullises to slowly (and loudly) rise up into the ceiling. The portcullis nearest the pushed candelabra opens in 1d4+2 rounds, while the other takes an additional three rounds to open fully. Opening the portcullises awakens the undead in locations 11 and 12.

#### 11: NECROPOLIS O F HEROES

Four part-mummified zombie hobgoblin warriors rest in their sarcophagi, waiting for Morg Drolak to call them to once again march forth to war.

*Four intact sarcophagi fill niches cut into the walls of this chamber. A pile of rubble, bones, wisps of grey cloth and scraps of armour fills a fifth niche.* 

**Foes** Four part-mummified zombie hobgoblin warriors rest in the sarcophagi. They awaken two rounds after the portcullises start to rise or when the sarcophagi are opened.

<span id="page-82-0"></span>**Tapestry**: A dusty and faded, brittle tapestry hangs behind the portcullis, obscuring an easy view of this room. It reaches to the floor and obscures all view of what lies beyond.

**Sarcophagi**: Four plain stone sarcophagi each fill a shallow niche. Each contains a zombie hobgoblin warrior.

**Rubble-Filled Niche**: Part of the ceiling has collapsed, and a pile of shattered rubble, broken bones, scraps of grey linen and the remains of a hobgoblin's battle gear fills this niche. The dusty pile is difficult terrain.

#### 12: WARLORD' S REST

Here, amid the dust of ages, the Warlord awaits Malbut's call.

**The Approaches**: Even when the tapestry over the entrance is moved aside, neither the altar, the statue, nor the urns are visible from the entranceway.

*A bronze statue covered in verdigris stands in a small niche in the north wall behind a plain stone altar. Four small urns stand on stone plinths carved from the chamber's south wall.* 

**Foes**: If the characters open the portcullis, the warlord, Morg Drolak, awakes. Sounds of nearby battle also bring him forth. Alternatively, he becomes aware of their presence once the characters enter the chamber through the secret door. After a few minutes, if he has not been discovered, he bursts forth to slay the interlopers. The guardian axe on the altar animates one round after Morg Drolak emerges from the statue.

**Tapestry**: A dusty and faded, brittle tapestry hangs behind the portcullis, obscuring an easy view of this room. It reaches to the floor and obscures all view of what lies beyond. Even when the tapestry is moved aside, neither the altar, the statue, nor the urns are visible from the entranceway.

**Altar**: An axe and a half-dozen skulls lie on the plain and austere altar (The axe is a guardian axe).

**Statue**: This hollow bronze, verdigris-speckled statue holds the part-mummified remains of the warlord, Morg Drolak. Morg can easily open the statue from the inside.

• **Treasure**: The warlord's half-plate armour, etched with a battleaxe sigil and curiously free of damage and rust, is still usable. It may have to be resized to fit a victorious warrior. (This costs between 10 and 40% of the armour's base value— 750 gp).

**Urns on Shelves**: Four small stone plinths carved from the

chamber's southern wall display a plain c e ra m i c u r n . E a c h u r n contains fine grey dust—the cremated remains

of one of the warlord's greatest enemies.

#### AFTERMATH

Once the characters have explored the Dread Shrine of the Supreme Warlord and dealt with its denizens, resolve the adventure hook(s) that brought them to the place.

If you used any of the hooks presented in "The Adventure Begins", use these notes to resolve the adventure's aftermath:

- **Ancient Map**: The ancient map the characters recovered could show other locales of interest or note; perhaps such are so faded that the characters only notice them once they again examine the map—perhaps idly by the fire one night while recovering from their adventure.
- **Getting Out of the Storm**: Once the storm has abated or moved on, and the characters have completed their investigation of the Dread Shrine, they can continue their onward journey.
- **Talkative Peasants**: If an adventurer found the trapdoor the peasants gossiped about, that individual (and their friends) would be less than pleased that the characters beat them to the tomb. If they discover the characters' identities, this could set up a minor rivalry between the two groups.

![](_page_82_Picture_21.jpeg)

# <span id="page-83-0"></span>C ONCLUSION

The Shunned Valley of the Three Tombs is an open-ended adventure site, and the party can leave the valley whenever they please. Once they have completed their exploration, they'll likely return to Dulwich to sell their loot and report to their employer.

- **Missing Woodsman**: Assuming they found his father's remains, Jani tearfully thanks the party and offers them the agreed reward. It should be blindingly obvious, however, to even the dimmest adventurer that if Jani pays them, he'll end up virtually destitute. If they refuse payment, award them 100 XP. In this instance, Jani begs them to let him come with them; he can't adventure, but he can tend their fire at night, cook, clean and so on. He forms a particularly strong bond with whichever character most strongly refuses payment.
- **Rival Sages**: Ilari Sianio pays the party the agreed 100 gp, if they provide credible information regarding the origins of the tombs in the valley. If they have done a particularly comprehensive job, he mentions that the ruin of Valentin's Folly lies in the woods to the southwest and that such a place might be of interest to adventurers like themselves. He adds that if the party discovers items of interest in the ruined keep, he might be interested in purchasing them.

# FURTHER ADVENTURES

While the party may have exhausted the possibilities for adventure in the Shunned Valley of the Three Tombs and the Dread Shrine of the Supreme Warlord, other adventure sites lie nearby. In particular, the ruined Valentin's Folly—otherwise known as the Shadowed Keep on the Borderlands—lies nearby. (The party may already be aware of the keep because of Random Event #5: Corpse in the Water.)

- **The Shadowed Keep**: A ruined monument to folly and ego, the Shadowed Keep (Valentin's Folly on the area map) stands atop an isolated bluff deep in a mist-wreathed forest. Sacked by marauding goblins and orcs decades ago, the place was thought abandoned, but shadows now creep among the forest's great boles and footprints have appeared on the overgrown, tenebrous track leading to the keep. Travellers have begun to disappear with alarming regularity from the nearby road and local folk fear some slumbering evil has claimed the ruin as its own.
- **Returning Hobgoblins**: Perhaps a local tribe of hobgoblins learn of the discovery of the Dread Shrine and claim it and the valley above as their new home. If the characters hear of this development they may feel obligated to meet and end this new threat.

![](_page_83_Picture_8.jpeg)

# <span id="page-84-0"></span>TH E SHADOWED KEEP

# <span id="page-85-0"></span>AN OVERVIEW O F THE SHADOWED KEEP

Valentin's Folly is a small, simple fortification. Construction was never completed, and so it lacks many of the features of a more sophisticated, grander and better-financed fortress. It lacks a stout gatehouse, and the donjon never gained crenelations or much of an upper floor. However, although the keep appears like a ramshackle ruin, much of its structure remains intact.

- **Outer Walls**: Stout, crenellated outer walls protect the courtyard and donjon. A walkway, accessed by two stairs and from the watchtower, runs around much of the outer wall.
- **Courtyard**: The keep's muddy courtyard once held several wooden buildings, including a stable and smithy.
- **Tumbled Buildings**: All that remains are heaps of charred and rotten, moss-covered wood.
- **Tracks**: Tracks crisscross the courtyard; mainly, they lead between the donjon, the watchtower and the main gate.

#### TH E DONJON

This two-storey building is of solid construction, but even those with no engineering knowledge can tell the donjon was never completed. The building lacks crenelations, and several large stone blocks stand on the roof (presumably where Valentin's labourers left them when the money to pay them ran out).

Encounter areas in the donjon are prefaced with a D. Stat blocks for the donjon's denizens appear in Appendix 3.

# TH E WATCHTOWER

The keep has one watchtower. A small band of bandits claim the tower and guard it carefully against the Blood Moon Goblins lurking in the donjon's cellars. When they are not waging inconclusive war against the goblins, the bandits skulk in the surrounding woodlands waiting for foolish or unlucky travellers to blunder into their clutches. The human bandits never wander the woods at night.

Encounter areas in the watchtower are prefaced with a W. Stat blocks for the watchtower's denizens appear in Appendix 3.

#### TH E DONJON' S CELLARS

The Goblins of the Blood Moon claim the donjon's cellars as their lair. From here, they creep forth at night to hunt for food and victims and occasionally try to break into the bandits' tower.

Encounter areas in the cellars are prefaced with a M. Stat blocks for the cellar's denizens appear in Appendix 4.

#### TH E UNDERCRYPT

Encounter areas in this abandoned, undead-infested portion of the dungeons are prefaced with a U. Stat blocks for the undercrypt's denizens appear in Appendix 5.

![](_page_85_Picture_17.jpeg)

![](_page_86_Picture_0.jpeg)

# <span id="page-87-0"></span>TIMELINE O F ADVENTURE

The Shadowed Keep is a dynamic living environment. Therein, the Blood Moon Goblins war with the bandits of the watchtower for control of the place, while within the goblins' ranks, the shaman Sar (M11) plots to overthrow his bestial chieftain.

Thus, when the characters arrive, each group is pre-occupied with defeating the other. When not fighting the characters, the bandits and the goblins don't simply sit around doing nothing. A few bandits might sneak into the woods searching for prey, while the goblins may launch a night-time attack on the bandit's tower.

#### EVENTS DAY B Y DAY

The following notes suggest a sequence of events you can use to bring the Shadowed Keep to life. You can follow the timeline below as detailed or simply pick and choose events that look interesting or that will enhance play. You can also use the events below as a way to give the characters experience points if they need a few more to level.

Some of these events happen at specific times, while others are triggered by the characters. The characters' actions, of course, might render some of these events moot; simply ignore or modify such events as required. For example, if the goblins attack the bandits' watchtower after the characters have killed all the bandits, the goblins will either fight the characters or ransack the tower (if the characters are elsewhere).

#### DAY 1

The characters arrive at the Shadowed Keep. Neither the goblins nor the bandits are aware of their presence (unless random encounters in the surrounding woodlands dictate otherwise).

That night, the goblins launch a raid on the bandits' tower. A group of six **Blood Moon warriors** led by **Razogen**, Ruknar's son, sneak out of the donjon and try to burn down the tower's front door. The goblins fail and withdraw when two of their number are

# CUSTOMISING EVENTS

You'll know how fast your players will likely explore the Shadowed Keep. If your players are the type to cautiously explore the place over several weeks or months, you might want to slow down the pace of the events detailed above so they don't all occur while the party are off resting elsewhere.

Conversely, if you want to emphasise the low-grade conflict between the goblins and brigands, have the bandits approach the characters for aid as soon as they reach the Shadowed Keep. Most groups are much more likely to aid the brigands than the goblins. However, for fun you could also have Sar approach the characters with his proposal as soon as is practicable. Such interactions give the characters a real sense of the antipathy between the goblins and the brigands; clever players will find a way to exploit this!

slain by bandits hurling down chunks of masonry into the courtyard from the tower's roof.

#### DAY 2

A light drizzle greets the dawn. Around midmorning this turns into a downpour that lasts for most of the day. For the next two days the stream connecting W2 and M2 is a raging torrent; travel along its course is impossible.

#### DAY 4

Three **brigands** led by a **veteran brigand** emerge from the woods and return to the watchtower. If they discover it sacked (or in the hands of the characters), they loot what they can and flee. If not, they reinforce their fellows and can be found in location W5.

#### DAY 5 (NIGHT)

Four hungry **wolves** enter the courtyard. They scratch at the door of the watchtower but do not enter the donjon.

#### DAY 6 (NIGHT)

Six **Blood Moon warriors** return to the tribe. Unless needed elsewhere, they lair in M7.

#### DAY 7

Three **brigands** led by a **veteran brigand** leave the tower in search of prey. They disappear into the woods and set up watch over the road to Dulwich. They return empty-handed (and in a foul mood) at sunset.

#### DAY 8

Gentle rain falls over the keep and its surrounds during the morning. It stops around midday, but the day remains gloomy.

#### DAY 8 [NIGHT]

Angered at continually being stuck in the kitchen, **Bareli** (location W4) gathers her treasure and deserts the brigands, slipping out of the tower at dusk. She immediately makes a run for the woods, trusting to her darkvision to see her through. She avoids contact with the characters if she can help it and flees to Dulwich. If she encounters the characters, she tries to strike a bargain with them they let her go free in return for detailed information about the tower's defenders and so on.

#### DAY 9

Three **brigands**—bored by the drudgery of living in the tower decide to explore some of the donjon. They investigate locations D1 and D3i (where they find a be-gemmed dagger [result 11-15 on the random treasure table]) before losing their nerve when confronted by the **monstrous viper** in location D6 and returning to the watchtower.

#### DAY 10 (NIGHT)

**Ruknar** stirs himself from the company of his concubines and leads a dozen of his minions (nine **Blood Moon warriors** and three **Blood Moon bruisers)** in an assault on the watchtower. The goblins attack in the dead of night. Ruknar batters down the <span id="page-88-0"></span>tower's front door and the goblin warriors surge inside. They easily take the ground floor, but Firean is a skilled warrior and manages to keep the goblins contained downstairs. The goblins discover the prison in the basement and rescue Yar before brutally slaying Reithic.

By the time the goblins withdraw, dawn is breaking. Three **brigands** and six **Blood Moon warriors** lie dead.

**Note**: Be careful running this encounter if the characters have claimed the watchtower from the bandits. This is an incredibly tough encounter for a low-level group of characters; however, the watchtower provides significant defensive advantages. Even if the goblins get inside, they baulk at fighting their way up the stairs into the tower's upper reaches. Have them retreat when you deem the characters have done enough to break their morale.

#### DAY 12

A thick fog shrouds the area, providing concealment in the courtyard as obscuring mist. The fog burns off by about midday.

#### DAY 18

In the early morning, the bear living in the surrounding woods (see "Surrounding Territory") wanders into the courtyard, looking for food. It only fights if attacked or threatened.

# CHARACTER-TRIGGERED EVENTS

#### BANDIT PARLEY

If the characters investigate the ruined donjon without attacking the bandit's watchtower, the bandits notice the party's arrival. Realising the characters could be powerful allies in her battle against the goblins, Firean tries to enlist them to her cause.

She directs the sentries atop the watchtower to keep an eye out for the returning adventurers. When the party emerge from the donjon, the sentry hails them and also calls for Firean. She quickly climbs to the tower roof and negotiates with the characters for help eradicating the goblins. If the characters agree (and if she believes them), Firean allows them to rest in the watchtower between forays. Unless victory over the goblins is certain, she does not commit her forces to the attack.

Sadly (but unsurprisingly), Firean is unpredictable and greedy. Unless the characters seem content to leave the keep after defeating the goblins, she has her warriors fall upon them when they are sleeping, disorganised or otherwise distracted.

#### GOBLIN ATTACK

If the characters have made two forays against the Blood Moon, but have not yet slain Ruknar, the goblins organise a counterattack. At night, a large force led by Ruknar's son, Razogen (location M12), emerges from the cellars and falls upon the characters. If the characters are in the watchtower, the goblins attack both outside doors at once and try to burn their enemies out. If the characters are camping in the woods, the goblins surround their campsite before unleashing a hail of missiles.

#### SA R' S TREACHERY

After the characters' first successful foray into the Blood Moon's lair, Sar (location M11) realises they represent his best chance of getting rid of Ruknar. Accompanied by his two loyal guards, he creeps forth to negotiate with the characters.

Sar desperately wants to rule the Blood Moon tribe and agrees to practically anything to get what he wants. He can give the party full details of the cellars, explain where guards are set and so on. Of course, he doesn't want to stand by any agreement he makes and turns on his puppets as soon as is practical.

#### RIVAL ADVENTURERS

If you want to introduce an element of haste to the characters' exploration, you can have a group of rival adventurers arrive in the area. At first, these NPCs can linger at a local tavern, searching for information, interrogating locals and (possibly) even trying to get information out of the characters. (This warns the characters that rival adventurers may soon venture to the keep and gives them an impetus to speed up their own exploration.) If you want to build the rival theme further, engineering a barroom brawl between the two groups can be fun and a great change of pace.

When you judge the time right, the rival adventurers finally reach the Shadowed Keep and start poking around. Of course, they are somewhat more unsavoury than the characters and have no qualms about slaying the party for its treasure.

- **Kuura Otra** (NE male human **bandit captain**) wants gold—lots of gold. Kuura dreams of retiring and opening an inn. He loves bar-hopping, mainly to spy on potential future rivals, and is a borderline alcoholic. Perpetually dishevelled and pale-skinned, Kuura has deep bags under his eyes, which make him look sad. He is a merciless foe.
- **Noora Ilakka** (N female human **druid**) loathes the undead, viewing them as foul monstrosities that must be put down at all costs. Rabid, in her defence of nature, Noora has a onetrack mind and is utterly unable to compromise. She wears a thick bear-skin cloak no matter the weather or situation. With tousled brown hair, a deep tan and freckles, she is attractive and uses this to her advantage.
- **Samu Rauma** (NE male human **cult fanatic**) leads the group through dint of his cunning. In love with his intelligence, Samu views his companions as nothing but tools and won't risk his life to help them. Samu worships Braal and dreams of rising high in his shadowy lord's service.
- **Vilutar Toiva** (CN female human **berserker**) forgets herself in battle, falling into a frenzy at the first sight of blood. Vilutar is larger than life—she drinks, she carouses, and she slays. Life is good. Impetuous and supremely dangerous, she acts first and thinks last (if at all). With short-cropped hair, a tattooed neck and stocky figure, Vilutar is an imposing sight—particularly when drenched in her enemies' blood.

Not every encounter with this group must include all four adventurers. Each NPC has a challenge rating of 2; for low-level groups, such a fight would almost certainly prove disastrous.

# <span id="page-89-0"></span>WATCHTOWER O F THE BANDIT QUEEN

A small bandit gang claims the keep's watchtower. Led by the halfelf bandit queen **Firean Maiethil** (location W7) and her cowardly henchman **Cullen Asikka** (location W6), the brigands have had little success recently in their skirmishes with the Blood Moon goblins lairing in the chambers below the donjon. The goblins keep travellers away from the keep's immediate environs, and the brigands lack the numbers to crush the goblins. Firean dreams of defeating the goblins and claiming the whole fortress for her own. She plans to use the keep as a base from which to exert her will over the nearby villages. Soon, she will rule all Ashlar!

Most of the brigands within the tower are typically blackhearted but nondescript villains, but a few are worthy of note:

- **Bareli (W4)**: This half-orc woman is an army deserter, a terrible cook and a mean drunk. Firean sees her as a threat to her hold over the bandits.
- **Cullen Asikka (W6)**: Devoted to his dog, Fang, Cullen is a coward who flees if the brigands' cause seems lost.
- **Firean Maiethil (W7)**: With delusions of grandeur and the dream of making the Shadowed Keep the foundation of a kingdom forged in war and blood, Firean is the most dangerous of the tower's inhabitants.

All the stat blocks for the watchtower's denizens appear in Appendix 3: Watchtower Denizens.

#### ARCHITECTURE & ENVIRONMENT

The tower has the following general features.

**Ceilings**: The ceilings in the tower are 12 ft. high.

**External Walls**: Although of solid construction, the tower's outer walls have begun to deteriorate. Mortar between the great stone blocks has begun to flake away. The walls can be scaled with DC 20 Strength (Athletics) checks.

**Arrow Slits**: Arrows slits provide three-quarters cover and allow dim light to filter into the tower. Small-sized characters can squeeze through an arrow slit with a DC 15 Dexterity check. Medium-sized characters must make a DC 20 Dexterity check to squeeze through an arrow slit. (Note, however, it may be impossible for particularly bulky characters or those wearing armour to gain access to the keep in such a fashion.)

**Shuttered Windows**: Windows are normally open during the day (except in bad weather) but firmly shuttered at night.

**Spiral Staircase**: A spiral staircase (which is difficult terrain) links the tower's above-ground levels. Combatants on the stairs gain half cover against attacks from below.

**Internal Wooden Doors**: Unlocked wooden doors (AC 15, hp 20, immune to poison and psychic damage) ward most rooms. Doors open into the room beyond. A locked door can be opened with a DC 15 Dexterity check made with thieves' tools.

**Wooden Floor Boards**: The tower's first and second floors have wooden floorboards that creak when walked upon. The floorboards impose disadvantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to move quietly across such areas.

#### TOWER DEFENCES

Having fought several skirmishes with the Blood Moon goblins, the bandits have prepared defensive plans to fight off any intruders. Unless in use, external doors are barred day and night, and the bandits react quickly to repel any incursion.

If enemies are without, two **brigands** move to the tower roof and hurl stones down upon their enemies. The others hold the guardroom (location W1) as long as possible before retreating upwards. They tenaciously defend location W3, hurling stones down upon intruders daring the stairs. If intruders force their way into location W3, the brigands either flee onto the battlements via location W5 or retreat to the tower roof. If both Cullen and Firean have fallen or fled, surviving bandits flee or surrender.

# RANDOM ENCOUNTERS

The characters have a 1 in 10 chance of encountering some of the tower's denizens for every 10 minutes they remain in the watchtower. Each encounter can occur only once. If the creatures are defeated, remove them from the relevant encounter area.

#### **D20 LOCATION ENCOUNTER**

| 1-5   | W5 | A brigand visits W2 to draw water.                                         |
|-------|----|----------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 6-9   | W5 | A veteran brigand wanders the tower<br>looking for a gambling partner.     |
| 10-13 | W4 | Bareli carries a tray of food and drink to the<br>prisoners in W2.         |
| 14-16 | W6 | Fang (Cullen's beloved wolfhound)<br>wanders the tower looking for snacks. |
| 17-18 | W6 | Cullen decides to take Fang for a hunt in<br>the surrounding woodlands.    |
| 19-20 | W7 | Firean Maiethil makes a surprise<br>inspection of her troops.              |

#### WATCHTOWER KE Y

- **W1 Brigand Guardroom**: The gang keep a constant guard here, and the outer door is normally barred from within.
- **W2 Dungeon of the Bandit Queen**: The tower cellar doubles as a well room and prison.
- **W3 Hallway**: The tower's hall is a key defensive position for the bandits should intruders force their way into the tower.
- **W4 Kitchen**: **Bareli**—army deserter and terrible cook—lairs here.
- **W5 Barracks**: Here dwells the bulk of Firean's gang. The door leading to the battlements is normally barred from within.
- **W6 Cullen's Chamber**: The cowardly **Cullen** lives here with his beloved hound, **Fang**. Cullen flees if things seem grim.
- **W7 Chamber of the Bandit Queen**: The Bandit Queen's quarters hold most of the gang's loot. **Firean** can normally be found here unless she is leading her troops in the tower's defence.
- **W8 Tower Roof**: During the day, two **brigands** keep watch here. At night, the roof is deserted.

![](_page_90_Figure_0.jpeg)

<span id="page-91-0"></span>![](_page_91_Picture_0.jpeg)

# W1: BRIGAND GUARDROOM

**Denizens**: This guardroom is always occupied. Two **brigand veterans**—Adhearn and Conn—keep watch here.

*A closed iron-bound door pierces the tower's wall. The door's sturdy wood bears signs of assault—it is pitted and splintered, and scorch marks mar its bottom portion.* 

**Investigating the Door**: A character making a DC 10 Wisdom (Perception) check hears murmured conversation behind the door. A character making a DC 15 Wisdom (Survival) check discovers Medium- and Small-sized tracks around the door. The tracks lead through the keep's gate or to the donjon (location D1).

**Breaking Down the Door**: The tower's iron-banded door (AC 17, hp 30, damage threshold 5, immune to poison and psychic damage, DC 25 Strength check opens) is barred from the inside. Attempting to break down the door automatically draws the attention of Adhearn and Conn. Two rounds after the party start battering down the door, the two **brigands** on the tower's roof (location W8) notice the commotion.

#### GETTING IN: VIOLENCE

If intruders try to break in, Conn dashes upstairs to alert his fellows while Adhearn flips over the table and loads their crossbows. Two rounds later, Conn returns, and they ready to shoot at the first intruder through the door. If this drops the attacker, the bandits fight on. If not, they drop their crossbows and retreat upstairs.

#### GETTING IN: GUILE & PERSUASION

The characters can use guile and cunning to get into the tower.

- **Adhearn** is a lazy, cantankerous drunk. He is on guard duty as punishment for falling asleep at his post several days ago. He is short-tempered and tired.
- **Conn** has known no other life. He dislikes Adhearn, and is a romantic who dreams of finding wealth and fame as well as love through his banditry.

**Deception and Persuasion**: The bandits are hostile to strangers and wary of anyone coming to the tower door. A character can bluff way into the tower with a DC 20 Charisma (Deception) or (Persuasion) check by convincing the brigands the group wants to join the band. Alternatively, a character can make a DC 15 Charisma (Deception) check to pretend to be bandits returning from a foray into the woodlands.

**Outcome**: If the characters are successful, the bandits unbar the door and let them in. If the characters fail, the bandits refuse to open the door, and one goes upstairs to alert his companions to possible trouble.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Table and Bench**: A flagon of vinegary wine, two cups and a bunch of keys (for the cellar door, and cell door and manacles in location W2) lie atop the table. Flipped over, the table provides half cover.

**Locked Cellar Door:** This locked door wards the cellar.

#### <span id="page-92-0"></span>W2: DUNGEON O F THE BANDIT QUEEN

**Denizens**: This room served Valentin's followers as a prison and well room, and the bandits use it for the same purposes. Currently, two prisoners languish here.

*A wall of iron bars divides this small, dank chamber. Within the cell, a dwarf and a goblin sit manacled to the wall. A well, surrounded by a low wall, pierces the chamber's floor. Nearby lie several buckets attached to damp lengths of rope.* 

The brigands hold two prisoners here:

- **Reithic Yurgirn** (LN male dwarf) lusts for revenge against the brigands. He is a trader of dwarven weapons and armour, and is grateful to adventurers setting him free. Reithic's full stat block and roleplaying notes appear in Appendix 3.
- **Yar** (NE male goblin) speaks only Goblin and has been savagely beaten by the brigands who want information about the Blood Moon's lair. Yar's full stat block and roleplaying notes appear in Appendix 3.

When the characters enter the chamber, Reithic immediately calls out, asking to be released. Yar says nothing, sullenly observing intruders. The two are unhappy cell mates and spend much of their time insulting and threatening each other.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Illumination**: Darkness fills the chamber.

**Well**: A crumbling 2 ft. high stone wall encircles the 20 ft. deep well. If a character sits or leans on the wall, it collapses; the character falls into the well and suffers 2d6 bludgeoning damage (DC 10 Dexterity saving throw negates the fall and damage). The well's rough-hewn walls (DC 15 Strength [Athletics] check scales) descend to a shallow stream flowing to the southwest (eventually intersecting location M2). The bandits (and goblins) are unaware of this connection.

**Cell**: Iron bars (AC 19, hp 18, DC 25 Strength check bends) pierced by a locked iron bar door (DC 15 Dexterity check made with thieves' tools unlocks) divide the room.

**Manacles**: Manacles (AC 19, hp 15, DC 20 Strength check breaks, DC 20 Dexterity check escapes or DC 15 Dexterity check made with thieves' tools unlocks) affixed to the wall keep Reithic and Yar apart.

#### W3: HALLWAY

If the bandits in W1 have alerted their comrades, the warriors from W5 make their stand here, hurling rubble and stones at intruders daring the stairs.

*A barrel full of rubble stands by the stairs. Several doors lead away from this hallway. The spiral staircase continues upwards.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Barrel of Rubble**: Alerted bandits throw these rocks down the stairs at intruders. A character struck by a rock suffers 1d6 bludgeoning damage (DC 15 Dexterity save negates) as it tumbles down the stairs.

#### W4: KITCHEN

**Denizen**: An army deserter, **Bareli**, serves as the gang's cook. Bareli is a skilled soldier, and Cullen and Firean see her as a threat to their leadership; thus, they keep her here, trapped in drudgery.

**Door**: The kitchen door is shut but not locked. The smell of cooking emanates from behind the door.

*The smell of simmering stew fills the hazy air of this kitchen. A fat half-orc woman clad in food-splattered hide armour stands near a steaming iron cauldron.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Smoke**: A haze of smoke hangs in the air.

**Cauldron**: A large cast iron cauldron (containing simmering stew) hangs over a small fire. A character can kick over the cauldron with a DC 10 Strength check. The stew creates a 15 ft. cone of slippery floor. Characters within the cone suffer 1 fire damage from the scalding stew. Characters moving through the area must make a DC 10 Dexterity (Acrobatics) check or stop in the first stew-filled square they enter. A character failing the check by 5 or more falls prone.

**Boxes and Sacks**: The boxes and sacks contain basic foodstuffs—flour, hardtack biscuits, salted meats and so on.

**Barrels**: Two barrels (one half full) contain thin, watery wine (each worth 10 gp full). A third barrel contains 20 pints of lamp oil.

![](_page_92_Picture_27.jpeg)

#### <span id="page-93-0"></span>W5: BARRACKS

**Denizens**: Herein dwell the gang's rank and file. Normally, during the day, four **brigands** rest here. At night, off-duty brigands slumber here.

*This plain, unassuming chamber houses eight two-tier bunks.* 

**Diplomacy**: Unless the party has made a lot of noise fighting the bandits on the lower level, violence does not have to immediately ensue when they reach this chamber. A successful Charisma (Deception) or (Persuasion) check averts bloodshed, but the brigands send one of their number to fetch Cullen and Firean. The bandits are unfriendly and suspicious but assume the characters are meant to be here. If the characters render the bandits friendly, they win their trust and can learn the band's composition, brief details of Cullen and Firean and so on.

**Fighting**: Brigands fighting in this chamber are cornered and fight desperately. The bandits use the bunk beds as cover and unleash a barrage of crossbow bolts at anyone entering the chamber. If a chance to escape presents itself, a bandit takes it rushing out of the room and down the spiral staircase or out onto the battlements.

• **Bunk Beds as Weapons**: Characters may push over bunk beds (DC 15 Strength succeeds) onto their enemies, who are knocked prone and restrained unless they dodge out of the way (DC 10 Dexterity saving throw succeeds). A fallen bunkbed counts as difficult terrain.

![](_page_93_Picture_6.jpeg)

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Illumination**: A lantern hanging from a hook on the ceiling lights this room. Sometimes, during the day, the brigands open the door leading to the battlements to let in light and fresh air.

**Bunk Beds**: Eight two-tier bunk beds stand against the walls. Some are obviously unused. Two small unlocked chests sit under each bunk bed. These contain the bandits' personal possessions, such as spare clothes and mundane equipment (flint and steel, spare pouches, and other odds and ends). A careful search may uncover items of note:

- **Chest 1**: A DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check reveals a small opaque mottled deep blue stone (an azurite worth 10 gp) hidden in an empty wineskin.
- **Chest 3**: A DC 5 Wisdom (Perception) check discovers a dark blue fur-lined cloak (worth 25 gp) carefully folded at the bottom of the chest.
- **Chest 4**: A DC 10 Wisdom (Perception) check uncovers a silver belt buckle (10 gp worth).
- **Chest 8**: A DC 20 Wisdom (Perception) check reveals a selection of ladies' silk under-things (worth 5 gp) stuffed into a pair of old boots.

**Iron-Bound External Door**: A sturdy barred iron-bound door (AC 17, hp 30, damage threshold 5, immune to poison and psychic damage, DC 25 Strength check opens when barred) provides access to the battlements.

# W6: CULLEN' S CHAMBER

**Denizens**: Firean's lieutenant, **Cullen Asikka**, dwells here with his beloved wolfhound, **Fang**.

**Door**: The door is shut but not locked.

*The musty smell of wet dog fills this small bedchamber. A bed stands against one wall; at its foot lies a pile of wet and muddy cloaks. A chest stands against the opposite wall.* 

Cullen is here if the characters have affected a relatively quiet approach to this floor. The craven rogue investigates any sounds of battle in the tower, and if all seems lost, he retreats to his chamber, barricades the door (DC 20 Strength check forces open), and gathers his treasures before tying a rope to his bed. He lowers his beloved Fang to the ground before fleeing.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Illumination**: Windows allow light into the chamber during the day. At night, a lantern provides illumination.

**Bed**: This large bed is comfortably appointed.

**Locked Chest**: This chest (AC 15, hp 18, DC 15 Dexterity check using thieves' tools unlocks) contains spare clothes and other mundane equipment as well as a small sack containing 327 cp, 39 sp and 33 gp.

#### <span id="page-94-0"></span>W7: CHAMBER O F THE BANDIT QUEEN

**Denizens**: This is **Firean Maiethil's** chamber, but she is unlikely to be encountered here as she vigorously conducts the tower's defence on the lower levels. If the characters defeat the bandits on the lower levels, Firean retreats to the tower roof with any survivors to make a last stand.

*This chamber feels lived in. A few papers lie scattered on a desk against one wall, while an unmade bed stands against another. Clothes are scattered on the floor and across a bearskin rug.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Illumination**: A window allows light into the chamber during the day. At night, a lantern provides illumination.

**Bed**: This large bed is comfortably appointed.

**Table and Chair**: A few sheets of scattered paper and an inkpot and quill stand on the table.

**Bearskin Rug**: This worn bearskin rug smells musty. A character making a DC 20 Wisdom (Perception) check finds a small gold ring (worth 50 gp) hidden deep in the bear's mouth. The rug is worthless.

**Unlocked Chest**: This chest contains Firean's spare clothes and mundane equipment along with a scrap of parchment (Player Handout 3), which shows the location of the fallen dwarven hold of Vongyth (see "Further Adventures" and below for more details).

**Locked Chest**: The chest (DC 15 Dexterity check using thieves' tools opens) contains 430 cp, 126 sp and 32 gp as well as a set of silver cutlery (worth 50 gp), a *spell scroll of speak with animals* and a *spell scroll of chill touch*.

#### W8: TOWER ROOF

**Denizens**: During the day, two **brigands** keep watch from the keep's roof. At night, the tower is deserted except when the brigands expect trouble. Normally, the guards posted here are lazy and inattentive.

*The tower's battlemented roof is empty but for a battered flagpole.* 

The roof provides a marvellous view of the surrounding area and the ruined donjon.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

The tower is 40 ft. high. Characters falling from its roof suffer 4d6 bludgeoning damage.

**Flagpole**: This flagpole is 15 ft. high. Characters can stand in the same square as the flagpole, and it provides half cover.

**Rubble**: The bandits have stored rubble here to hurl down upon attackers' heads. Squares containing rubble cost 2 squares of movement to enter. Small pieces of rubble deal 1d6 damage, while larger pieces deal 2d6 damage on a hit.

**Crenelations**: The tower's battlements provide cover against attacks from below.

![](_page_94_Picture_19.jpeg)

# <span id="page-95-0"></span>TH E RUINED D ONJON

Much fought over and looted, the Shadowed Keep's donjon stands all but empty and abandoned. Vermin claim much of the place as their own. No one has explored the upper level for months because two **giant spiders** lair in the donjon's great hall.

The Blood Moon goblins occasionally poke about some of the unoccupied chambers in search of lost treasures, but the tribe has learnt to avoid the donjon's most dangerous occupants.

#### ARCHITECTURE & ENVIRONMENT

The donjon has the following general features:

**Ceilings**: The ceilings in the donjon are 12 ft. high.

**Illumination**: Darkness and shadow shrouds much of the ruined donjon.

- **Ground Floor**: During the day, areas on the ground floor with high, narrow windows or arrow slits are illuminated with dim light. Other areas are in darkness.
- **First Floor**: Most rooms on the first-floor benefit from at least one window and are flooded with bright light during the day. Windows provide half cover.

**Floor**: Rotting and splintered furniture, trash from previous explorations and so on litter some of the floor on both levels of the donjon. Treat such areas as difficult terrain.

- **Ground Floor**: The ground floor comprises flagstones.
- **First Floor**: The tower's first floor has wooden floorboards that creak when walked upon. The floorboards impose disadvantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to move quietly across such areas.

**External Walls**: Although of solid construction, the donjon's outer walls have begun to deteriorate. Mortar between the great stone blocks has begun to flake away. A character can scale the walls with DC 20 Strength (Athletics) checks.

**Arrow Slits**: Arrow slits provide three-quarters cover and only enable dim light to filter into the donjon's interior. Small-sized characters can squeeze through an arrow slit with a DC 15 Dexterity check. Medium-sized creatures must make a DC 20 Dexterity check to squeeze through an arrow slit. (Note, however, it may be impossible for armour-clad or particularly bulky characters to gain access to the keep in such a fashion).

**Spiral Staircase**: A staircase (which counts as difficult terrain) links the tower's above-ground levels. Combatants on the stairs gain half cover against attacks originating from below.

**Wooden Doors**: Unlocked wooden doors (AC 15, hp 20, immune to poison and psychic damage) ward most rooms. Doors open into the room they serve.

# RANDOM ENCOUNTERS

The characters have a 1 in 10 chance of a random encounter for every 10 minutes they remain on the ground floor. No random encounters occur on the upper floor (locations D11- D13) or in the lost treasure vault (locations D14 - D16). Each random encounter occurs only once. If the creatures are defeated, remove them from the relevant encounter area.

#### **D20 LOCATION ENCOUNTER**

| 16    | —  | Wolf (1)                                                                 |
