#### DONJON KE Y

- **D1 Guard Chamber**: Nothing but trash and detritus lies in this central chamber.
- **D2 Sergeants' Chamber**: A small colony of **giant rats** dwell in this oft-looted chamber.
- **D3 Personal Chambers**: Hidden and lost treasure yet lie in these abandoned chambers, awaiting discovery.
- **D4 Stair of the Blood Moon**: A crudely hidden fire trap wards the entrance to the Blood Moon's domain.
- **D5 Abandoned Armoury**: This room is empty and oft-looted.
- **D6 Lair of the Vipers**: A **monstrous viper** dwells here with her young.
- **D7 Kitchen**: This ruined chamber holds little of interest.
- **D8 Pantry**: Green and brown mould, along with a small mushroom colony, grows upon the floor of this small chamber.
- **D9 Buttery**: The skeleton of one of the keep's defenders and a small amount of treasure await discovery here.
- **D10 Great Hall**: Two **giant spiders** claim this sealed chamber.
- **D11 Einar's Bedchambe**r: The ghost of Valentin's slain son, **Einar Ironwolf**, lingers here.
- **D12 Bedchamber**: Kaarina Ironwolf's skeletal remains lie among the ruins of the couple's bedchamber.
- **D13 Audience Chamber**: Here, Valentin plotted and planned against his enemies.
- **D14 Secret Stair**: These cunningly hidden secret stairs tunnel deep into the hill beneath the keep.
- **D15 The Demonic Door**: Warded by a cunning trap and a bound **fire elemental,** this door protects the Ironwolf's treasure vault.
- **D16 Treasure Vault of the Ironwolf**: Here lies the Ironwolf's remaining wealth, guarded by a **necrophidius**.

# <span id="page-97-0"></span>DONJON DRESSING

Use this table to generate minor points of interest, as desired. Such features have little or no impact on play but serve to underscore the current state of the donjon.

# **D20 DRESSING**

- <sup>1</sup> The bones of a small animal (a rat, rabbit or similar) lie crushed on the ground.
- 2 A pile of leaves and other detritus covers the floor.
- <sup>3</sup> One or more old skeletons lie where they fell in battle, surrounding by mouldering, worthless equipment.
- 4 An old, dried spray of blood splatters on one wall.
- 5 Thick spider webs obscure the ceiling.
- <sup>6</sup> A smear of charcoal on one wall shows where someone extinguished a torch.
- 7 A shattered arrow lies on the ground.
  - Crudely drawn pictures—depicting battle and slaughter—
- 8 are daubed over one wall. They show small, goblin-like creatures killing humans.
- 9 The word "Danger" is scratched onto a wall in Common.
- 10 An empty potion vial lies hidden, under some debris.
- <sup>11</sup> Faint tracks on the floor (DC 20 Wisdom [Survival] check spots) hint at what lurks in a nearby chamber.
- 12 Scrapes and scratches—weapon strikes—scar a wall.
- <sup>13</sup> Gossamer wisps of spiderwebs, moving gently in the breeze, hang from the ceiling.
- <sup>14</sup> A damp patch mars a wall. The smell of damp mould pervades the area.
- <sup>15</sup> A small stand of mushrooms grow amid a pool of faint light filtering in from outside.
- <sup>16</sup> The remains of a rotting backpack lie on the floor. A rent in the pack shows where the owner was brutally stabbed.
- 17 The words, "Here fell Conrah" are scratched into the floor.
- <sup>18</sup> A faded bloody handprint decorates one wall. The print is small—around the size of a human child's (or a goblin's).
- 19 A rusting, broken crowbar lies amid the trash and detritus.
- 20 Shards of soft, rotten wood litter the floor.

![](_page_97_Picture_24.jpeg)

# D1: GUARD CHAMBER

A stout pair of double doors once warded the donjon.

*A set of low steps leads up to a wide doorway. Stout iron-bound doors once warded access to the donjon. Now, one hangs crazily from one hinge while the other lies upon the steps.* 

Beyond stand the remains of a guard chamber. When the characters enter the chamber, read:

*Beyond the ruined doors lies a disused, leaf-strewn chamber. Two doors and three corridors lead away from the room.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Illumination**: Bright light fills the chamber.

**Graffiti**: Bored guards scratched crude graffiti into the chamber's walls. None is of immediate use to explorers, instead describing the sexual proclivities of certain folk.

# D2: SERGEANTS ' CHAMBER

**Denizens**: Sergeants of the guard once occupied this ruined chamber. Now, six **giant rats** dwell within. The rats have suffered terribly at the hands of the monstrous viper lairing in location D6 and thus are particularly alert.

*This small chamber is mostly empty. Two sagging and rotting beds stand against one wall. A pile of rotting wood and other detritus is piled on and under the beds.* 

The rats do not attack unless someone disturbs their nest. If forced into battle, the rats attack savagely, focusing their attacks on the intruder disturbing their home. They fight to the death but do not pursue intruders from the room.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Dilapidated Beds**: Two beds stand against one wall. Both are sagging and rotten; they collapse if any creature bigger than a halfling stands on them.

**Rat Warren**: The rats live in a filthy warren in and under the room's beds. The bodies of three discoloured dead rats lie in the warren. A DC 15 Wisdom (Medicine) check reveals they were poisoned. A character investigating the corpses who makes a DC 15 Intelligence (Investigation) check discovers puncture marks piercing each body.

**Treasure**: The rats have unknowingly incorporated some treasures into their nest. A character making a Wisdom (Perception) check while searching the warren may discover some small treasures:

- **DC 15**: 15 cp and 12 sp.
- **DC 20**: A soft, black velvet pouch. The pouch needs a good wash but is worth 1 gp.
- **DC 25**: A teardrop-shaped silver earring (worth 5 gp).

#### <span id="page-98-0"></span>D3 (I – I V): PERSONAL CHAMBERS

These chambers once housed important folk. Now, nothing remains but wrack and ruin.

*Dust and rotten, shattered furniture cover the floor.* 

Looters, bandits and Blood Moon goblins have repeatedly searched these chambers; little of value now remains.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Ruined Furniture**: Ruined furniture—rotten and smashed—lies scattered about the chamber.

**Treasure**: A character making a DC 20 Wisdom (Perception) check finds a trinket overlooked by previous explorers.

#### **D20 TREASURE** 1-5 Under a loose flagstone, the character finds a small mouldy pouch containing 7 sp and 1 gp. 6-10 Hidden in an old cloak's folds the character finds an opaque mottled blue gem (an azurite worth 10 gp). 11-15 Wrapped in a mouldering cloth, the character finds a dagger; tiny dark green opaque stones decorate its hilt (malachites; total worth 20 gp). 16-20 Under a slashed mattress riddled with mildew, the character finds a worn quiver holding four *+1 arrows* fletched with jet black feathers.

Each treasure can be found only once.

#### D4: STAIR O F THE BLOOD MOON

This staircase leads to the cellars claimed by the Blood Moon goblins (location M1).

*A fallen door lies across the corridor. Beyond the open doorway, a staircase leads down into darkness. Crude circular symbols daubed in dried blood decorate the wall on either side of the stair.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Exploding Door Trap**: The goblins have set a crude trap in front of the stairs by hiding two vials of alchemist's fire under the door lying across the entrance to the staircase. A character making a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check notices one end of the door is raised as if something rests underneath.

Unless a character specifies they avoid standing on the door when entering the stairway, they set off the crude trap. Characters setting off the trap suffer 2d4 fire damage and catch fire. They suffer another 2d4 fire damage at the start of each of their next turns. Such characters can make a DC 10 Dexterity check to extinguish the flames.

**Blood Moon Symbol**: A character making a DC 15 Intelligence check identifies the symbol as the device of the Blood Moon tribe.

**Staircase**: This staircase descends 20 ft. to the keep's cellars. The stair is oft-travelled by Blood Moon goblins; a DC 15 Wisdom (Survival) check reveals scuffed muddy goblin tracks leading up and down the stair.

**Treasure**: If the characters deactivate the trap, they can recover two vials of alchemist's fire.

#### D5: ABANDONED ARMOURY

This oft-looted chamber was once an armoury.

**Denizens**: A small colony of spiders dwells in this chamber. Characters making a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check see many of the creatures scuttling about. Although the spiders are not numerous enough to form a swarm, paranoid explorers may assume otherwise.

*Dusty, cobweb-shrouded empty racks line this chamber's walls.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Wooden Weapon Racks**: Cobwebs shroud the weapon racks.

#### D6: LAIR O F THE VIPERS

The goblins know of the vipers herein and avoid this chamber.

**Tracks**: A DC 20 Wisdom (Perception) or Wisdom (Survival) check notes the faint marks of a slithering creature in the corridor outside this room.

**Denizens**: A **monstrous viper** lairs here with three **baby vipers**, amid a pile of smashed furniture. The adult snake ignores intruders unless they enter the chamber. If they do so, it slithers forth to protect its young. It attacks the enemy nearest to its nest, repeatedly biting until its foe collapses. The baby vipers hide in the nest and only strike if someone disturbs their lair.

*A large pile of smashed and rotten furniture stands against one wall. The remains of a collapsed chest juts from the mess.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Dust**: A DC 20 Wisdom (Perception) or Wisdom (Survival) check reveals the faint marks of a slithering creature in the dust leading to and from the partially collapsed chest.

**Smashed Furniture**: A mass of broken, rotting wood stands against one wall. Squares containing smashed furniture count as difficult terrain. Snakes within the pile gain three-quarters cover.

**Nest**: A broken chest lies amid the vipers' nest. A character searching the nest must make a Perception check opposed by the young snakes' Dexterity (Stealth) c h e c k . I f t h e character fails to spot the snakes, they attack with surprise. If the character spots the snakes and retreats, they do not strike.

#### <span id="page-99-0"></span>D7: KITCHEN

During the keep's fall, those who worked here rushed to the Great Hall to aid in its defence (and died there).

*This area was obviously once a kitchen. A large soot-stained fireplace dominates one wall. Toppled tables surrounded by shattered crockery and rusting utensils lie about the room.* 

Like most of the donjon, this area has been thoroughly looted.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Toppled Tables**: Three toppled tables lie on the floor, surrounded by a mass of broken pottery and rusting utensils.

**Great Fireplace**: A huge fireplace, its walls blackened with soot, dominates the room.

Characters can scale the chimney to reach the donjon's roof (DC 10 Strength [Athletics] check succeeds). However, birds now nest in the chimney's upper reaches, and characters climbing the chimney startle them. A character startling the birds must make a DC 10 Dexterity saving throw or slip 10 feet down the chimney (taking 1d6 bludgeoning damage) before catching themselves. Characters climbing the chimney get covered in old soot and pungent bird excrement.

# D8: PANTRY

This storeroom once held the fortresses' food supplies.

*Sagging shelves starting at waist height and reaching almost to the ceiling line this chamber's walls. Dust, cobwebs, and rotting food cover the shelves. Patches of green and brown mould, as well as small stands of mushrooms, cover the floor.* 

This chamber has been comprehensively looted.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Smell**: The faint stench of rotten food pervades the room.

**Mushrooms & Mould**: Green and brown mould and mushrooms cover the walls and shelves of this chamber; a DC 15 Intelligence (Nature) check reveals they are harmless.

#### D9: BUTTERY

This storeroom held the fortress's supply of beer and wine.

**Door**: The door leading to this chamber has been hacked and battered down. Its rotten shards lie in the doorway.

*Smashed and broken barrels lie about the floor. Amid the shattered wood lie the skeletal remains of a humanoid.* 

During the keep's fall, one of the defenders locked himself in the buttery. While he survived longer than his brethren, eventually, the goblins and orcs battered down the door and killed him.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Smell**: The barely detectable odour of stale beer lingers in the air. **Skeleton**: The skeleton of a man-sized humanoid lies on the floor, surrounded by mouldering equipment. A DC 10 Wisdom (Medicine) check reveals the remains are of a human who died from a heavy blow to the head. The skeleton still wears rotting leather armour, but its weapon is missing. A character making a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check discovers a small hidden pocket sewn into the leather armour containing 5 sp and 18 cp.

**Wooden Butts**: These large empty butts once held beer. The slight smell of hops and barley lingers in the air.

**Small Barrels**: These split and broken small barrels held wine. **Loose Stone**: A character making a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check spots a loose flagstone. Below lies a small cavity containing a dusty bottle of brandy (worth 10 gp).

#### D10: TH E GREAT HALL

The Great Hall was the heart of the keep. Here were held revels and feasts to celebrate the Ironwolves' many victories.

**Denizens**: Claimed by a mated pair of **giant spiders**, the Great Hall is a charnel house strewn with bones. After discovering the spiders within, the Blood Moon goblins secured the doors by wrapping chains around their handles.

**Stout Chained Double Doors**: Stout, iron-banded double doors (AC 17, hp 30, damage threshold 8, immune to poison and psychic damage, DC 20 Strength check opens when chained) bar access to the Great Hall. A chain is wrapped around the doors' handles. If the characters are not trying to be stealthy when removing the chain, the spiders automatically hear them.

*Dust and cobwebs shroud this large chamber. Long feasting tables fill the main part of the room, and at the far end stands a dais with another table atop. Shadows wreath the high, web-shrouded ceiling. Bones and rusting equipment cover the floor.* 

When the characters enter the chamber, the spiders lurk in their web. Characters whose passive Perception score beats the spiders' Dexterity (Stealth) check (+7 modifier) notice the lurking danger. If the characters do not notice the spiders, the fell beasts strike when intruders reach the hall's midpoint.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

Ceiling: The ceiling is 20 ft. high. Thick six-inch wooden beams set in a "V" shape hold aloft the upper floor. A great mass of cobwebs obscure the beams. Burning the webs away (AC 10, hp 15, vulnerability to fire, immune to bludgeoning, piercing and psychic damage) fills the hall with smoke for 1d6 x 10 minutes. Creatures in the burning web suffer 2d4 fire damage. Burning the web causes the bodies within to plummet to the floor.

A character can traverse a beam with DC 15 Dexterity (Acrobatics) checks. Characters failing this check by 5 or more fall, but can attempt a DC 20 Dexterity saving throw to grab the beam. Falling characters plummet to the ground and take 2d6 bludgeoning damage. A character on the rafters can make its way to the six web-shrouded corpses.

**Chandeliers**: Two wrought iron chandeliers hang from the ceiling on thick iron chains. Wreathed in dust and webs, the chandeliers can be raised and lowered using chains. A character must spend an action to lower a chandelier. The chains are strong enough to hold up to 150 lbs. of additional weight. Characters raised on a chandelier can reach the rafters.

**Spiders' Web**: A great mass of webs covers the ceiling and serves as the spiders' lair. A creature entering a webbed area for the first time on a turn or starting its turn in such an area must make a DC 12 Dexterity saving throw or be restrained. Restrained characters can spend an action and make a DC 12 Strength (Athletics) check or Dexterity (Acrobatics) check to escape.

A character making a DC 10 Wisdom (Perception) check notices several humanoid shapes wrapped within the webs.

- **Goblins (4)**: These partially eaten goblins have no treasure.
- **Human Bandit**: Dead but uneaten, this bandit has 1 gp and 14 sp in a worn belt pouch. He wears studded leather armour and has a longsword.
- **Elf**: This elf wears leather armour and carried two daggers. His pouch contains a vial of antitoxin and a set of thieves' tools. (If the body falls to the floor, the vial shatters.)

**Dais**: A two-foot-high dais stands at one end of the chamber. Here, Valentin, his family and favoured retainers feasted. The dais's shallow steps do not impede movement.

**Great Tables**: A character can jump atop a table with a DC 12 Dexterity (Acrobatics) check or clamber up by spending an extra five feet of movement. Characters under a table gain threequarters cover against attack from above.

**Bones**: When the donjon fell, the defenders made their final stand here. The bones and rusting equipment of the slain litter the floor. The floor is difficult terrain.

**Lost Treasures**: Characters searching the Great Hall and making a Wisdom (Perception) check may uncover a few small treasures amid the bones of the fallen:

- **DC 5**: One of the human skeletons was obviously the focus of many attacks; its skull has been cleaved several times by cutting weapons, and several other bones are broken. (These are Valentin Ironwolf's remains.)
- **DC 10**: Every minute of searching uncovers 1d4 gp worth of mixed coinage. Characters spending more than ten minutes searching find no more coins.
- **DC 15**: A bone scroll tube stoppered by black, smoothed river stones. Investigation reveals the scroll tube to be watertight. The tube contains a *spell scroll of identify*.

**Faded Tapestries**: Faded, cobweb-draped tapestries showing scenes of battle and slaughter cover the walls. Characters can scale a tapestry with DC 10 Strength (Athletics) checks; however, a tapestry only supports 130 lbs. of weight. Heavier characters rip the tapestry from the wall once they have climbed 10 ft.; such climbers suffer 1d6 bludgeoning damage and land prone.

**Wooden Door**: An unlocked wooden door provides access to a dusty spiral staircase leading to the keep's upper levels.

![](_page_100_Picture_14.jpeg)

# <span id="page-101-0"></span>D11: EINAR' S BEDCHAMBER

This chamber belonged to Einar Ironwolf, Valentin's young son.

**Door**: The door to this chamber stands slightly open. As they approach, characters with a passive Perception score of 11 or more hear sobbing coming from this chamber.

**Denizen**: During the keep's fall, **Einar Ironwolf** was slain here, but his spirit lingers on, unable to find rest until he is laid to rest with his parents. He is not immediately hostile to intruders, but if they attack him, he fights back. He cannot leave the chamber.

*Dust shrouds this obviously looted bedchamber. The small skeleton of a child lies sprawled among the ruin. Above the skeleton hovers the translucent figure of a young boy, his spectral face streaked with tears.* 

If the characters attack Einar, he screams loudly and rushes at them, using his withering touch to slay his tormentors. Consumed by the sorrow and horror of his fate, he fights until destroyed.

#### SPEAKING WITH THE DEAD

A homely, shy child in life with a love of knowledge, Einar is now wracked by grief; nearly driven insane by the terror and pain of his last few minutes among the living, he craves to rest alongside his parents. To simulate his state of mind, treat him as hostile toward the characters (but he does not attack without provocation).

**Goal**: Einar wants his bones and those of his parents to be laid to rest together. He senses the necrotic taint in the undercrypt and does not want to be buried there. Valentin's bones lie in the Great Hall (D10), while his mother's lie in her bedchamber (D12).

**Reward**: If the characters agree to Einar's request, he tells them his father hid his treasure behind a secret door (D16). He does not know exactly where the door is, but he knows from overhearing his parents speak of it that it lies somewhere on this floor. He also tells them his father often boasted of the terrible guardians watching over his treasure.

If the characters lay the family's bones to rest together, award them each 50 XP.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Bed**: The moulding sheets and mattress have been viciously slashed. A large dried bloodstain covers much of the bed.

**Skeleton**: The skeleton is of a young human child of about ten years old. A DC 10 Wisdom (Medicine) check reveals deep gashes in his vertebrae that suggest someone sawed at his throat with a jagged blade.

#### D12: BEDCHAMBER

This was Valentin's and Kaarina's bedchamber. Refer to D14 for details of the secret trapdoor set in the floor against the east wall.

*What was once an opulent bedchamber is now a shattered wreck. Dust lies thickly, and scorched, broken furniture is scattered about. A skeleton lies on the bed, and several more blackened skeletons lie by the door.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Skeleton**: The skeleton on the bed is Kaarina's. On the night the keep fell, Kaarina fought by her husband's side until he was struck down. She fled here to gather her possessions and son, but before she could reach Einar (D11) she was cornered and killed.

A DC 10 Wisdom (Medicine) check reveals the skeleton on the bed to be of a human female killed by a caved-in skull. She wears mouldering, blood-spattered clothes that were once high quality.

**Blackened Skeletons**: A character examining the blackened and scorched skeletons by the door making a DC 10 Intelligence (Investigation) check identifies them as two goblins and an orc.

**Secret Trapdoor**: A character making a DC 25 Wisdom (Perception) check spots this extremely well-hidden secret trapdoor. If Einar has told the characters of the secret door's existence, the characters have advantage on checks made to find the door.

#### D13: AUDIENCE CHAMBER

Here, Valentin met privately with trusted henchmen and close friends and plotted his conquest of the surrounding area.

*A large table and six chairs dominate this chamber. Against another wall stands a dusty desk, its drawers pulled out and smashed on the floor. Mouldering paper surrounds the desk.* 

This area has been looted, but not as comprehensively as other parts of the keep, and a few treasures remain. Additionally,

> this chamber makes an excellent place to rest as the large table can be used to barricade the chamber's door.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Large Table**: A character searching around the table who makes a DC 20 Wisdom (Perception) check discovers a secret compartment in one of its stout legs. Within lies a plain, wickedly sharp dagger in a leather sheath. Silver wire cunningly sewn into

the sheath depicts the Ironwolf family crest. The dagger and sheath are worth 5 gp.

**Loose Floorboard**: A character searching the desk who makes a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check discovers a loose floorboard beneath the desk. A small niche under the floorboard holds a mouldering, spider-web coated pouch containing 25 gp.

![](_page_102_Picture_0.jpeg)

# <span id="page-103-0"></span>L OST TREASURES O F THE IRONWOLVES

Valentin Ironwolf dug this small sub-level to hold his wealth. Only Valentin and his wife knew of the sub-level's entrance, and thus, after the Shadowed Keep's fall, it remained undisturbed.

#### ARCHITECTURE & ENVIRONMENT

The sub-level has the following general features:

**Illumination**: Darkness.

**Ceilings**: The ceilings are eight feet high.

**Flagstone Floor**: The floor's flagstones have started to shift and move under time's remorseless influence, but generally they do not inhibit movement.

**Stone Walls**: The walls are of dressed stone (DC 20 Strength [Athletics] check scales) in fair condition.

# D14: SECRET STAIR

This secret spiral staircase leads to location D15.

*A three-foot wide stair spirals downwards into darkness. Thick dust cloaks the floor, and dusty curtains of thin spider webs hang from the low ceiling.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Ceiling**: Beyond the secret door, the ceiling is barely six feet. high. **Spiral Staircase**: A steep, three-foot-wide staircase spirals downwards to Valentin's secret treasure vault. The stairs are difficult terrain. Combatants on the stairs gain half cover against attacks originating from lower down the stairs.

**Thick Dust**: Thick dust lies on the stairs. A character making a DC 10 Wisdom (Survival) check can confirm that nothing has come this way in decades.

#### D15: TH E DEMONIC DOOR

No one has entered the corridor since the keep's fall

**Trap**: Several traps ward the Demonic Door. A hidden portcullis in the ceiling lurks at the bottom of the stairs (see "Portcullis Trap") while a magical fire trap and a **fire elemental lesser guardian** wait in the carven demon mouth (see "Demon Breath Trap").

*Flickering torchlight fills a corridor at the bottom of the narrow stairway. A stout wooden door flanked by brightly burning torches bars further progress. Above the door, a horrible carving of a demon's face leers down at you.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Illumination**: Two torches, each treated with a *continual flame,* fill the corridor with bright light.

**Ceiling**: The arched ceiling is seven feet high above the centre of the corridor.

**Demon Face Carving**: Intricately carved, the demon face above the door represents no commonly known demon or devil (DC 15 Intelligence [Arcana] check confirms). The mouth is hollow.

- **Lever**: A character making a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check notices a small raised piece of rock (a lever) at the back of the demon's throat. Moving the lever raises or lowers the portcullis (as appropriate). Once the stone is pressed, the mouth springs shut (+6 to hit, one target, 11 [2d10] bludgeoning damage and the target is restrained). The mouth stays shut for one minute before opening. A restrained character can free their hand with a DC 15 Strength check.
- **Tiny Runes**: A character making a DC 20 Wisdom (Perception) check while searching the demon carving notices tiny runes engraved into the demon's tongue. A DC 15 Intelligence (Arcana) check reveals the runes deal with fire and flame. See "Demon Breath Trap" for more details.

**Wooden Door**: An average lock (DC 15 Dexterity check made with thieves' tools opens) protects this stout (AC 15, hp 20, immune to poison and psychic damage) door. Valentin held the only key, but it is now long lost.

#### **P ORTCULLIS TRAP**

**Trigger**: A creature standing on the hidden pressure plate in front of the Demonic Door triggers the portcullis trap.

**Spotting the Trap**: A character making a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check spots the pressure plate in front of the door or the disguised bottom of the portcullis (depending on where they search).

**Disabling the Trap**: A DC 15 Dexterity check made using thieves' tools disables the pressure plate. A check result of DC 10 or lower sets off the trap. Alternatively, the characters can lift the portcullis (DC 25 Strength check succeeds) or destroy it (AC 19, hp 50, damage threshold 8, immune to fire, poison and psychic damage).

**Effect**: The iron portcullis hidden in the ceiling at the bottom of the stairs drops down. Characters under the portcullis suffer 11 (2d10) bludgeoning damage and are restrained (DC 15 Strength check ends). A DC 15 Dexterity saving throw halves this damage and negates the restrained effect; characters making the saving throw can choose to jump forward or backward out of the portcullis's way.

#### **DEMON BREATH TRAP**

**Trigger**: A creature opening the Demonic Door triggers the trap. See "Demon's Breath" and "The Guardian Appears" below.

**Spotting the Trap**: A DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check reveals the faint glimmer of flame at the back of the demon's mouth. See also "Tiny Runes" under "Demon Face Carving".

**Disabling the Trap**: A character making a DC 15 Intelligence (Arcana) check removes the magic lurking in the demon's mouth by effacing some of the runes carved onto its tongue. A successful *dispel magic* (DC 13 ability check using the character's spellcasting ability) cast on the demon face carving destroys the trap. Smashing the carving also destroys the trap.

**Demon's Breath**: Flames burst from the demon's mouth, filling the 15-foot of corridor in front of the door. Creatures in the corridor suffer 11 (2d10) fire damage (DC 15 Dexterity save halves). The trap resets after one minute.

<span id="page-104-0"></span>**The Guardian Appears**: One round after the Demon's Breath effect, the faint flicker of flame appears in the carven demon's mouth. The next round, a **fire elemental lesser guardian**  forms in the mouth and issues forth to slay intruders.

#### D16: TREASURE VAULT O F THE IRONWOLVES

Here, Valentin stored his (sadly depleted) wealth. This area was not looted during the keep's fall and has lain undisturbed since then.

**Denizen**: Valentin was more than a little paranoid, and thus he expended a good portion of his loot commissioning a deathless, incorruptible guard—a **necrophidius**. The necrophidius attacks anyone who does not display the Ironwolf sigil.

*This dusty chamber has a low ceiling, and several chest-filled niches pierce the walls. A sinuous snake skeleton topped with a fanged human skull rises gracefully from the floor at your arrival.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Ceiling**: The ceiling is eight feet high.

**Stone Niches**: Stone niches pierce the chamber's walls. Each is about a five-foot square and holds an (unlocked) chest.

**Treasure**: The Ironwolves' remaining treasures fill several of the chests in this room. The treasure comprises:

- **Mixed Coinage**: 1,287 cp, 427 sp and 78 gp in five small sacks.
- **Fine Longsword**: This finely balanced weapon has the Ironwolf crest carved into its oval-shaped pommel and rests in a plain, dusty leather scabbard.
- **Shield**: This iron shield has a raised black boss wrought in the shape of a snarling wolf's head—the Ironwolf family crest.
- *Potion of Greater Healing*: This small iron vial holds a red liquid. Shaking the vial makes the red liquid glimmer.
- *Driftglobe*: A soft black velvet pouch holds a small sphere of thick glass. Red thread stitching on the bag spells out the word, "Sitheran". This is the *driftglobe's* command word.
- **Gems**: A soft black velvet pouch holds two small opaque orange stones (carnelians worth 50 gp each) and one lustrous white stone (a pearl worth 100 gp).

![](_page_104_Picture_15.jpeg)

# <span id="page-105-0"></span>REALM O F THE BLOOD MOON

The Blood Moon tribe, led by their dread chieftain **Ruknar**, claims the cellars below Ironwolf Keep. Several in the tribe resent Ruknar and secretly plot to overthrow him. Until now, his martial prowess and boundless appetite for barbaric cruelty dissuade all from striking against him. The characters' arrival, however, may be just the opportunity the shaman **Sar** needs to finally strike.

#### ARCHITECTURE & ENVIRONMENT

The dungeon has the following general features:

**Illumination**: Darkness.

**Ceilings**: The ceilings are 8 ft. high.

**Flagstone Floor**: The floor's flagstones have started to shift and move under time's remorseless influence, but generally, they do not inhibit movement.

**Stone Walls**: The walls are of dressed stone (DC 20 Strength [Athletics] check scales) in fair condition. In places, moss and lichens grow on the walls, and water oozes through the mortar.

**Wooden Door**: Doors (AC 15, hp 20, immune to poison and psychic damage) open into the room or space beyond. A locked door can be opened with a DC 15 Dexterity check made by someone using thieves' tools.

# RANDOM ENCOUNTERS

The characters have a 1 in 10 chance of encountering some of the dungeon's denizens for every 10 minutes, they remain below ground. Each encounter can occur only once. If the creatures are defeated, remove them from the relevant encounter area.

| D20   | LOCATION | ENCOUNTER                                         |
|-------|----------|---------------------------------------------------|
| 1-5   | M7       | Blood Moon warriors (3)                           |
| 6-12  | M1       | Blood Moon sniper (1), Blood Moon<br>warriors (2) |
| 13-18 | M7       | Blood Moon noncombatant (4)                       |
| 19    | M8       | Fuzght & Mugut (orc mercenaries)                  |
| 20    | M12      | Razogen, Blood Moon warriors (3)                  |

#### ECOLOGY & SOCIETY

The tribe has many small lairs and outposts scattered throughout the forest. This small band dwells below Ironwolf Keep. They jealously guard their subterranean home and skirmish with the bandits claiming the watchtower. Vicious combatants, the concept of a fair fight is totally lost on the Blood Moon goblins.

The vast majority of the tribe are typical unimaginative and sadistic goblins. A few are of note, however:

- **Razogen (M12)**: Ruknar's young son, Razogen, desperately craves his father's approval and is fanatically loyal to him.
- **Ruknar (M13)**: The tribe's chieftain, this powerful ogre, is a bully and sadist of breath-taking enthusiasm.

• **Sar (M11)**: The tribe's shaman, Sar, incessantly plots against Ruknar and tries to enlist the characters to his cause.

All the stat blocks for the cellar's denizens appear in Appendix 4: Blood Moon Denizens.

# A COORDINATED DEFENCE

Because they skirmish with the bandits of the watchtower, the goblins have a basic plan to combat serious incursions into their lair. When it becomes clear the tribe faces a serious threat, Ruknar emerges from his chambers to lead the defence. Accompanied by his concubines and son, he gathers any nearby warriors and charges to the sound of battle.

If Ruknar falls, the remaining goblins flee the ruins as quickly as possible, taking with them anything of value they can quickly collect. If Razogen survives his father's death, he also flees but swears revenge against his father's killers.

#### CELLAR KE Y

- **M1 Guardroom:** Four **Blood Moon warriors** and two **Blood Moon snipers** occupy this guardroom. All are likely distracted when the characters first assault the cellar.
- **M2 Well Chamber**: This chamber features a well that secretly links to the well in the watchtower's cellar (location W2).
- **M3 Emissaries of the Grinning Skull**: Two visiting **Grinning Skull bugbears** lair here.
- **M4 Storeroom**: The tribe uses this chamber to store their foodstuffs. While they prefer the taste of fresh meat, when their supply of prisoners runs low, they use the food stored here.
- **M5 Armoury**: The Blood Moon store their weapons and armour here. They also store captured mundane equipment here.
- **M6 Cavern-Pit of the Devourer**: A trapped **gelatinous cube** lurks in this natural cavern.
- **M7 Common Room Complex**: This network of chambers—once a series of small cells and associated chambers—serves as the tribe's common room and private living area.
- **M8 Orc Mercenaries**: Two **orc mercenaries**, Fuzght and Mugut, dwell here. They serve as the tribe's shock troops and venture forth on important raids or to repulse dangerous intruders.
- **M9 Guardroom**: Three **Blood Moon warriors** and one **Blood Moon bruiser** guard this room (which also doubles as a torture chamber).
- **M10 Prisoners of the Blood Moon**: The tribe uses this unfinished part of the keep's cellars as a prison.
- **M11 Shaman of the Blood Moon**: These chambers serve as the Blood Moon's fane.
- **M11a Sar's Personal Chamber**: Here dwells **Sar**—Blood Moon shaman, and want-to-be chief.
- **M12 Guardians of the Blood Moon**: **Razogen** has been honoured with the task of defending the approach to his father's inner sanctum. He watches here with three **Blood Moon bruisers**.
- **M13 Chieftain of the Blood Moon**: **Ruknar** dwells here with his large and aggressive trio of **Blood Moon concubines**.

![](_page_106_Figure_0.jpeg)

# <span id="page-107-0"></span>DUNGEON DRESSING

Use this table, to generate minor points of interest. Such features serve to underscore the cellar's current state.

# **D20 DRESSING**

| 1  | A partially gnawed rat corpse lies on the floor.                                                              |
|----|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 2  | Crude graffiti in blood covers the wall; it comprises<br>curses and suchlike in Goblin.                       |
| 3  | Water oozes through the wall to form a small puddle.                                                          |
| 4  | Gnawed bones lie on the floor.                                                                                |
| 5  | Guttural laughter or brief conversation (in Goblin)<br>reaches the characters' ears from some far-off locale. |
| 6  | Broken and slashed equipment—backpack, pouch, hilt<br>of a dagger and so on—are scattered on the floor.       |
| 7  | The rancid stench akin to that of a wet, flatulent dog<br>fills in the air.                                   |
| 8  | A small puddle of green, foul smelling liquid.                                                                |
| 9  | Deep scratches mar a wall (possibly caused by a<br>powerful warrior striking it with a bladed weapon).        |
| 10 | A small patch of slightly phosphorescent fungus<br>grows on the ceiling. A musty smell hangs in the air.      |
| 11 | Crude graffiti depicts small stick figures stabbing<br>bigger stick figures.                                  |
| 12 | Water drips from a crack in the ceiling.                                                                      |
| 13 | A rotten backpack holds three rusty iron spikes.                                                              |
| 14 | Dried blood splatters decorate the floor.                                                                     |
| 15 | A minor collapse has created a hollow in one wall.                                                            |
| 16 | Muddy scrape marks on the floor show where a chest<br>or something similar was dragged along.                 |
| 17 | A broken arrow lies on the floor.                                                                             |
| 18 | The heady stench of goblin sweat fills the air.                                                               |
| 19 | A large gash in the floor shows where something<br>immensely strong hit it with a large, bladed weapon.       |
| 20 | A single gold coin is wedged into a crack in a wall.                                                          |

# M1: GUARDROOM

**Denizens**: Four **Blood Moon warriors** and two **Blood Moon snipers** occupy this guardroom. However, the goblins' vigil has become somewhat lax of late. When the characters first reach this area, the guards argue over a game of chance and are distracted. Intruders automatically hear the argument while on the stairs unless they are distracted. The first time they come here, the characters surprise the guards unless they make an exceptional amount of noise on the stairs or set off the trap in area D4.

*A faint glimmer of light emanates from a small fire smouldering between four slender pillars. Tables and chairs—occupied by a halfdozen filthy humanoids—stand nearby.* 

An injured goblin retreats to warn the tribe of the attack. Once one goblin has fled, the others retreat down the western corridor.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Illumination**: Darkness fills much of the chamber; dim light surrounds the smouldering fire in a 10 ft. radius.

**Ceiling**: The ceiling is 10 ft. high; black soot coats the ceiling above the fire.

**Fire**: A small fire smoulders amid a pile of rubble. Several rats wrapped in leaves slowly cook in the embers.

**Downward Stairs**: The air in this stairway is cold. The stairs lead to location U1.

**Walls**: The walls of this chamber are of dressed stone. Here and there, water oozes down the wall, and mould grows. On the drier patches of wall, goblins have scrapped and drawn lurid graffiti. Many of the scenes depict slaughter and torture.

**Slender Pillars**: Four slender pillars hold the roof aloft. A character in an adjacent square gains half cover. An empty iron torch sconce hangs from each pillar.

**Tables and Benches**: Two long tables and six chairs stand near the fire.

#### M2: WELL CHAMBER

This small chamber's main feature is a well that takes its water directly from the same stream that flows under the bandit's watchtower (see W2). Characters discovering the connection between the two can use this route to assault the goblins' liar.

*A crumbling low wall surrounds what looks to be a well. Two buckets—each attached to a short length of rope—lie nearby.* 

This area is not normally garrisoned. If goblins from location M1 have been forced to retreat here, they use the well's low, crumbling stone wall for cover.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Well**: A crumbling 2 ft. high stone wall encircles this 20 ft. deep well. If a character sits or leans on the wall, it collapses, and the character falls into the well and suffers 2d6 bludgeoning damage (DC 10 Dexterity saving throw negates). The well's rough-hewn walls (DC 15 Strength [Athletics] check scales) descend to a shallow stream. To the southeast lies the well in the dungeons below the watchtower (location W2.) The goblins (and the bandits) are unaware of this connection. See "Further Adventures", for more details on what lies to the northwest.

**Torch Sconces**: Three empty iron torch sconces hang from the chamber's walls.

#### M3: EMISSARIES O F THE GRINNING SKULL

**Denizens**: Ruknar has billeted a visiting pair of **Grinning Skull bugbears** here. The pair make no move to aid the goblins in defending their lair but fight viciously if attacked. If attacked, the bugbears seek to escape at the first opportunity. If the characters initially bypass this area, the emissaries leave to inform their tribe of the attack (and the goblins' likely doom).

*Two piles of sleeping furs lie against one wall; camping gear is strewn nearby.* 

<span id="page-108-0"></span>The Grinning Skull's chieftain has recently proposed an "alliance" between the two groups, which Ruknar is considering. Of course, this is the first stage in the chieftain's plan to conquer the Blood Moon goblins and turn them into little more than slaves and expendable warriors. While the emissaries await Ruknar's response, they linger here.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Camping Gear**: The emissaries' gear—two small piles of furs, the remains of several meals and other odds and ends—lie scattered about the chamber. None of it has appreciable worth.

#### M4: STOREROOM

The tribe uses this chamber to store their foodstuffs. While they prefer the taste of fresh meat, when their supply of prisoners runs low, they use the food stored here.

**Door**: The room's wooden door is swollen (DC 10 Strength check opens) but not locked.

*An untidy tangle of boxes and barrels fills much of this chamber.* 

Goblins are not normally encountered here. If the characters decide to rest in the complex, this area makes an excellent camp as the many boxes and barrels can be used to block the door.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Boxes**: The many boxes here hold looted foodstuffs captured by the tribe during their raids. They contain salted meats, flour, grain and so on and can be looted as rations.

**Barrels**: Three large barrels hold sour, vinegary red wine. One is half-empty.

# M5: ARMOURY

The Blood Moon store their weapons and armour here. They also store captured mundane equipment here.

**Door**: The room's wooden door is swollen (DC 10 Strength check opens) but not locked.

*This small room serves as an armoury. Small-sized suits of leather armour lie heaped in one corner near a pile of haphazardly dumped small shields. Sagging shelves holding a jumbled array of weapons line the walls.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Sagging Shelves**: The shelves sag dangerously. A DC 10 Intelligence (Investigation) check reveals that the shelves could not take a human's weight. However, a light climber could easily scale the shelves without them collapsing.

• **Hidden Treasure**: A small dust-covered pouch lies on the top shelf, hidden behind a rotting rag. A character climbing the shelves who makes a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check spots the pouch. It contains 13 gp and a small tarnished gold ring (worth 25 gp).

**Armour and Shields**: Eleven suits of leather armour sized for goblins—all emblazoned with the tribe's sigil—lie in a pile. Several have gashes in them (in all likelihood, evidence of fatal wounds). A like number of shields—all also emblazoned with the tribe's sigil lie next to the pile.

**Weapons**: Roughly a dozen daggers, morningstars, short swords and shortbows (along with around 200 arrows) lie in glorious disorganisation on the shelves; all are sized for goblins.

**Captured Equipment**: The goblins store captured equipment on the shelves. This includes four morningstars, two longswords, five suits of studded leather armour and two suits of scale mail along with backpacks, belts, pouches and so on. All these items are sized for Medium-sized creatures.

![](_page_108_Picture_21.jpeg)

#### <span id="page-109-0"></span>HIDDEN BOLTHOLE

The goblins have not discovered this room's hidden bolthole.

**Secret Door**: A character making a DC 20 Wisdom (Perception) check finds a secret door behind the pile of leather armour. A loose stone at the wall's base hides its opening mechanism (an easily depressed catch). The door is only 2 ft. high and leads to a long-forgotten hidden bolthole.

This place was designed as a refugee for use in times of peril. During the keep's fall, none of the defenders made it here.

*Cobwebs throng the ceiling of this small, roughly finished chamber. Trackless dust lies thickly on the floor. A small chest stands against one wall next to a pile of mouldering bedrolls. The flickering light of a torch fills the room.* 

#### The niche contains:

- One torch with a *continual flame* cast upon it.
- Four musty bedrolls.
- An empty barrel that one held water.
- An unlocked chest containing rotten and decayed food, oncefine travellers' clothes and the like.

# M6: CAVERN-PI T O F THE DEVOURER

**Denizen**: A trapped **gelatinous cube** lurks in this cavern.

The goblins utilise this sinkhole to dispose of rubbish. Occasionally, Ruknar drags a prisoner or ill-favoured goblin here. The unfortunate is hurled into the cavern below, whereupon the trapped gelatinous cube consumes them. Such events are much anticipated by the tribe, and many come to watch the spectacle.

*This natural cavern is roughly 30-foot wide, 40-foot long and 30 foot deep. Several small passageways—high up in the cavern walls —lead away from the cavern.* 

The gelatinous cube mindlessly patrols the cavern searching for food; it has not realised food often appears from above and thus does not lurk directly beneath the sinkhole. A character making a DC 13 Wisdom (Perception) check notices the cavern floor is completely (and suspiciously) clear of debris.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Depth**: The sinkhole is 30 ft. deep. Characters falling into the sinkhole take 3d6 bludgeoning damage and land prone.

**Ceiling**: The ceiling is of natural stone (DC 25 Strength [Athletics] check scales).

**Walls**: The cavern and sinkhole walls are of natural stone (DC 15 Strength [Athletics] check scales). Several small passageways lead away from this cavern; they are high up on the walls, and the

![](_page_109_Picture_19.jpeg)

<span id="page-110-0"></span>gelatinous cube cannot reach them. See "To Deeper Caverns" below for more details.

**Floor**: The pit's floor is of stone; no mud, sand or other detritus mars its surface. For perceptive characters, the floor provides an important clue as to what lurks within this chamber.

#### TO DEEPER CAVERNS…

The passages leading away from the cavern-pit lead to an extensive network of caverns deep below the Shadowed Keep. See "Further Adventures", for more details.

#### M7: COMMON ROOM COMPLEX

This network of chambers—once a series of small cells and associated chambers—serves as the tribe's common room and private living area.

**Denizens**: Normally, eight **Blood Moon warriors,** two **Blood Moon snipers** and one **Blood Moon bruiser,** along with about a score of females and young (**Blood Moon noncombatants**) congregate in this area. The state of this area depends on whether the characters take the occupants by surprise.

- **Denizens (Surprised)**: If the characters surprise the goblins, the females and young are here cooking, talking, arguing and so on. Characters with a passive Perception score of 10 or more hear the general commotion of the goblins going about their daily lives as they approach. Three **Blood Moon warriors** are also here. When the characters arrive, the noncombatants scatter while the warriors move to defend their home. The other eight goblin combatants arrive on the second round of combat.
- **Denizens (Unsurprised)**: If the characters are expected, no non-combatants linger in the communal eating area; rather, they have all taken shelter in their personal chambers. Instead, all 11 of the room's defenders hide among the tables and unleash a barrage of missiles at the most capable-looking enemy warriors.

*Two large tables and many chairs stand around this chamber. A huge fireplace—complete with a blazing fire and gigantic spit upon which some kind of meat cooks—dominates one wall.* 

The warriors fight hard to protect the tribe's females and young. They prefer to snipe from the corridors or from behind tables, hoping to keep the intruders away from the living areas. Unless

cornered and given no chance to surrender, the young and females do not fight.

![](_page_110_Picture_12.jpeg)

This large area was once a guardroom

f o r t h e a t t e n d a n t cells; now, the g o b l i n s e a t and relax here.

**Illumination**: Normal light fills the room within 30 ft. of the fireplace. Dim light extends for another 30 ft.

**Tables and Chairs**: There are two sturdy wooden tables in this room. Each is 3 ft. high and covered in the foul detritus of the goblins' feasting. Scraps of food and wine stains cover the floor around the tables and benches.

Characters behind or under a table have half cover.

**Fireplace**: A huge fireplace, its stones blackened with soot, pierces one wall. The fireplace features a fiercely burning fire and a huge spit upon which the decapitated corpse of a human cooks.

The fireplace is 15 ft. wide and utilises a natural fissure in the rock that rises directly upwards for 10 ft. before turning west. A character can climb the chimney with DC 10 Strength (Athletics) checks. After another 30 ft., the fissure opens into a small, lowceiling cave; soot covers its walls, floor and ceiling.

#### LIVING QUARTERS

The cells have several noteworthy features:

**Ceiling**: The ceiling is 6 ft. high.

**Doors**: Each small cell has a rusting iron-bound door (AC 17, hp 22, immune to poison and psychic damage). While each has a simple lock (DC 15 Dexterity check made by someone proficient with thieves' tools unlocks), the keys were lost long ago.

**Cells**: Occupied cells serve as a goblin family's home. Mangy blankets, mouldering bracken and rotting grass cover the floor. Mingled with this are the family's pathetic, valueless possessions.

If a character searches a cell and makes a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check, they find something of value. Roll once for each cell searched. Each "treasure" can be found only once; re-roll duplicate treasures.

# <span id="page-111-0"></span>M8: OR C MERCENARIES

**Denizens**: Two **orc mercenaries,** Fuzght and Mugut, dwell here. They serve as the Blood Moon's shock troops, only venturing forth on important raids or to repulse dangerous intruders.

The orcs rest here unless aiding their goblin paymasters. If battle has raged throughout the complex, they are ready for action and lurk, ready to surprise anyone passing or entering their room. If not, they sit at the table drinking cheap, sour wine and arguing about who is better at decapitating enemies. The characters' arrival gives them the perfect opportunity to decide the argument.

*This decent-sized chamber features two large beds, a sturdy chest table and two chairs.* 

Aggressive fighters, the orc's instinct is to take the fight to intruders. Trusting to their prodigious strength and vitality, they strike suddenly, preferably from ambush. If surprised in their quarters, they force their way from the room, using a bench to shove foes into the corridor. They delight in slaughtering their enemies and, if not pressed closely, stop to (gleefully) decapitate fallen foes.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Beds**: Two large, sturdy beds stand against one wall.

**Table**: This sturdy wooden table is 3 ft. high. Characters under or behind it have half cover. Characters under the table automatically spot a key (DC 20 Wisdom [Perception] check otherwise discovers) nailed to the table's underside. The key opens the orcs' chest.

**Locked Chest**: The orcs store their pay, loot and personal possessions in this chest (AC 15, hp 10, immune to poison and psychic damage, DC 15 Dexterity check made by someone using thieves' tools unlocks). Along with their rancid mundane personal possessions, the chest holds 367 cp, 197 sp and 87 gp.

#### M9 GUARDROOM

**Denizens**: Three **Blood Moon warriors** and one **Blood Moon bruiser** guard this room (which also doubles as a torture chamber). Although they are tasked with watching the orc mercenaries (location M8) and the tribe's prisoners (location M10) they are complacent. Thus, unless warned of intruders, the guards have disadvantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks.

**Door**: The door to this chamber is partially open when the characters first reach this area.

*A table and two benches stand in the rough centre of the chamber. A barred, stout door pierces the far wall. Another table holds objects of obvious torture. A rust-coloured stain covers a nearby bench and the surrounding floor.* 

Unless alerted, the guards sit at the table, swapping lies about their raids and kills. If they are aware of approaching intruders, the goblins push over their table (for half cover). When enemies appear, the goblins shoot their bows until forced to melee. When one of the goblins is slain, the survivors retreat to location M10. Once inside, one holds the door using the Dodge action while the other vindictively slaughters the prisoners (starting with the humans).

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Illumination**: It is dark in the chamber, except within 10 ft. of the smouldering brazier; the burning coals therein emit dim light.

**Smell**: A DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check detects the slight stench of burnt flesh in the air (along with the smell of goblin sweat and cheap wine).

**Barred Wooden Door**: A sturdy, barred (but not locked) stout wooden door leads to the tribe's prison (location M10). A large nail driven into the door holds a bunch of keys. There are the keys for the manacles used in the prison beyond the door.

**Smouldering Brazier**: Several irons poke from the smouldering coal-filled wrought iron brazier. Characters can draw a poker from the fire and use it as an improvised weapon that inflicts 1d6 piercing damage and 1 fire damage. A character holding a poker at the end of their turns suffers 1 fire damage.

**Torture Equipment**: A bench against one wall holds several objects of torture—clamps, pokers, pliers and so on.

**Bloodstained Bench**: The goblins strap prisoners prone to this bench before torturing them. Dried blood covers the bench and surrounding flagstones.

#### M10: PRISONERS O F THE BLOOD MOON

The tribe uses this unfinished part of the keep's cellars as a prison.

**Denizens**: Currently, two brigands (**Jorma Lempiä** and **Unto Tapio**), a mercenary warrior (**Kerkko Salme**) and five disarmed **Blood Moon warriors** languish here.

*This long chamber's natural walls glisten with moisture. The ceiling is low—barely 5 ft. high. Within, slumped against the walls, languish three humans and five goblins. All are chained to the walls and look like they have been recently beaten. At the sight of you, the humans call for aid while the goblins hiss and draw back.* 

All the goblins' prisoners greatly desire their freedom. Stat blocks and full details for the human prisoners appear in Appendix 4.

- **Goblins (5)**: These Blood Moon warriors have all displeased Ruknar in some way and are doomed to either be eaten by their fellows or fed to the Devourer (location M6). They are desperate to escape and agree to anything—even fighting their comrades. Of course, they are lying and, if armed, turn on their rescuers as soon as they meet more of their tribe.
- **Jorma Lempiä**: One of the brigands from the watchtower, Jorma (CN male human; Appendix 4), thirsts for revenge on the goblins.
- **Kerkko Salme**: A mercenary guard—the only survivor of his small caravan—Kerkko (LN male human; Appendix 4) has been here for two weeks.
- **Unto Tapio**: Jorma's friend and fellow bandit, Unto (CN male human; Appendix 4), is a coward and desperate to escape.

**Ceiling**: The ceiling is 5 ft. high.

**Walls**: This area was unfinished when the keep fell. Thus, the walls are of hewn rock.

<span id="page-112-0"></span>**Manacles**: Each prisoner is bound to the wall with manacles (DC 20 Dexterity check escapes, DC 20 Strength check breaks, DC 15 Dexterity check made with thieves' tools unlocks). Each is secured to the wall by a normal lock (DC 15 Dexterity check made with thieves' tools unlocks).

#### M11: SHAMAN O F THE BLOOD MOON

These chambers serve as the Blood Moon's fane and their shaman's home.

**Stout Wooden Door**: A sturdy, stout wooden door (AC 15, hp 20, immune to poison and psychic damage) protects this area. If Sar has been warned of intruders abroad in the complex, the door is barred from within (DC 20 Strength check opens).

**Denizens**: The Blood Moon's shaman, **Sar**, is as loyal a member of the tribe as any goblin—that is, he lusts for power and advancement but is terrified of Ruknar's power. The characters' arrival gives Sar an idea; he immediately starts plotting to use them to kill Ruknar so he may become chieftain.

Two **Blood Moon bruisers** guard Sar. When the characters arrive, they are hiding behind slender pillars watching the entrance. If they spot intruders, they shout for Sar and ready themselves for combat. Once Sar becomes aware of intruders, he calls for parley (see "Sar" for details).

*Several slender pillars hold aloft this large chamber's vaulted ceiling. At the chamber's far end, a large recess holds an altar covered in candles. Strange, obviously evil symbols cover the walls.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Illumination**: The candles on the altar bathe it in normal light and provide dim light in a 5-foot radius. Darkness fills the balance of the chamber.

**Ceiling**: The ceiling arches to 15 ft. in height.

**Slender Pillars**: Four slender pillars hold the ceiling aloft. An empty iron torch sconce hangs from each pillar.

**Altar**: The altar is actually a heavy table covered in an old, rancid sheet drenched with bloodstains, melted candle wax and other unidentifiable substances.

**Symbols**: Symbols of obviously evil, malign intent cover the walls. Sar daubed these in blood but, in truth, doesn't really understand them. A DC 10 Intelligence (Religion) check reveals that although they appear sinister, they are essentially gibberish.

**Skulls**: The skulls of four Medium-sized humanoids flank the altar. A DC 15 Wisdom (Medicine) check reveals that their skin and other soft tissues were removed by boiling.

#### M11A: SA R' S PERSONAL CHAMBER

Here dwells **Sar**.

*Bric-a-brac fills this small chamber. A bed of furs lies in one corner, and a workbench covered with magical paraphernalia and a chest stand against another wall.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Fur Bed**: A pile of rank fur comprises Sar's bed. The furs are fleabitten, dirty and smell.

**Workbench**: Covered with objects of supposed magical power, the bench is a triumph of disorganisation. A character spending ten minutes sorting through it finds enough material to make one healer's kit and one component pouch.

**Chest**: The locked chest (AC 15, hp 10, immune to poison and psychic damage; DC 15 Dexterity check made by someone using thieves' tools unlocks) contains four sticks of incense (each worth 5 gp), a golden statue of a dretch (DC 15 Intelligence [Arcana] identifies; worth 50 gp) and 136 sp. Sar carries the key to this chest secreted in his robes.

![](_page_112_Picture_21.jpeg)

#### <span id="page-113-0"></span>M12: GUARDIANS O F THE BLOOD MOON

**Denizens**: **Razogen** and three **Blood Moon bruisers** have been honoured with the task of defending the approach to his father's inner sanctum. He is very keen to add to his skull display and attacks intruders immediately.

The guards here chase fleeing intruders. Unless the characters immediately surrender, they cannot avoid fighting Razogen. Razogen is a ferocious warrior, desperate to gain his father's approval. He hurls himself into battle, seeking out the biggest opponent to slay.

**Door**: This chamber's wooden door is swollen and partially open so the occupants can watch the corridor.

*This smallish room contains a blazing fire set into the floor, a table and several benches. A primitive display of skulls atop a tripod stands near the door.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Illumination**: The fire fills the room with normal light.

**Ceiling**: The ceiling is 10 ft. high.

**Fire**: A large fire burns inside a ring of stones. The fire's smoke escapes through many cracks in the ceiling.

Characters can leap the blazing fire with a DC 10 Strength (Athletics) check; a character failing this check lands in the flames suffers 1d4 fire damage, and must make a DC 10 Dexterity saving throw or catch on fire. A character on fire suffers 1d4 fire damage at the start of its turn but can make a DC 10 Dexterity check to extinguish the flames by using their action.

**Table**: This sturdy wooden table is 2 ft. high. Characters under the table have half cover.

**Decorative Skulls**: Razogen has started to collect the skulls of those he has slain to celebrate his savage prowess.

#### M13: CHIEFTAIN O F THE BLOOD MOON

Here dwells the Blood Moon's savage ogre chieftain.

**Denizens**: **Ruknar** dwells here with his large and aggressive concubine-consorts Nig, Sbux and Zus (**Blood Moon concubines**). Each concubine vies for the honour of bearing his young and attacks intruders savagely to gain his favour. If Ruknar and his concubines are unaware of intruders, they are lounging about the table when the characters arrive. If alerted to impending danger, they are ready for battle.

*A long, very low table stands behind a blazing fire. Piles of furs surround the table, which is heaped with food and drink. The fire's* 

![](_page_113_Picture_16.jpeg)

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Illumination**: A blazing fire fills the room with normal light.

**Ceiling**: The ceiling is 20 ft. high.

**Torch Sconces**: Four empty torch sconces hang from the chamber's walls.

**Fire**: A large fire burns inside a ring of stones. The fire's smoke escapes through many cracks in the ceiling.

Characters can leap the blazing fire with a DC 10 Strength (Athletics) check; a character failing this check lands in the flames suffers 1d4 fire damage and must make a DC 10 Dexterity saving throw or catch on fire. A character on fire suffers 1d4 fire damage at the start of each of its subsequent turns, but can make a DC 10 Dexterity check to extinguish the flames by using their action.

Ruknar hides a large key in a secret hollow beneath the fire (DC 25 Wisdom [Perception] check locates if the fire is lit, DC 15 Wisdom [Perception] check locates if the fire is extinguished). The key opens Ruknar's large ironbound chest.

**Trophy Wall**: Broken weapons, skulls, sundered armour and other items of battle booty are nailed to one wall. All are worthless but serve as testimony to Ruknar's battle prowess.

**Tapestries**: Faded and stained tapestries cover the chamber's walls. Depicting scenes of battle and death, they have been looted from the ruins above. All are worthless.

Characters behind the tapestries are heavily obscured. The tapestries are only loosely affixed to the wall and can be pulled free with a DC 10 Strength check, perhaps onto an enemy. A

character trying to entangle a foe in a tapestry must first pull it from the wall. The tapestry then attempts a grapple by making a Strength (Athletics) check (+8 modifier). Success indicates the target is grappled until they break free from the tapestry.

**Low Table**: This sturdy wooden table is 1 ft. high; its legs have been deliberately shortened. Mounds of fur—used as seats surround the table.

**Large Ironbound Chest**: This large ironbound chest (AC 17, hp 15, immune to poison and psychic damage; DC 15 Dexterity check made by someone using thieves' tools unlocks) holds the tribe's accumulated wealth.

- **Mixed Coinage**: 795 cp, 497 sp, 296 gp and 19 pp.
- **Jewellery**: A golden necklace set with four small translucent yellow gems (carnelians) worth 150 gp.
- **Thieves' Tools**: These finely made thieves' tools nestle in a soft black leather pouch (which bears the initials A.H.)
- *Wand of Secrets*: Runes of power are carved into this long, tapered wand of dark purple, almost black willow. The wand is crafted from an aged piece of rosewood, and the runes carved into its surface deal with secrets and magic.
- **Treasure Map**: This faded map shows the location of the lost dwarven hold of Vongyth (see Player Handout 2).

![](_page_114_Picture_18.jpeg)

# <span id="page-115-0"></span>TH E UNDERCRYPT

This small dungeon sub-level lies below the cellars and is free of the Blood Moon goblins. Built by Valentin to house the remains of those who fell in his service, the Undercrypt has laid mostly undisturbed since the keep's fall. However, an earthquake two decades ago linked the Undercrypt to deeper caverns, and an insidious, ancient corruption has begun to seep forth.

#### A NOTE ON RELIGION

The chapel and Undercrypt are dedicated to the hero-god Kalron, hero-god of battle and heroic struggle. It is a simple job to exchange this personage for one more suitable to your campaign. If you decide to do so, remember to change the descriptions of the various statues, religious symbols and so on throughout this area and surrounding chambers to better suit your chosen deity.

#### KALRON

N hero-god of battle, martial skill and heroic struggle

**Epithets**: The Warrior

**Symbol**: A two-headed battleaxe

**Domains**: War

**Favoured Weapon**: Battleaxe

**Raiment**: Followers of Kalron normally wear armour of some sort, over which they wear a tabard with the god's axe sigil emblazoned upon it.

**Worshippers**: Guards, soldiers, mercenaries and warriors

**Teachings**: Through hardship and struggle comes strength and glory. Sacrifice begets strength. Become one with your weapon, for in such unity lies unbreakable strength.

**Holy Texts**: Kalron's followers study the *Art of the Fighting-Master*. This book sets out the techniques required to wield an array of weapons, including the battleaxe, longsword and morningstar. Additionally, it comprises many lessons on determination, struggle, courage and strength through adversity. Various worshippers have written additional treatises—for example, Lempinen's *On the Axe*—which deals with more advanced fighting techniques and practises.

**Additional Notes**: Kalron was an ancient hero elevated to divine status because of his legendary bravery, battlefield exploits and devotion to his martial skills. His worship is comparatively new, given Kalron ascended to godhood mere centuries ago.

**Temples & Shrines**: Most shrines to the hero-god are found in barracks, castles and other places worshippers gather.

#### ARCHITECTURE & ENVIRONMENT

The Undercrypt has the following generic features:

**Illumination**: Darkness.

**Ceiling**: In most areas, the ceiling is between 10 – 15 ft. high.

**Temperature**: It is noticeably colder in the Undercrypt than in the other caverns and cellars below the keep. In most areas, the lower temperature has no mechanical effects. (However, this is not the case in area U6.)

**Dripping Water**: Cold water drips into the Undercrypt from above. The constant sound of dripping water give disadvantage to hearing-based Wisdom (Perception) checks.

Additionally, unless the characters rig some kind of protection from the unceasing dripping, it is impossible to get a good night's rest in the Undercrypt.

**Grey Sludge**: The water dripping from the ceiling has turned the Undercrypt's deep dust into a grey sludge. A DC 15 Intelligence (Nature) check reveals the sludge to be harmless.

The sludge makes tracking much easier. Characters making checks to find or follow tracks do so with advantage. Where the sludge is particularly deep, it counts as difficult terrain.

**Hewn Stone Walls**: The slick walls are of hewn stone. Crudely hacked from the hill's bedrock, they provide numerous hand and footholds for climbers (DC 15 Strength [Athletics] check scales).

**Necrotic Corruption**: Necrotic corruption has leaked into the Undercrypt from below, corrupting the bodies of those interred within. A character casting *detect evil and good* discovers the Undercrypt was once magically consecrated but that a subsequent more powerful desecration effect now lies over the place. (The source of this corruption is a matter for you to decide, but see "U6: Chasm of Ebon Depths" for more information.)

# UNDERCRYPT DRESSING

Use this table to generate minor points of interest, as desired. Such features have little or no impact on play, but serve to underscore the current state of the Undercrypt.

#### **D12 DRESSING**

| 1  | Thick grey sludge covers the floor. Treat the area as<br>difficult terrain.                                                                         |

| 6  | The sludge hides a small hole in the floor. A random<br>character stumbles and falls prone in the sludge (DC<br>15 Dexterity saving throw negates). |
