# <span id="page-116-0"></span>UNDERCRYPT KE Y

- **U1 Pit of the Dead**: This 20-foot deep pit holds two sodden **zombies** and bars access to the rest of the sub-level. Beyond, a sodden door wards the rest of the Undercrypt.
- **U2 Hall of Battle**: Intricate carvings of Valentin Ironwolf's victories decorate this uninhabited corridor.
- **U3 Warrior's Chapel**: This large chamber was the keep's chapel. It is unoccupied.
- **U4 Columned Hallway**: Two **animate statues** protect this earthquake-damaged corridor. If too many of the pillars are damaged here, the ceiling collapses.
- **U5 The Crypt**: Four **gravechill skeletons**, along with animate skulls attached to chains hanging from the ceiling, lurk in this chill chamber.
- **U6 Chasm of Ebon Depths**: Necrotic corruption wells up into the Undercrypt from this deep chasm. **Shadows** dwell within.

![](_page_116_Picture_7.jpeg)

![](_page_116_Figure_8.jpeg)

# <span id="page-117-0"></span>U1: PI T O F THE DEAD

The characters must cross this area to access the Undercrypt.

**Denizens**: Two sodden human **zombies** lie under the pit's black water. The remains of two bandits who triggered this trap long ago attack any living creatures in the pit. The zombies are so water-logged they have fire resistance while in the pit and for one hour after they emerge. The zombies fight until destroyed or until there are no living creatures in sight. If there are no living creatures in the pit, they climb out to kill any other visible targets.

*A narrow, dust-shrouded stair descends about thirty feet and ends in a corridor. The walls and floor are wet and glisten in your light. The sound of dripping water fills your ears.* 

When the characters reach the bottom of the stairs, read:

*This narrow corridor ends in a wall pierced by a single doorway, partially filled by a rotting wooden door. An open 20 ft. long pit blocks further progress. Black water fills the pit.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Steep Stairs**: Characters taking the Dash action on the stairs must make a DC 10 Dexterity (Acrobatics) check. A character failing this check falls 1d2x5 ft. and lands prone.

**Ceiling**: The ceiling above the stairs is only six feet high. In the corridor, it rises to 12 ft.

**Walls**: The slick, hewn stone walls require DC 20 Strength (Athletics) checks to scale. Water oozes down the walls.

**Rotten Door**: This rotten door blocks the view of what lies beyond but collapses as soon as a character touches it.

#### TH E PI T

The pit blocks progress along the passageway and has the following noteworthy features:

**Depth**: The pit is 20 ft. deep. Characters falling into the shallow pit suffer 2d6 bludgeoning damage and land prone.

**Walls**: Characters can scale the pit's slick walls with DC 20 Strength (Athletics) checks.

**Water**: Three-foot-deep black, stagnant water fills the pit. Characters in the water have half cover.

# U2: HALL O F BAT TLE

This hallway is unoccupied.

*An intricate bas-relief carving of human warriors fighting a host of orcs and goblins covers one long wall of this hallway.* 

Valentin had this hallway decorated in celebration of his great victory against his orc and goblin enemies.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Battle Carving**: This intricate bas-relief carving depicts a woodland battle between Valentin's followers and his enemies: the Severed Hand orcs and the Blood Moon goblins. The humans are shown crushing their enemies and trampling on the many corpses of the fallen. A warrior is shown surrounded by piles of the fallen.

Characters viewing the carving may learn more:

- **DC 10 Intelligence (History)**: Forty years ago, Valentin defeated the orcs of the Severed Hand and the goblins of the Blood Moon. He also exterminated the Ebon Scales kobolds.
- **DC 15 Intelligence (History)**: The orcs are from the Severed Hand tribe, while the goblins hail from the Blood Moon tribe. The scene probably depicts one of his famous victories, possibly the Battle of Slaughter Meadow, wherein he broke the tribes' strength and slew the Severed Hand's chief (and many of his bodyguards) in single combat.

#### U3: WARRIOR' S CHAPEL

This large chamber was the keep's chapel. It is unoccupied.

*Two statues of warriors clad in plate and wielding a battleaxe flank a stone altar at the far end of this chamber. A small rotting ironbound coffer stands on the altar. Grey sludge covers much of the floor, and thick clumps of black mould grows on the walls.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Air Temperature**: It is cold within the chapel.

**Grey Sludge**: A thick layer of grey sludge covers much of the floor. A DC 10 Wisdom (Survival) check reveals nothing has recently moved through the sludge. A character using the Dash action must make a DC 10 Dexterity (Acrobatics) check or stop moving in the first sludge-filled square they enter. A character failing this check by 5 or more falls prone.

**Black Mould**: Several patches of black mould grow around the warrior statues. A DC 15 Wisdom (Nature) check reveals that the mould is natural and harmless.

**Warrior Statues**: Each intricately carved statue stands 10 ft. tall and depicts a warrior of severe mien clad in plate armour and holding a battleaxe grounded at their feet. A statue can be scaled with a DC 10 Strength (Athletics) check.

**Altar**: This plain stone altar stands 4 ft. high.

**Rotting Coffer**: This small, rotting, unlocked, iron-bound coffer contains items of religious significance. Much of the contents—including a copy of *Art of the Fighting-Master* and so on —have rotted away, leaving the chest half-full of sludge; a few treasures remain, however:

- A gold idol of a warrior wielding a battleaxe (worth 30 gp).
- A set of silver chimes (worth 10 gp) that produce a harsh, discordant sound when struck.
- A small wrought iron tripod (worth 10 gp) holding a sludgefilled iron bowl. The sludge hides three matched small opaque dark green gems (malachites, each worth 15 gp).

#### U4: COLUMNED HALLWAY

This columned hallway suffered some damage when the earthquake struck 20 years ago.

**Denizens**: Two **animate statues**, indistinguishable from the other statues holding aloft the ceiling, protect this area. They animate and attack when the first intruder reaches the mid-way point of the hallway. They focus on the intruders furthest along the <span id="page-118-0"></span>hallway. The statues pursue intruders as far as U1 but do not cross the pit.

*Slender pillars—carved to represent human warriors clad in plate armour and holding a battleaxe grounded in front of them—hold aloft this chill hallway's sagging ceiling.* 

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Air Temperature**: It is barely above freezing here.

**Ceiling**: The cracked and sagging ceiling is 12 ft. high. A DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check reveals that the ceiling is unsafe. A DC 20 Wisdom (Perception) check reveals that the destruction of two pillars will cause a cave-in.

**Warrior Columns**: The damaged columns (AC 14, hp 27, damage threshold 8, immune to poison and psychic damage, DC 15 Strength check breaks) hold the ceiling aloft. The columns provide half cover and can be scaled with a DC 15 Strength (Athletics) check. Destroying one or more of the inanimate columns causes the ceiling to collapse. Refer to "Collapsing Ceiling" for more details.

#### COLLAPSING CEILING

The characters may deliberately (or accidentally) cause the ceiling in U4 to collapse. Use these notes to adjudicate the subsequent events.

- **First Round**: In the round after a column falls, the ceiling in adjacent squares noticeably sags; dust and small rocks fall. The animate statues do not understand the danger and make no special actions to avoid the effect.
- **Second Round**: The ceiling collapses in a 10-foot radius around the collapsed pillars. Any character under the collapsing part of the ceiling must make a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw or suffer 4d10 bludgeoning damage or half as much damage on a successful save. Once the ceiling has collapsed, rubble, which counts as difficult terrain, covers the floor below the collapsed section.
- **Subsequent Rounds**: The area of collapsing ceiling expands in a 5-foot radius every subsequent round until the entire hallway's ceiling has collapsed.

# U5: TH E CRYPT

Here, Valentin Ironwolf interred his slain followers in honour and state amid the remains of those they vanquished in battle. Sadly, the corruption emanating from the Chasm of Ebon Depths (U6) has animated some of the remains as fell undead creatures.

**Denizens**: As soon as a living creature enters the chamber, the skull chains animate; the clacking of their jaws alerts the four **gravechill skeletons** to intruders. The skeletons rise and move to attack in the next round. They fight until destroyed.

*It is freezing here. Chains, a skull hanging from each one, hang from the ceiling of this large chamber. In the centre of the room, a silver aspergillum hangs from a stout chain.* 

Rusted iron bars running from floor to ceiling divide this chamber into a number of distinct sections. Within each section, a jumble of bones covers the floor.

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Ceiling**: The ceiling is 20 ft. high.

**Air Temperature**: It is barely above freezing within the crypt. **Skull Chains**: Frost-rimmed chains (AC 19, hp 10; DC 20 Strength check bursts) hang from the ceiling to about four feet above the floor. A grinning goblin or orc skull (AC 15, hp 5) hangs from each one. The skulls animate, gnashing their teeth, when a living creature enters the chamber.

- **Movement (Medium or Larger Creatures)**: Medium or larger characters can avoid the animated skulls by moving slowly and carefully through the room. (It costs 2 squares of movement to enter a square in such a manner .) Alternatively, a character can ignore the skulls and move at normal speed. Every round a character does so, they take two piercing damage as the skulls bite at the living creature moving through their squares.
- **Movement (Small or Smaller Creatures)**: Small or smaller characters move normally under the skulls and do not take damage from the skulls.

**Bone Piles**: Squares containing piles of bones count as difficult terrain (it costs 2 squares of movement to enter such a square).

**Chained Silver Battle Aspergillum**: A silver aspergillum filled with holy water hangs from a chain in the chamber's centre.

• **Silver Battle Aspergillum (25 gp)**: This simple one-handed melee weapon deals 1d6 bludgeoning damage. A character can fill a battle aspergillum with holy water by using an action. A fiend or an undead struck by a battle aspergillum filled with holy water suffers 1d6 radiant damage and the weapon's normal bludgeoning damage. After two hits, the aspergillum must be refilled.

**Stone Columns**: Thick stone columns hold the roof aloft.

**Iron Bars**: Rusted iron bars (AC 19, damage threshold 8, hp 22, DC 20 Strength check bends) divide the room into sections. The iron bars provide half cover.

**Treasure**: Some of the glorious dead were interred with items of sentimental or actual value. A character making a Wisdom (Perception) check may uncover one or more items as they search the crypt:

- **DC 10**: A rotted grave shift embroidered with electrum braiding. The bright yellow braiding is in good condition (and worth 20 gp), but the shift is valueless.
- **DC 15**: A pair of golden earrings shaped like intricate flowers (worth 150 gp).
- **DC 20**: This steel potion vial has a wavy blue pattern etched into its neck. It contains a cloudy green liquid—a *potion of water breathing*.

# <span id="page-119-0"></span>U6: CHASM O F EBON DEPTHS

A connection to the Chasm of Ebon Depths formed when an earthquake struck the area and dumped a section of the Undercrypt into the chasm below.

**Denizen**: The characters may encounter one or more **shadows** here. (See "Necrotic Corruption" for more information).

*The still, black water filling this chasm glimmers sinisterly in the light. Water drips down from above, filling the cavern with the sound of rain. An aura of malign cold hangs in the air.* 

The flooded chasm likely blocks further exploration but could serve as the route to future adventures. (See "Further Adventures" for more details .)

#### NOTABLE FEATURES

**Temperature**: The water in the chasm is only a few degrees above freezing, and the air above the chasm is no warmer. A character without cold resistance, thick and warming clothing, or the like must make a DC 10 Constitution saving throw after one hour in the chasm's proximity (and every hour thereafter). Characters failing their saving throw gain one additional level of exhaustion.

**Depth**: The water-filled chasm is 120 ft. deep.

**Chasm Walls**: The chasm walls are of natural stone and contain many niches and several entrances to small, inundated cavern systems. Characters can climb the cavern walls with DC 15 Strength (Athletics) checks.

**Black Water**: Calm, black water (DC 10 Strength [Athletics] check to swim) fills the bottom 60 ft. of the chasm. Additionally:

- **Vision**: The black water obscures vision as the *darkness* spell.
- **Evil Aura**: *Detect evil* a*nd good* reveals an aura of desecration emanating from the water.
- **Water Temperature**: The water is virtually freezing. Characters in the water must make a Constitution saving throw as detailed in "Temperature" every ten minutes.

#### NECROTIC CORRUPTION

The flooded chasm is the source of the necrotic corruption warping the remains of the heroic dead interred in U5. The corruption's cause is up to you, but some examples of the corruption's vile source include:

- The barrier between the Shadow Plane and the Material Plane is weak around the chasm. This weakness allows necrotic energy to seep into the world. A small colony of six **shadows** has also slipped through into the cave. They lurk in the cracked chasm walls. Occasionally, they enter the cavern and immediately attack any living creature they encounter.
- Ancient, terrible things slither and ooze in the Ebon Realm. Although the Ebon Chasm is but 120 ft. deep, cracks and fissures in the rock descend far deeper into places where light and surface dwellers have never ventured. Eventually, these caverns intersect with the frozen lair of a mighty shoggoth. The shoggoth (fortunately) does not know of the connection between its realm and the Ebon Chasm, but certain of its unspeakable, alien activities are propagating the chill of its lair upwards.

Some characters—particularly those strong in the cause of good and law—may desire to remove this foul necrotic taint from the dungeons under the Shadowed Keep (particularly if they plan to claim the keep as their own). Such a quest could become the focus of an entire subterranean campaign! Refer to "Further Information" for more suggestions about how to continue play.

![](_page_119_Picture_18.jpeg)

# <span id="page-120-0"></span>FURTHER ADVENTURES

The Shadowed Keep can fade from your campaign—an adventure site cleansed and forgotten—or it can feature in future adventures.

#### CAVERNS DEEP

There are deep caverns below the keep, unknown (until now) by surface dwellers. If the characters discover their hidden entrances (locations M6 and W2) they could begin an epic quest to explore the lightless realms below. Alternatively, an invasion of deep dwellers could boil forth from the eternal dark. If the characters have claimed the keep as their own, they must end this threat or lose their home.

#### CHASM O F EBON DEPTHS

This water-filled fissure (location U6) offers further adventures beyond this adventure's scope. However, the characters likely require magic to make appreciable progress therein. If you decide to stock the chasm and the caverns radiating out from it first decide what is causing the corruption seeping upwards from below (see "Necrotic Corruption" [location U6]).

Alternatively, if the characters lack water-breathing magic and you want to include the area in your campaign, a minor earthquake or rock fall could open up a new passageway that slowly drains the chasm. As the water level gradually drops, the party gains access to new caves and new adventures!

# CLAIMING THE KEEP

Once the keep is empty, the characters could claim it as their own. In this way, the keep can become the focus of an entire campaign as the characters battle to clear the surrounding woodlands of enemies while repairing the shattered fortress. The obstacles to successfully completing such a task are legion.

Of course, the remaining denizens of the woods do their utmost to stymie such efforts. If any serious attempt at rebuilding is to be undertaken, the characters must first make the area safe for the many workers they must employ. They must also protect the routes by which men and material flow to the fortress.

Wido Gall, other local rulers or even Duke Armas Nenonen himself may take exception to the characters' power grab or see them as a nascent threat best nipped in the bud.

Over all this hangs the spectre of money (or lack thereof). The characters cannot rebuild their new home if they do not have the necessary funds. Thus, they must continue adventuring, find a rich patron or devise other inventive schemes to meet the high costs of rebuilding, completing and garrisoning their home.

Once the keep is firmly under their command, they have a base from which they can extend their control over the surrounding woodlands. (The sudden appearance at this time of a relative of Valentin Ironwolf, who demands the character return the castle to its rightful owner, could create interesting role-playing opportunities.)

#### HOLDING A GRUDGE

It is unlikely that the characters wipe out the goblins and bandits. Survivors could hold a grudge and return later in the campaign to exact their revenge. Such folk could be nothing more than a minor irritant or could have gained power consummate to the party's.

#### VONGYTH

In two places (locations W7 and M13), the characters may find maps (Player's Handout 3 and 4, respectively) regarding the fallen dwarven hold of Vongyth. They may choose to seek out the dwarves' fallen home.

Refer to "Vongyth" (page 32) to learn more about Vongyth.

#### WA R

The keep could be occupied in the future by bandits or by a force —perhaps a large migrating tribe of orcs or the like—that menaces the whole duchy. As the characters know the area and keep, they are called upon to end the threat. If this second threat emerges when the characters are relatively powerful and famous, they may subsequently be given the right to rebuild the keep by Wido Gall or Duke Nenonen in return for their support and loyalty. This could open a new chapter in the campaign wherein the characters must deal with and navigate the machinations of Ashlar's nobles.

# <span id="page-123-0"></span>APPENDIX 1: DENIZENS O F DULWICH

This appendix presents the additional stat blocks you need to run encounters in Dulwich. The stat blocks appear in alphabetic order.

#### BRAALITES

Foul worshippers of the Dweller in Shadows stoop to any hateful depravity to venerate their loathsome patron. Such folk are wellversed at hiding among Ashlar's common folk. Careful cults can remain undetected for decades while more bloodthirsty groups inevitably reveal themselves (with predictable results).

**Braalite Cultist**: The cult's rank-and-file kidnap sacrificial victims, attend dark rituals and so on. Most are easily led, selfentered folk; all dream of advancement in the cult's ranks.

**Braalite Fanatic**: Such is the depth of a fanatic's depravity they have been granted a small measure of power by their shadowy patron. They assist the priest in running the cult, all the while scheming to increase their own standing and power.

**Braalite Priest**: The priest wields supreme authority over their minions. Ostensibly, their position is secure, but many are wildly paranoid and obsessed with power and their own survival.

# BRAAL

NE lesser god of hate, malice and revenge

**Epithets**: The Hated, Dweller in Shadows

**Symbol**: A cloven skull **Domains**: Death, Trickery **Favoured Weapon**: Morningstar

**Raiment**: Braal's adherents wear cowled black cloaks smeared with their sacrifices' blood and often shave their heads.

**Worshippers**: Braal whispers dark promises to the disposed, the bullied and those who desire power over their compatriots. Goblins and half-goblins also worship Braal, although he disdains such odious worshippers.

**Teachings**: Strike from the shadows; punish those who have wronged you and show no mercy. Take what you want and destroy that which you cannot take.

**Holy Texts**: The worship of Braal is not as prescriptive as other religions. No universally agreed upon text exists, but several dark tomes are preferred by various sects.

**Additional Notes**: Braal is the dark to Darlen's light. The struggle between the two is ancient and unending, and great enmity exists between their worshippers. For all his plotting and evil doings, however, Braal is nothing compared to the elder power of certain ancient, primal demons.

**Temples & Shrines**: Braal's temples are dark, hidden places concealed far from the prying eyes of non-believers. Normally his worshippers organise themselves into cults that confine themselves to a small geographical area. His followers are always secretive types, well versed in hiding in plain sight.

#### **BRAALITE C ULTIST**

*Medium humanoid (human), neutral evil* 

**Armour Class** 12 (leather armour)

**Hit Points** 9 (2d8)

# **BRAALITE PRIEST**

*Skull Cloud*. As a bonus action, the Braalite priest can expend a spell slot to create a whirling cloud of biting skulls around one target it can see within 60 ft. The target must make a DC 13 Dexterity saving throw or suffer 10 (3d6) necrotic damage. A successful save reduces the damage by half. The skull cloud then disappears. If the priest expends a spell slot of 2nd level or higher, the damage increases by 1d6 for each level above 1st.

*Spellcasting*. The Braalite priest is a 5th-level spellcaster. Its spellcasting ability is Wisdom (spell save DC 13, +5 to hit with spell attacks) The priest has the following cleric spells prepared:

1st level (4 slots): *command*, *cure wounds*, *inflict wounds, sanctuary*

#### SAINI ALANEN

*This modestly dressed woman wears red velvet robes. A chunk of glowing crystal hangs around her neck.* 

**Background**: Sage and librarian, Saini is one of Dulwich's most educated and informed citizens.

**Personality**: Fascinated by local history, Saini is an avid collector of diaries, books and maps about the history of Dulwich and its surrounds. She loves finding a new diary, travelogue or sheaf of maps. She also delights in speaking with "old-timers" and non-humans with long lifespans, such as dwarves and elves. Possessed of prodigious intellect, Saini is one of the cleverest, most educated folk in the town.

**Mannerisms**: Impressively patient and softly spoken, Saini is capable of great bouts of concentration. She's not particularly enamoured with "outside".

#### **S AINI ALANEN**

*Medium humanoid (human), neutral good* 

**Armour Class** 11 **Hit Points** 27 (8d8)

**Speed** 30 ft.

|---------|---------|---------|---------|---------|---------|
| 10 (+0) | 13 (+1) | 10 (+0) | 16 (+3) | 12 (+1) | 10 (+0) |

**Saving Throws** Int +5

**Skills** Arcana +5, History +5, Religion +5

**Senses** passive Perception 11

**Languages** Common, Draconic, Elven

**Challenge** 1 (200 XP)

*Spellcasting*. Saini is a 3rd-level spellcaster. Her spellcasting ability is Intelligence (spell save DC 13, +5 to hit with spell attacks). She has the following wizard spells prepared:

Cantrips (at will): *mage hand*, *message*, *prestidigitation*

1st level (4 slots): *comprehend languages*, *detect magic*, *identify*, *magic missile*

2nd level (2 slots): *detect thoughts*, *locate object*

#### **ACTIONS**

*Dagger*. *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack*: +3 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 20/60 ft. one target. *Hit*: 3 (1d4+1) piercing damage.

# <span id="page-125-0"></span>APPENDIX 2: SHUNNED VALLEY DENIZENS

Use these stat blocks to depict the various traps, friends and foes the characters encounter in the Shunned Valley.

#### TH E SHUNNED VALLEY

#### AILA O F THE LAKE

If you use the optional encounter "Dead Aila", use these statistics to depict the ghostly druid.

#### **AILA**

*Bedraggled and muddy, this translucent woman's hair floats in the air about her head in an unsettling manner.* 

*Medium undead, neutral* 

**Armour Class** 11 **Hit Points** 27 (6d8) **Speed** 0 ft., fly 40 ft.

| STR     | DEX     | CON     | INT     | WIS     | CHA     |
|---------|---------|---------|---------|---------|---------|
| 10 (+0) | 13 (+1) | 10 (+0) | 10 (+0) | 15 (+2) | 14 (+2) |

**Damage Resistances** acid, fire, lightning, thunder; bludgeoning, piercing and slashing from nonmagical weapons

**Damage Immunities** cold, necrotic, poison

**Condition Immunities** charmed, exhaustion, frightened, grappled, paralysed, petrified, poisoned, prone, restrained

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 14

**Skills** Nature +2, Perception +4

**Languages** Common **Challenge** 3 (700 XP)

*Ethereal Sight.* Aila can see 60 ft. into the Ethereal Plane when she is on the Material Plane, and vice versa.

*Incorporeal Movement.* Aila can move through other creatures and objects as if they were difficult terrain. She takes 5 (1d10) force damage if he ends his turn inside an object.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Withering Touch*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +3 to hit, reach 5 ft., target. *Hit*: 11 (3d6+1) necrotic damage.

*Etherealness*. Aila enters the Ethereal Plane from the Material Plane or vice versa. She is visible on the Material Plane while she is in the Border Ethereal and vice versa yet she can't affect or be affected by anything on the other plane.

*Horrifying Visage.* Each non-undead creature within 60 ft. of Aila that can see her must make a DC 13 Wisdom saving throw or be frightened for 1 minute. If the save fails by 5 or more, the target also ages 1d4 x 10 years. A frightened target can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the frightened condition on itself with a successful save. If a target's saving throw is successful or the effect ends for it, the target is immune to Aila's Horrifying Visage for the next 24 hours. The ageing effect can be reversed with a *greater restoration* spell, but only within 24 hours of it occurring.

*Possession (Recharge 5-6).* One humanoid that Aila can see within 5 feet of her must make a DC 13 Charisma saving throw or be possessed by her; Aila then disappears, and the target is incapacitated and loses control of its body. Aila now controls the body but doesn't deprive the target of awareness. Aila can't be targeted by any attack or spell, except ones that turn undead, and she retains her alignment, Intelligence, Wisdom, Charisma and immunity to being charmed and frightened. She otherwise uses the possessed target's statistics, but doesn't gain access to the target's knowledge, class features or proficiencies. The possession lasts until the body drops to 0 hit points, Aila ends it as a bonus action, or she is turned or forced out by an effect like the *dispel evil and good* spell. When the possession ends, Aila reappears in an unoccupied space within 5 feet of the body. The target is immune to Aila's Possession for 24 hours after succeeding on the saving throw or after the possession ends.

#### GIANT FROG

The giant frog lurks in location C.

# **GIANT FROG**

*This gigantic frog has moist, mottled green and black skin.* 

*Medium beast, unaligned* 

**Armour Class** 11 **Hit Points** 18 (4d8) **Speed** 30 ft., swim 30 ft.

| STR     | DEX     | CON     | INT    | WIS     | CHA    |
|---------|---------|---------|--------|---------|--------|
| 12 (+1) | 13 (+1) | 11 (+0) | 2 (-4) | 10 (+0) | 3 (-4) |

**Skills** Perception +2, Stealth +3

**Damage Resistances** 

**Senses** darkvision 30 ft., passive Perception 12

**Languages** —

**Challenge** 1/4 (50 XP)

*Amphibious. The frog can breathe air and water.*

*Standing Leap. The frog's long jump is up to 20 feet and its high jump is up to 10 feet, with or without a running start.*

#### **ACTIONS**

*Bite*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +3 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 4 (1d6+1) piercing damage, and the target is grappled (escape DC 11). Until this grapple ends, the target is restrained, and the frog can't bite another target.

*Swallow*. The frog makes one bite attack against a Small or smaller target it is grappling. If it hits, the target is swallowed, and the grapple ends. The swallowed target is blinded and restrained, it has total cover against attacks and other effects outside the frog, and it takes 5 (2d4) acid damage at the start of each of the frog's turns. The frog can have only one target swallowed at a time. If the frog dies, a swallowed creature is no longer restrained by it and can escape from the corpse using 5 feet of movement, exiting prone.

#### E: TOMB O F THE STONE WOMAN

Deadly traps and a terrible animated guardian lurk in the Tomb of the Stone Woman.

#### COLLAPSING CEILING TRAP

Twinned with the Poison Gas Trap detailed below, this trap waits to trap and slay the unwary.

#### **C OLLAPSING CEILING**

**Triggering the Trap**: This trap uses a trip wire to collapse the supports keeping an unstable section of unstable ceiling in place.

**Spotting the Trap**: The trip wire (DC 15 Wisdom [Perception] spots) is 3 inches off the ground and stretches between two support beams.

**Disabling the Trap**: A DC 15 Dexterity check made by someone using thieves' tools disarms the trap. On a failed check, the trap triggers.

**Effect**: The ceiling collapses filling the two squares behind the capstone with rubble. Creatures in the area take 11 (2d10) bludgeoning damage and are buried in the rubble (DC 15 Dexterity saving throw halves the damage and negates the buried result. Characters making a DC 20 Dexterity saving throw may elect to dive out of the tomb (but still take damage). Once the trap is triggered, the entrance to the tomb is blocked.

- **Buried Characters**: A conscious character buried in the rubble must make a DC 15 Constitution saving throw or fall unconscious. Unconscious characters buried in the rubble must make a death-saving throw every round.
- **Freeing Buried Characters (or Escaping the Tomb)**: Freeing a character from the rubble requires a DC 20 Strength check. With a DC 23 Strength check a character clears the rubble in one round. It takes 2d10 minutes to clear the rubble from the entrance.

#### DART SWARM TRAP

Activated when the stone wizard steps down from its plinth, this trap fires darts until it runs out of ammunition.

**Triggering the Trap**: The dart swarm trap activates when the stone wizard steps down from the plinth.

**Spotting the Trap**: Twenty small holes ring the stone plinth (DC 11 Wisdom [Perception] spots). Checks made to find the holes once the trap has activated have advantage.

**Disabling the Trap**: A pressure plate system prohibits the trap from activating while a weight of 200 lb. or more, such as the stone wizard or a heavily armoured character, is on the plinth. A character can plug the gaps with a DC 11 Dexterity check, but this takes five minutes of work.

**Effect**: Once the trap activates, it fires darts into the room. Every round, the trap targets 1d3 living creatures in location E5; each takes 4 (1d4+2) piercing damage (a DC 11 Dexterity saving throw negates the damage). The trap continues firing until it has shot 20 darts.

#### POISON GA S TRAP

Twinned with the Collapsing Ceiling Trap detailed above, this trap waits to trap and slay the unwary.

#### **P OISON GA S**

**Triggering the Trap**: One minute after the ceiling collapses, a pale yellowy mist (insanity gas) starts to seep into the corridor through the tiny holes in the walls.

**Spotting the Trap**: A character making a DC 15 Wisdom (Perception) check spots the tiny holes in the walls.

**Disabling the Trap**: The tiny holes in the walls can be plugged with a DC 13 Dexterity check.

**Effect**: There is enough insanity gas to fill locations E2 and E3. It takes five rounds for the trap to fill the areas. For the subsequent five rounds all characters in these areas reduce their Wisdom by 1d3 (DC 13 Constitution saving throw negates). This reduction lasts until the character takes a long rest.

#### STONE WIZARD

The stone wizard slays all who dare invade the tomb.

#### **STONE WIZARD**

*This stone statue depicts a muscular hobgoblin female wearing form-hugging robes cinched with a wide belt.* 

*Medium construct, unaligned* 

**Armour Class** 16 (natural armour)

**Hit Points** 77 (14d10)

**Speed** 25 ft.

| STR     | DEX    | CON     | INT    | WIS    | CHA    |
|---------|--------|---------|--------|--------|--------|
| 16 (+3) | 8 (-1) | 11 (+0) | 1 (-5) | 3 (-4) | 1 (-5) |

**Saving Throws** Wisdom -2

**Damage Immunities** poison, psychic

**Condition Immunities** blinded, charmed, deafened, exhaustion, frightened, paralysed, petrified, poisoned

**Senses** blindsight 60 ft. (blind beyond this radius), passive Perception 6

**Languages** —

**Challenge** 3 (700 XP)

*Antimagic Susceptibility*. The stone wizard is incapacitated while in the area of an *antimagic field*. If targeted by *dispel magic*, the stone wizard must succeed on a Constitution saving throw against the caster's spell DC or fall unconscious for 1 minute.

*False Appearance*. While the stone wizard remains motionless, it is indistinguishable from a normal statue.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Multiattack*. The stone wizard makes two melee attacks.

*Slam*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 6 (1d6+3) bludgeoning damage.

#### DREAD SHRINE O F THE SUPREME WARLORD

#### CHARNEL GUARDIAN

*This dull grey stone statue depicts a double-headed battleaxe.* 

Charnel guardians are "living" statues. Priests of evil religions use these foul creations as protectors for their fallen shrines. They appear at first glance to be merely carven statues. Some charnel guardians look like skeletons or other forms of undead, and characters may suspect they are undead, but they are unaffected by such abilities as Turn Undead and the like.

**Combat Tactics**: A charnel guardian batters its foes until they are slain. It does not leave the area it protects.

**Constructed Nature**: A charnel guardian doesn't require air, food, drink or sleep.

The magic that animates a charnel guardian is dispelled when the construct drops to 0 hit points. A charnel guardian reduced to 0 hit points becomes inanimate and collapses—perhaps falling apart; at this point, it is too damaged to be of any further use either as a guardian or a decoration.

# **CHARNEL GUARDIAN**

*Medium construct, unaligned* 

**Armour Class** 18 (natural armour)

**Hit Points** 33 (6d8+6)

**Speed** fly 25 ft.

| STR     | DEX     | CON     | INT    | WIS     | CHA     |
|---------|---------|---------|--------|---------|---------|
| 14 (+2) | 11 (+0) | 13 (+1) | 1 (-5) | 10 (+0) | 13 (+1) |

**Damage Immunities** poison, psychic

**Condition Immunities** blinded, charmed, deafened, exhaustion, frightened, paralysed, petrified, poisoned

**Senses** blindsight 60 ft. (blind beyond this radius), passive Perception 10

**Languages** —

**Challenge** 2 (450 XP)

*Antimagic Susceptibility*. The charnel guardian is incapacitated while in the area of an *antimagic field*. If targeted by *dispel magic*, the charnel guardian must make a Constitution saving throw against the caster's spell save DC or fall unconscious for one minute.

*False Appearance*. While the charnel guardian remains motionless, it is indistinguishable from a normal statue.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Multiattack*. The charnel guardian makes two melee attacks.

*Slam*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 5 (1d6+2) slashing damage.

*Terrifying Gaze*. The charnel guardian targets one creature it can see within 30 feet of it. If the target can see the charnel guardian, the target must succeed on a DC 11 Wisdom saving throw or be magically frightened until the end of the charnel guardian's next turn. The frightened target is paralysed.

#### GUARDIAN AX E

*This rusty battleaxe flies through the air under its own volition.* 

Mindless guardians of the shrine, the guardian axes attack anyone profaning its precincts. A guardian axe attacks the nearest foe.

**Combat Tactics**: A guardian axe hacks at its foes until they are destroyed. It does not leave the area it protects.

**Constructed Nature**: A guardian axe doesn't require air, food, drink or sleep.

The magic that animates a guardian axe is dispelled when the construct drops to 0 hit points. A guardian axe reduced to 0 hit points becomes inanimate and falls to the ground—perhaps sundered or irrevocably bent; at this point, it is too damaged to be of any further use either as a guardian or a decoration.

#### ZOMBIE HOBGOBLIN WARRIOR

*Swathed from head to toe in greying, mouldering funeral bandages worn under rusty chain armour, this human-sized humanoid clutches a battleaxe. Its red eyes gleam balefully.* 

Centuries ago, a hobgoblin priest experimented with mummification to preserve the best qualities of a warrior after death. However, he failed, and all he created were zombies that looked like mummies but which had a few of a mummy's special features and qualities. For example, the hobgoblin zombie can talk (after a fashion) and retains more intelligence than a normal zombie. Sadly, however, the zombie is also vulnerable to fire.

**Looks Like a Mummy**: At first glance, this hobgoblin zombie looks like a mummy.

**Undead Nature**: A zombie hobgoblin does not require air, food, drink or sleep.

#### **Z OMBIE H OBGOBLIN WARRIOR**

*Medium undead (goblinoid [hobgoblin]), lawful evil* 

**Armour Class** 11 (chain shirt) **Hit Points** 30 (4d8+12)

**Speed** 20 ft.

|---------|--------|---------|--------|---------|--------|
| 15 (+2) | 6 (-2) | 16 (+3) | 6 (-2) | 10 (+0) | 5 (-2) |

**Saving Throws** Wis +0 **Damage Vulnerabilities** fire

**Damage Immunities** poison

**Condition Immunities** poisoned

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 10

**Languages** Common and Goblin

**Challenge** 1/4 (50 XP)

*Undead Fortitude*. If damage reduces a zombie hobgoblin warrior to 0 hit points, it must make a Constitution saving throw with a DC of 5 + the damage taken, unless the damage is radiant or from a critical hit. On a success, the zombie hobgoblin warrior drops to 1 hit point instead.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Battleaxe*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 6 (1d8+2) slashing damage or 7 (1d10+2) slashing damage if used with two hands.

#### MORG DROLAK, ZOMBIE WARLORD

*Swathed from head to toe in greying, mouldering funeral bandages worn under ornate half-plate armour, this human-sized humanoid clutches a battleaxe in both hands. Its red eyes gleam balefully as it shuffles forward.* 

Centuries ago, a hobgoblin priest experimented with mummification to preserve the best qualities of a warrior after death. However, he failed, and all he created were zombies that looked like mummies but which had a few of a mummy's special features and qualities. For example, the hobgoblin zombie can talk (after a fashion) and retains more intelligence than a normal zombie. Sadly, however, the zombie is also vulnerable to fire.

**Looks Like a Mummy**: At first glance, the zombie warlord looks like a mummy.

**Undead Nature**: The zombie warlord does not require air, food, drink or sleep.

#### **MORG DROLAK , Z OMBIE WARLORD**

*Medium undead (goblinoid [hobgoblin]), lawful evil* 

**Armour Class** 15 (half plate) **Hit Points** 60 (8d8+24)

**Speed** 20 ft.

| STR     | DEX    | CON     | INT    | WIS     | CHA    |
|---------|--------|---------|--------|---------|--------|
| 17 (+3) | 6 (-2) | 16 (+3) | 6 (-2) | 10 (+0) | 5 (-2) |

**Saving Throws** Wis +0 **Damage Vulnerabilities** fire **Damage Immunities** poison

**Condition Immunities** poisoned **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 10

**Languages** Common and Goblin

**Challenge** 2 (450 XP)

*Undead Fortitude*. If damage reduces Morg Drolak to 0 hit points, he must make a Constitution saving throw with a DC of 5 + the damage taken, unless the damage is radiant or from a critical hit. On a success, Morg Drolak drops to 1 hit point instead.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Multiattack*. Morg Drolak makes two greataxe attacks.

*Greataxe*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 9 (1d12+3) slashing damage.

# <span id="page-133-0"></span>APPENDIX 3: D ONJON DENIZENS

This appendix presents all the stat blocks you need to run the encounters in the Shadowed Keep's ruined donjon. The stat blocks appear in alphabetic order.

#### EINAR IRONWOLF

*Gaping, ragged wounds (including a slashed throat) pierce this spectral child's bloodstained nightshirt and body. Tears roll down its cheeks as it regards you with red eyes filled with a mixture of fear and loathing.* 

Valentin and Kaarina's only child, Einar was brutally slain when the keep fell. The trauma of his death and the separation from his parents anchored his soul to the Material Plane.

# **EINAR IRONWOLF**

*Medium undead, neutral* 

**Armour Class** 11 **Hit Points** 27 (6d8) **Speed** 0 ft., fly 40 ft.

| STR    | DEX     | CON     | INT     | WIS     | CHA     |
|--------|---------|---------|---------|---------|---------|
| 7 (-2) | 13 (+1) | 10 (+0) | 10 (+0) | 12 (+1) | 13 (+1) |

**Damage Resistances** acid, fire, lightning, thunder; bludgeoning, piercing and slashing from nonmagical weapons

**Damage Immunities** cold, necrotic, poison

**Condition Immunities** charmed, exhaustion, frightened, grappled, paralysed, petrified, poisoned, prone, restrained

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 11

**Languages** Common **Challenge** 3 (700 XP)

*Ethereal Sight.* Einar can see 60 ft. into the Ethereal Plane when he is on the Material Plane, and vice versa.

*Incorporeal Movement.* Einar can move through other creatures and objects as if they were difficult terrain. He takes 5 (1d10) force damage if he ends his turn inside an object.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Withering Touch*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +3 to hit, reach 5 ft., target. *Hit*: 11 (3d6+1) necrotic damage.

*Etherealness*. Einar enters the Ethereal Plane from the Material Plane or vice versa. He is visible on the Material Plane while he is in the Border Ethereal and vice versa yet he can't affect or be affected by anything on the other plane.

*Horrifying Visage.* Each non-undead creature within 60 ft. of Einar that can see him must make a DC 13 Wisdom saving throw or be frightened for 1 minute. If the save fails by 5 or more, the target also ages 1d4 x 10 years. A frightened target can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the frightened condition on itself with a successful save. If a target's saving throw is successful or the effect ends for it, the target is immune to Einar's Horrifying Visage for the next 24 hours. The ageing effect can be reversed with a *greater restoration* spell, but only within 24 hours of it occurring.

*Possession (Recharge 5-6).* One humanoid that Einar can see within 5 feet of him must make a DC 13 Charisma saving throw or be possessed by him; Einar then disappears, and the target is incapacitated and loses control of its body. Einar now controls the body but doesn't

deprive the target of awareness. Einar can't be targeted by any attack or spell, except ones that turn undead, and he retains his alignment, Intelligence, Wisdom, Charisma and immunity to being charmed

and frightened. He otherwise uses the possessed target's statistics, but doesn't gain access to the target's knowledge, class features or proficiencies. The possession lasts until the body drops to 0 hit points, Einar ends it as a bonus action, or he is turned or forced out by an effect like the *dispel evil* 

*and good* spell. When the possession ends, Einar reappears in an unoccupied space within 5 feet of the body. The target is immune to Einar's Possession for 24 hours after succeeding on the saving throw or after the possession ends.

#### FIRE ELEMENTAL LESSER GUARDIAN

*This small creature comprises nothing but leaping, writhing flame.* 

Fire elemental lesser guardians delight in setting fire to those intruding on the area they are bound to protect.

#### **FIRE ELEMENTAL LESSER GUARDIAN**

*Medium elemental, neutral* 

**Armour Class** 13 **Hit Points** 52 (7d8+21)

**Speed** 50 ft.

| STR     | DEX     | CON     | INT    | WIS     | CHA    |
|---------|---------|---------|--------|---------|--------|
| 10 (+0) | 17 (+3) | 16 (+3) | 6 (-2) | 10 (+0) | 7 (-2) |

**Damage Resistances** bludgeoning, piercing and slashing from nonmagical weapons

**Damage Immunities** fire, poison

**Condition Immunities** exhaustion, grappled, paralysed, petrified, poisoned, prone, restrained, unconscious

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 10

**Languages** Ignan **Challenge** 3 (700 XP)

*Fire Form*. The elemental can move through a space as narrow as 1 inch wide without squeezing. A creature that touches the elemental or hits it with a melee attack while within 5 ft. of it takes 4 (1d8) fire damage. In addition, the elemental can enter a hostile creature's space and stop there. The first time it enters a creature's space on a turn, that creature takes 4 (1d8) fire damage and catches fire; until someone takes an action to douse the fire, the creature takes 4 (1d8) fire damage at the start of each of its turns.

*Illumination*. The elemental sheds bright light in a 30-foot radius and dim light in an additional 30 ft.

*Water Susceptibility*. For every 5 ft. the elemental moves in water, or for every gallon of water splashed on it, it takes 1 cold damage.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Multiattack*. The elemental makes two attacks.

*Touch*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 10 (2d6+3) fire damage. If the target is a creature or flammable object, it ignites. Until a creature takes an action to douse the fire, itt takes 5 (1d10) fire damage at the start of each of its turns.

#### GIANT RAT

*This filthy oversized rat is covered in mangy grey fur, and its shining black eyes glitter menacingly.* 

The size of small dogs, these ever-hungry vermin can present a serious danger to injured or lone adventurers.

#### **GIANT R AT**

*Small beast, unaligned* 

**Armour Class** 12 **Hit Points** 7 (2d6) **Speed** 30 ft.

| STR    | DEX     | CON     | INT    | WIS     | CHA    |
|--------|---------|---------|--------|---------|--------|
| 7 (-2) | 15 (+2) | 11 (+0) | 2 (-4) | 10 (+0) | 4 (-3) |

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 10

**Languages** —

**Challenge** 1/8 (25 XP)

*Keen Smell*. The rat has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on smell.

*Pack Tactics*. The rat has advantage on attack rolls against a creature if at least one of the rat's allies is within 5 feet of the creature and the ally isn't incapacitated.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Bite*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 4 (1d4+2) piercing damage.

#### GIANT SPIDER

*This gigantic black spider is the size of a large dog.* 

These near-mindless ambush predators are aggressive hunters.

#### **GIANT SPIDER**

*Large beast, unaligned* 

**Armour Class** 14 (natural armour)

**Hit Points** 26 (4d10+4)

**Speed** 30 ft., climb 30 ft.

| STR     | DEX     | CON     | INT    | WIS     | CHA    |
|---------|---------|---------|--------|---------|--------|
| 14 (+2) | 16 (+3) | 12 (+1) | 2 (-4) | 11 (+0) | 4 (-3) |

**Skills** Stealth +7

**Senses** blindsight 10 ft., darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 10

**Languages** —

**Challenge** 1 (200 XP)

*Spider Climb*. The spider can climb difficult surfaces, including upside down on ceilings, without making an ability check.

*Web Sense*. While in contact with a web, the spider knows the exact location of any other creature in contact with the same web.

*Web Walker*. The spider ignores movement restrictions caused by webbing.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Bite*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one creature. *Hit*: 7 (1d8+3) piercing damage, and the target must make a DC 11 Constitution saving throw, taking 9 (2d8) poison damage on a failed save, or half damage on a successful save. If the poison damage reduces the target to 0 hit points, the target is stable but poisoned for 1 hour, even after regaining hit points, and is paralysed while poisoned in this way.

**Web (Recharge 5-6)**. *Ranged Weapon Attack*: +5 to hit, range 30/60 ft., one creature. *Hit*: The target is restrained by webbing. As an action, the restrained target can make a DC 12 Strength check, bursting the webbing on a success. The webbing can also be attacked and destroyed (AC 10; hp 5; vulnerability to fire damage; immunity to bludgeoning, poison and psychic damage).

# NECROPHIDIUS

*The sinuous skeleton of a large snake topped with a humanoid skull, complete with a snake's fangs, sways menacingly.* 

Also known as the Death Worm, necrophidius are created to be assassins or guards. Although they appear to be undead—having the skeleton of a giant snake and a fanged human skull—they are actually constructs.

#### **NECROPHIDIUS**

*Large construct, unaligned* 

**Armour Class** 14 (natural armour)

**Hit Points** 86 (12d10+20)

**Speed** 30 ft.

**Damage Vulnerabilities** bludgeoning

**Damage Immunities** poison

**Condition Immunities** charmed, exhaustion, frightened, paralysed, petrified, poisoned

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 10

**Languages** Common **Challenge** 4 (1,100 XP)

*Silent Slither*. The necrophidius has advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to move silently.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Bite*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +5 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit*: 10 (2d6+3) piercing damage. If the target is a creature other than an undead, it must make a DC 14 Constitution saving throw or be paralysed for 1 minute. The target can repeat the saving throw at

![](_page_135_Picture_18.jpeg)

the end of its turns, ending the effect on itself with a successful saving throw.

*Dance of Death*. A necrophidius can entrance its foes by swaying back and forth in a hypnotic, semi-magical way. All creatures within 30 ft. who can see the necrophidius making its dance of death must make a DC 14 Wisdom saving throw or be stunned for 1 minute. The target can repeat the saving throw at the end of its turns, ending the effect on itself with a successful saving throw.

# <span id="page-136-0"></span>APPENDIX 4: WATCHTOWER DENIZENS

This appendix presents all the stat blocks required to run the Watchtower of the Bandit Queen portion of this adventure. The stat blocks appear in alphabetic order.

#### BARELI

*Clad in filthy hide armour, this fat and slovenly black-haired halforc woman has tiny pig-like eyes.* 

**Background**: Bareli is a deserter from the garrison at Dulwich Keep. She is also a murderer who slew her sergeant when he threatened her with—in her mind—an unfair punishment for sleeping through her guard duty.

**Personality**: Bareli is a thoroughly self-centred woman wholly obsessed with her own aggrandisement. She dreams of a life of easy luxury and of having many servants to carry out her will. The only problem is she can't be bothered to earn that lifestyle.

**Mannerisms**: Bareli spits great gobs of phlegm—sometimes into the food she cooks. She has no sense of personal hygiene and smells of stale food and sweat.

#### **B ARELI**

*Medium female humanoid (half-orc), chaotic neutral* 

**Armour Class** 14 (hide armour)

**Hit Points** 33 (6d8+4)

**Speed** 30 ft.

| STR     | DEX     | CON     | INT     | WIS     | CHA     |
|---------|---------|---------|---------|---------|---------|
| 14 (+2) | 14 (+2) | 13 (+1) | 10 (+0) | 10 (+0) | 10 (+0) |

**Skills** Intimidation +2

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 10

**Languages** Common, Orc **Challenge** 1/2 (100 XP)

*Special Equipment*. Bareli has a *potion of healing*.

*Relentless Endurance*. When Bareli is reduced to 0 hit points, but not killed, she drops to 1 hit point instead.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Battleaxe*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 7 (1d10+2) slashing damage.

*Handaxe*. *Ranged Weapon Attack*: +4 to hit, range 20/60 ft., one target. *Hit*: 5 (1d6+2) slashing damage.

**Wanted Bandit**: Returning Bareli to Dulwich Keep to face justice or presenting incontrovertible proof of her death earns the party 25 gp.

#### CULLEN ASIKKA

*Greasy black hair frames the face of a human male dominated by high cheekbones and acne.* 

**Background**: Unloved by his family, Cullen left home while still a child. Falling into the clutches of a smuggler gang, he was abused and exploited. An argument over loot left many of his fellows dead; with no ties (and none of the treasure), he fled and soon after fell in with Firean.

**Personality**: Unpredictable, violent and prone to brooding, Cullen has few friends. He respects Firean, but does not like her and thus does not have much loyalty to his fellows. He loves Fang. He is an inveterate hoarder and has squirrelled away a small cache of silver and gold. He does not willingly abandon it.

**Mannerisms**: Cullen talks to Fang as a parent to a child.

# **C ULLEN ASIKKA**

*Medium humanoid (human), chaotic neutral* 

**Armour Class** 14 (studded leather)

**Hit Points** 44 (8d8+8)

**Speed** 30 ft.

| STR     | DEX     | CON     | INT     | WIS     | CHA     |
|---------|---------|---------|---------|---------|---------|
| 11 (+0) | 14 (+2) | 12 (+1) | 11 (+0) | 13 (+1) | 11 (+0) |

**Skills** Deception +4, Perception +5, Sleight of Hand +6, Stealth +6 **Senses** passive Perception 15

**Languages** Common **Challenge** 1 (200 XP)

*Special Equipment*. Cullen has a *potion of healing*.

*Keen Hearing and Sight*. Cullen has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks relying on hearing or sight.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Multiattack*. Cullen makes two melee or two ranged attacks.

*Shortsword*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 5 (1d6+2) piercing damage.

**Shortbow**. *Ranged Weapon Attack*: +4 to hit, range 80/320 ft., one target. *Hit*: 5 (1d6+2) piercing damage.

# FANG

#### FIREAN MAIETHIL

*Muscular and attractive, this half-elf woman wears form-fitting leather armour and wields a morningstar. Her dark brown eyes regard you with a mixture of malevolence and boredom.* 

**Background**: A product of war, suffering and rape, Firean has wandered for many years, unable to find a place in the world.

**Personality**: Dedicated to Braal (NE lesser god of hate, malice and revenge), Firean dreams of establishing her own dominion from which she can war on her neighbours. The Shadowed Keep represents her chance to realise that dream. For her, might is right, and the weak are worthy of nothing but scorn.

**Mannerisms**: Firean cannot decide whether she wants her followers to love or fear her; consequently, she explains her decisions in great depth before threatening violence against any not sharing her perspective (or obeying her commands).

#### **FIREAN MAIETHIL**

*Medium humanoid (half-elf), chaotic evil* 

**Armour Class** 13 (leather armour)

**Hit Points** 33 (6d8+6)

**Speed** 30 ft.

| STR     | DEX     | CON     | INT     | WIS     | CHA     |
|---------|---------|---------|---------|---------|---------|
| 14 (+2) | 15 (+2) | 12 (+1) | 11 (+0) | 16 (+3) | 16 (+3) |

**Skills** Deception +5, Persuasion +5, Perception +5, Religion +2, Stealth +4

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 15

**Languages** Common, Elvish **Challenge** 2 (450 XP)

*Dark Devotion*. Firean has advantage on saving throws against being charmed or frightened.

**Fey Ancestry**. Firean has advantage on saving throws against being charmed, and magic can't put her to sleep.

*Spellcasting*. Firean is a 4th-level spellcaster. Her spellcasting ability is Wisdom (spell save DC 13, +5 to hit with spell attacks). She has the following cleric spells prepared:

Cantrips (at will): *light*, *sacred flame*, *thaumaturgy* 1st level (4 slots): *command*, *cure wounds*, *shield of faith* 2nd level (3 slots): *blindness*/*deafness*, *hold person*

#### **ACTIONS**

*Multiattack*. Firean makes two melee attacks.

*Morningstar*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 4 (1d8+2) piercing damage.

*Dagger*. *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack*: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 20 ft./60 ft., one target. *Hit*: 4 (1d4+2) piercing damage.

**Wanted Bandit**: Returning Firean to Dulwich Keep to face justice or presenting incontrovertible proof of her death earns the party 150 gp.

![](_page_138_Picture_38.jpeg)

# REITHIC YURGIRN

*Wide and heavily muscled, this dwarf has a thick black beard, glittering black eyes and thick, bushy eyebrows.* 

**Background**: A skilled warrior, Reithic is trying to carve out a career as a purveyor of fine dwarven weapons and armour. The bandits captured him during his first attempt at a trader's life.

**Personality**: Gruff and quick to anger, Reithic craves vengeance. He loudly asserts his desire to kill Yar.

**Mannerisms**: Reithic roars challenges in battle.

# **REITHIC Y URGIRN**

*Medium humanoid (dwarf), lawful neutral* 

**Armour Class** 13 (studded leather)

**Skills** Athletics +5, Perception +2

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 12

**Languages** Common, Dwarven

*Dwarven Resilience*. Reithic has advantage on saving throws against poison damage.

*Stonecunning*. Reithic adds +4 to Intelligence (History) checks related to the origin of stonework.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Multiattack*. Reithic makes two melee attacks.

*Morningstar*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 7 (1d8+3) piercing damage.

*Light crossbow*. *Ranged Weapon Attack*: +3 to hit, range 80/320 ft., one target. *Hit*: 5 (1d8+1) piercing damage.

The statistics above assume Reithic has looted equipment from slain brigands. If he has not done so, modify his statistics thusly:

- **Armour Class** 11
- *Unarmed Strike*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 4 bludgeoning damage.

**Reward**: Reithic happily (and enthusiastically) aids the characters in defeating the bandits but has no interest in exploring the rest of the ruin. He is grateful for his rescue, however, and 2d4 weeks after the party frees him, he seeks them out to gift them a *potion of greater healing*.

# YA R

*Clad in ragged, bloodstained clothes, this small, scrawny humanoid has a wide, ungainly head. Covered in sores and partially healed cuts and scrapes, it is a sorry sight.* 

**Background**: Captured several weeks ago, Yar has endured beatings and starvation during his incarceration.

**Personality**: Miserable and terrified, Yar is no longer a rapacious warrior of the Blood Moon. He has no desire to rejoin the tribe, preferring to flee the ruins if given the chance. His favourite battle tactic (preferably against helpless or oblivious foes) is "stabby stabby".

**Mannerisms**: Yar has developed a hacking cough during his incarceration and noticeably flinches when threatened.

#### **Y A R**

*Small humanoid (goblin), neutral evil* 

**Armour Class** 12 **Hit Points** 7 (2d6) **Speed** 30 ft.

| STR    | DEX     | CON     | INT     | WIS    | CHA    |
|--------|---------|---------|---------|--------|--------|
| 8 (-1) | 14 (+2) | 10 (+0) | 10 (+0) | 8 (-1) | 8 (-1) |

**Skills** Stealth +6

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 9

**Languages** Common, Goblin **Challenge** 1/8 (25 XP)

*Nimble Escape*. Yar can take the Disengage or Hide action as a bonus action on each of his turns.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Unarmed Strike*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +2 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 1 bludgeoning damage.

**Hooks & Reward**: Yar just wants to live. In return for his freedom, he can describe the general layout of the donjon's cellars. Sadly, his artistic skills are terrible; any map he attempts is illegible. Particularly interesting facts he can divulge include:

- The tribe's indestructible ogre-chief, Ruknar, and his sadistic son, Razogen, dwell to the south.
- The tribe has two fearsome orc mercenaries.
- The tribe's shaman, Sar, wields powerful magic.
- There are caves below the tribe's home. He doesn't know what lurks within.

If the characters have treated him well, he warns them of the exploding door trap in location D4.

# <span id="page-140-0"></span>APPENDIX 5: BLOOD MOON DENIZENS

This appendix presents all the stat blocks you need to run encounters in the Shadowed Keep's cellars. The stat blocks appear in alphabetic order.

#### BLOOD MOON BRUISERS

*This small humanoid has a flat face, a squashed nose and a wide mouth full of fangs. Clad in studded leather armour, it carries a heavy wooden shield and longsword.* 

Stronger and more aggressive than the average goblin, Blood Moon bruisers serve as the tribe's shock troops and enforcers.

#### **BLOOD MOON BRUISER**

*Small humanoid (goblin), neutral evil* 

**Armour Class** 13 (leather armour)

**Hit Points** 7 (2d6) **Speed** 30 ft.

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 9

**Languages** Common, Goblin

**Challenge** 1/4 (50 XP)

*Nimble Escape*. The goblin can take the Disengage or Hide action as a bonus action on each of its turns.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Warhammer. Melee Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: 6 (1d8+2) bludgeoning damage or 7 (1d10+2) bludgeoning damage if wielded two-handed.

#### *B*LOOD MOON CONCUBINES

*This large female goblin wears studded leather and radiates an aura of aggression and violence. She wields two curved sickles.* 

Ruknar's concubines (Nig, Sbux and Zus) are vicious creatures obsessed with bearing Buknar's "blessed" seed. They see each other as competition and only cooperate when Ruknar commands it. They hiss and curse at their foes and exult when an enemy succumbs to their attacks. They don't make any particular effort to help each other in battle. Particularly large and nasty goblins, a concubine is in many ways the equal of a hobgoblin.

#### RAZOGEN

*This lumbering humanoid has small, beady eyes and a wide mouth filled with ill-fitting teeth. It wears a breastplate and wields a sword.* 

Ruknar's son is desperate to both please his father and supplant him…when the time is right.

**Mannerisms**: Razogen bellows and shouts in battle.

**Distinguishing Features**: Vestigial black horns grow from Razogen's forehead.

**Personality**: Violent, unpredictable and sadist, Razogen is perfectly suited to life in a goblin tribe.

**Background**: Razogen is the product of his father's mating with a goblin concubine. The concubine died in childbirth—so large a baby was Razogen. The first sound he heard was his mother's anguished screams.

#### **R AZOGEN**

*Large giant (ogre), chaotic evil* 

**Armour Class** 13 (breastplate) **Hit Points** 59 (7d10+21)

**Speed** 40 ft.

| STR     | DEX    | CON     | INT    | WIS    | CHA    |  |
|---------|--------|---------|--------|--------|--------|--|
| 19 (+4) | 8 (-1) | 16 (+3) | 5 (-3) | 7 (-2) | 7 (-2) |  |

**Damage Resistances** cold, fire, lightning, poison

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 8

**Languages** Giant, Goblin **Challenge** 3 (700 XP)

#### **ACTIONS**

*Greatsword*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 14 (3d6+4) slashing damage.

*Javelin*. *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack*: +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., range 30/120 ft., one target. *Hit*: 11 (2d6+4) piercing damage.

#### RUKNAR

*This lumbering giant has small, beady eyes and a wide mouth filled with ill-fitting teeth. He wears mismatched pieces of chain armour and clutches an immense greatsword.* 

A foul, odious bully who delights in the pain, suffering, dismemberment and death of his foes, Ruknar is a terrible enemy.

**Mannerisms**: Ruknar spits and drools when excited. **Distinguishing Features**: Ruknar is immensely fat.

**Personality**: Ruknar enjoys his concubines' competition—even fostering it. He also enjoys dismembering and cooking his living enemies as a warning to those who plot against him.

**Background**: The taint of the Abyss lurks in Ruknar's past. As the only survivor of his original tribe, he easily wrested command of the Blood Moon from its previous chieftain two decades ago. Since then, he has lived the good life—plentiful women, loot and battle. He is content.

#### **R UKNAR**

*Large giant (ogre), chaotic evil* 

**Armour Class** 15 (chain mail) **Hit Points** 76 (8d10+24)

**Speed** 40 ft.

| STR     | DEX    | CON     | INT    | WIS     | CHA    |
|---------|--------|---------|--------|---------|--------|
| 19 (+4) | 8 (-1) | 16 (+3) | 8 (-1) | 13 (+1) | 7 (-2) |

**Damage Resistances** cold, fire, lightning, poison **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 11

**Languages** Giant, Goblin **Challenge** 4 (1,100 XP)

*Innate Spellcasting*. Ruknar's spellcasting ability is Wisdom (spell save 11). He can innately cast the following spells, requiring no material components:

1/day each: *burning hands*, *phantasmal force* 2/day each: *shield*, *invisibility* (self only)

#### **ACTIONS**

*Multiattack*. Ruknar makes two melee attacks.

*Greatsword*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 14 (3d6+4) slashing damage.

*Javelin*. *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack*: +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., range 30/120 ft., one target. *Hit*: 11 (2d6+4) piercing damage.

#### SA R, BLOOD MOON SHAMAN

*This bald and skinny humanoid wears dirty robes, and its head seems too large for its body.* 

Sar lusts to overthrow Ruknar and rule in his place. Although not a coward, Sar is not stupid and knows he is no match for the ogre. The characters' arrival presents him with a perfect opportunity to achieve his goal. Thus, he is keen to speak with the intruders.

**Distinguishing Features**: Impressively ugly, Sar stinks of blood, sweat and spell components.

**Mannerisms**: Sar has a hacking cough.

**Personality**: Obsessed with his own importance and consumed with a lust for power, Sar is self-obsessed to the point of mania. Totally immoral, he agrees to anything—no matter how shocking—to get his own way. He enjoys torture and has enjoyed time with the tribe's prisoners. He does not regret his actions.

**Background**: The favoured servant of the tribe's previous shaman, Sar gruesomely murdered his teacher several years ago.

# **S A R, BLOOD MOON SHAMAN**

*Small humanoid (goblin), neutral evil* 

**Armour Class** 13 (leather armour)

**Hit Points** 27 (6d6+6)

**Speed** 30 ft.

| STR    | DEX     | CON     | INT     | WIS     | CHA    |
|--------|---------|---------|---------|---------|--------|
| 8 (-1) | 14 (+2) | 12 (+1) | 10 (+0) | 14 (+2) | 8 (-1) |

**Skills** Stealth +6

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 11

**Languages** Common, Goblin **Challenge** 1/2 (100 XP)

*Nimble Escape*. Sar can take the Disengage or Hide action as a bonus action on each of his turns.

*Spellcasting*. Sar is a 4th-level spellcaster. His spellcasting ability is Wisdom (spell save 12 + 4 to hit with spell attacks). He has the following cleric spells prepared:

Cantrips (at will): *resistance, sacred flame, spare the dying, thaumaturgy*

1st level (4 slots): *cure wounds, sanctuary, shield of faith* 2nd level (3 slots): *hold person, silence, spiritual weapon*

#### **ACTIONS**

*Scimitar*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 5 (1d6+2) slashing damage.

#### **REACTIONS**

*Redirect Attack*. When a foe Sar can see targets him with an attack, Sar can choose another goblin within 5 feet of him. The two swap places and the other goblin becomes the attack's target.

# BLOOD MOON ALLIES

The Blood Moon tribe are not without allies.

GRINNING SKULL BUGBEAR

*This muscular, dark-furred creature has milk-white eyes. It wields a morningstar and wears leather armour.* 

Grinning Skull bugbears delight in decapitating their enemies and displaying the skulls as trophies and decorations.

# **GRINNING S KULL B UGBEAR**

*Medium humanoid (bugbear), chaotic evil* 

**Armour Class** 16 (hide armour, shield)

**Hit Points** 27 (5d8+5)

**Speed** 30 ft.

|---------|---------|---------|--------|---------|--------|
| 15 (+2) | 14 (+2) | 13 (+1) | 8 (-1) | 11 (+0) | 9 (-1) |

**Skills** Stealth +6, Survival +2

**Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 10

**Languages** Common, Goblin

**Challenge** 1 (200 XP)

*Brute*. A melee weapon deals one extra die of its damage when the bugbear hits with it (this is included in the attacks below).

*Surprise Attack*. If the bugbear surprises a creature and hits it with an attack during the first round of combat, the target takes an extra 7 (2d6) damage from the attack.

#### **ACTIONS**

*Morningstar*. *Melee Weapon Attack*: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 11 (2d8+2) piercing damage.

*Javelin*. *Ranged Weapon Attack*: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 30/120 ft., one target. *Hit*: 9 (2d6+2) piercing damage in melee or 5 (1d6+2) piercing damage at range.

OR C MERCENARY

*This muscular and tall grey-skinned warrior has small piggy eyes and short fangs protruding from its jaw. It wears poor-quality chainmail and clutches a huge axe.* 

An orc mercenary serves whoever pays it to fight and kill.
